ADPr - actin trimer is a short - F - actin oligomer that binds selectively to F - actin binding proteins by Navneet Sidhu A Thesis presented to The University of Guelph In partial fulfilment of requirements for the degree of Doctor of Philosophy in Molecular and Cellular Biology Guelph , Ontario , Canada © Navneet Sidhu , January , 2020 ABSTRACT ADPR - ACTIN TRIMER IS A SHORT - F - ACTIN OLIGOMER THAT BINDS SELECTIVELY TO F - ACTIN BINDING PROTEINS Navneet Sidhu University of Guelph , 2020 Advisor : Dr . John F . Dawson Actin is one of the most abundant and conserved proteins involved in a myriad of biological functions critical for maintaining eukaryotic life . The functions of actin rely on dynamic reorganization of actin filaments , which is modulated by several Actin Binding Proteins ( ABPs ) . Despite the significance of these interactions in regulating actin function , the field lacked atomic details of interactions of F - actin with ABPs until the first decade of the 2000s . With advances in cryo - Electron Microscopy ( cryo - EM ) since 2015 , structural models of F - actin alone and bound to ABPs have been proposed . The resolution of earlier EM structures lacked important atomic details ; consequently , traditional X - ray crystallography remains the mainstay technique to obtain high resolution structures . However , the ability of actin to self - assemble into filaments of varying lengths limits the application of X - ray crystallography . To overcome this challenge posed by actin , a short , non - polymerizable F - actin oligomer called ADPr - trimer was generated . The aim of my project was to generate heterocomplexes of ADPr - trimer with F - ABPs for structural work . A candidate - based approach was applied to determine interactions of ADPr - trimer with purified ABPs ( myosin subfragment - 1 , cofilin and gelsolin ) . Cofilin bound to ADPr - trimer and overcome polymerization inhibition properties of ADPr - trimer and forming filaments , and myosin did not bind ADPr - trimer . Gelsolin bound to ADPr - trimer ; however , the complex did not yield crystals . Therefore , a negative staining EM approach was used to determine the suitability of the gelsolin : trimer complex for cryo - EM structure determination . The EM - micrographs revealed the presence of heterogeneous species in the gelsolin : trimer complex sample . EM work led to identifying a workflow for future EM work in the lab . In addition , an unbiased approach was applied to identify binding proteins involving pull - down of ABPs from cell lysates on ADPr - trimer affinity columns coupled with mass spectrometry ( MS ) . An identified potential interactor , myosin light chain ( MLC6B ) , was produced for biochemical validation of the interaction . Apo - MLC6B and MLC6B associated with myosin bound to ADPr - trimer in pull - down assays , supporting the MS results . Understanding the interactions of actin with ABPs through the application of proteomics and cryo - EM structural determination will advance our knowledge of the critical role of actin and its binding proteins in maintaining eukaryotic life . iv ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS Firstly , I would like to extend my sincere appreciation to my advisor Dr . actin structures . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 206 Supplemental Table 3 Recent structures of F - actin bound to F - ABPs . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 207 1 1 INTRODUCTION 1 . 1 Overview Actin is one of the most abundant proteins that participates in a multitude of eukaryotic cellular processes . The actin protein is encoded by genes that have been conserved over the course of evolution and are present in all eukaryotic cells . Actin’s ubiquitous nature , extreme conservation , and involvement in diverse biological processes highlights its critical roles in maintaining eukaryotic lifeforms . 1 The key biological processes that actin mediates include sensing environmental forces , endocytosis , cell division , intracellular transport and force generation . 2 These functions of actin rely on the assembly of monomeric actin into filaments that can organize into a variety of architectures . Actin filaments can be stable , as in muscle , or dynamically reorganizing to drive cellular processes . This dynamic reorganization of actin into varied filament architectures is modulated by a large array of Actin Binding Proteins ( ABPs ) . 3 These proteins can bind to filament sides , ends and / or monomers and regulate each step of actin assembly and disassembly . Although the role of various ABPs in actin filament reorganization is established , understanding how many of these ABPs interact with actin filaments at the atomic level remains unsolved . Understanding these interactions at a molecular level through proteomics and structural determination will advance our knowledge of the mechanisms of actin filament organization and force generation — processes critical for maintaining eukaryotic life . The insights gained can also be applied to disease management and drug discovery . With recent advances in the field of cryo - Electron Microscopy ( cryo - EM ) , structural models of F - actin alone and bound to ABPs have been proposed . 4 – 9 However , the resolution from 2 EM studies lack atomic details , such as those at the peripheral radius exposed to the solvent . 10 Consequently , traditional structural protein X - ray crystallography remains the most preferred technique to obtain high resolution structures . However , the ability of actin to self - assemble into filaments of varying lengths limits the use of X - ray crystallography . To overcome the challenge posed by the inherent property of actin to self - assemble , a short , non - polymerizable F - actin oligomer known as ADPr - trimer was developed . 11 ADPr - trimer was shown to have F - actin like properties . It bound to ABPs , such as DNase I and gelsolin . Hence , I hypothesize that ADPr - trimer can be used as a scaffold for binding F - ABPs to study atomic interactions . My research goal is to use ADPr - trimer as a platform to understand how ABPs interact with F - actin at the atomic level . To achieve my goal , the specific research objectives are : ( 1 ) Use ADPr - trimer as a scaffold to identify F - ABPs and ( 2 ) purify heterocomplexes of ADPr - trimer with F - ABPs for biochemical and structural characterization . To fulfill these research objectives , two approaches were followed : ( 1 ) a candidate approach to determine interactions of ADPr - trimer with purified F - ABPs ( myosin subfragment - 1 ( S1 ) , cofilin , and gelsolin ) and ( 2 ) an unbiased approach using mass spectrometry ( MS ) to identify F - ABPs from cell lysates bound to ADPr - trimer . Identified F - ABPs were then produced in the laboratory and their interactions characterized for future structural work . This thesis begins by providing an overview of the protein actin , ABPs and structural advances made in the field of F - actinomics . The second chapter focuses on the candidate approach . That chapter includes the findings from the physical and biochemical assays used to confirm interaction of F - ABPs ( myosin S1 , gelsolin and cofilin ) with ADPr - trimer . The work around myosin S1 has been published . The preliminary structure of gelsolin - bound ADPr - trimer obtained from negative stained EM images is presented in this chapter as well . The final research chapter 3 covers an unbiased approach to identify and validate identified binding partners using mass spectrometry . This thesis concludes with a summary of the key findings and sets the stage for future studies . 1 . 2 Biology of Actin 1 . 2 . 1 Sequence Conservation and Isoforms Interestingly , actin is one of the most abundant eukaryotic proteins coded by one of ~ 400 ancestral genes . 12 It has been conserved over billions of years that have separated Saccharomyces , Arabidopsis and Homo sapeins . 13 Homologs of actin exist in other branches of life : crenactin in archaea , 14 and MreB and ParM in bacteria . 15 , 16 It has been postulated that eukaryotic actin evolved from an archaeal cytoskeleton when a relative of Lokiarchaeota , an archaeal cell with an actin gene , took on a bacterial symbiont giving rise to eukaryotic life . 17 Thus , the actin protein was present and may have actively participated in producing the first eukaryotic cell . In eukaryotes , actin is a universal force generator integrated into varied physiological processes which rely on rapid assembly and disassembly of the cellular actin pool . Consequently , during evolution eukaryotic cells developed several ABPs that interact with actin to regulate where and when actin will assemble and dissemble . Various ideas have been proposed to explain the remarkable conservation of the actin protein . It has been proposed that interaction of several ABPs with actin in the cell placed a strong selective constraint on its evolution . 18 As a result , actin has maintained a remarkable sequence conservation from yeast to humans with an overall 91 . 2 % sequence identity . An alternative theory states that actin requires a set of specific chaperonin proteins to fold and such regulated folding placed constrains on sequence divergence . 19 According to another school of thought , the allosteric 4 interactions that exist in distant sites of F - actin and the multiple interactions within the filament places selective pressure on amino acids in the actin molecule . 20 , 21 Moreover , abundantly expressed proteins like actin tend to evolve slowly to prevent misfolding . 22 Although actin is thought of as a single protein , it exists as six different isoforms in mammals encoded by separate genes . The isoforms of actin include : α - skeletal , α - cardiac , α - smooth and γ - smooth that are primarily found in skeletal , cardiac and smooth muscle , respectively , and β - and γ - cytoplasmic isoforms that are expressed ubiquitously . All the isoforms of actin are remarkably similar and share no less than 93 % sequence identity with each other . 23 Knock out studies in mice show that each of the actin isoforms has specialized functions . Interestingly , it has been shown that knock out of one specific isoform results in compensatory upregulation of a subset of the remaining actin isoforms . 24 The specialized functions of nearly identical isoforms of actin have been attributed to two theories . First , selective binding of ABPs to a specific isoform dictates a required function . Second , the localization of the actin isoforms result in different interactions with subsets of ABPs required for the function of each actin isoform . 23 Hence , the interaction of actin with over 100 different binding partners not only dictates the function of actin isoforms , but also imposes high selective evolutionary pressure on the actin sequence to remain unchanged . 13 1 . 2 . 2 Actin and Diseases In addition to being a component of the cytoskeleton and the cellular movement mechanism , actin also contributes to embryonic development , the functioning of cells such as lymphocytes , and maintaining complex structures like neural synapses and stereocilia . Therefore , misregulation of an actin gene can manifest as various diseased states including compromised immunity , neurodegeneration and metastatic cancer . 25 5 Mutations in the α - skeletal actin gene ACTA1 are associated with congenital myopathies including nemaline myopathy , actin myopathy , intranuclear rod myopathy and congenital fiber type myopathy . 26 – 28 These mutations can be either dominant or recessive , but most patients carry de novo dominant mutations . 26 Mutations in ACTC , a gene encoding for α - cardiac actin , lead to the development of hypertrophic cardiomyopathy and dilated cardiomyopathy . 29 , 30 Mutations in β - and γ - actin are rarely associated with diseases . These isoforms of actin are ubiquitously expressed and essential for life processes including cellular replication and migration that are critical for embryogenesis . While any mutation disrupting developmental functions of actin results in a non - viable offspring , some mutations in γ - actin lead to marginal effects on actin dynamics causing hearing loss , compromised immunity , deafness and dystonia , and developmental malformations . 31 – 33 Besides the genetic disorders described above , any unusual activation or loss of function of actin can result in pathological manifestations . One example is cellular metastasis in cancer where non - motile epithelial cells metamorphose into motile invasive mesenchymal cells due to alterations in actin cytoskeleton . 34 Other reported instances include the presence of rod shaped aggregates known as Hirano bodies , comprised of actin filaments and associated proteins in neurodegenerative diseases such as Alzheimer’s and CJD ( Creutzfeldt - Jakob disease ) . 35 Additionally , actin has been shown to aid in the virulence of several pathogenic bacteria such as , Listeria , Rickettsia and Shigella . 36 Thus , understanding the complex role of actin and its regulatory proteins can help describe the cause of these diseases and lead to development of targeted therapies . 6 1 . 2 . 3 Role of Actin in Biological Processes 1 . 2 . 3a Cytoskeleton Actin forms a part of the cytoskeleton . The cytoskeleton includes polymers of proteins including actin filaments , intermediate filaments and microtubules in varied proportions . The collective interaction between components of the cytoskeleton allows cells to resist sudden deformation . 37 The main role of actin filaments in the cytoskeleton is to provide structural support and shape to the cells , and to allow transport of proteins and vesicles within the cell . 38 , 39 Actin filaments form three types of structures within the cell : microfilament networks , bundles and periodic actin rings . Microfilament networks form at the cell cortex just under the plasma membrane and are connected to receptors relaying signals to and from the extracellular environment . Actin bundles in association with the contractile protein non - muscle myosin , allow intracellular transport of substances . Periodic actin rings are specifically found in axons where they form cytoskeleton structures along with spectrin that support the axonal membrane . 40 1 . 2 . 3b Motility In muscle cells , myofibrils comprised of thin filaments of actin and thick filaments of the motor protein myosin use energy derived from ATP to create force and motion . 41 Our current knowledge of the mechanism of force generation in muscle is described in Section 1 . 3 . 1b . Besides muscle movement , actin supports motility of cells . Although the contractile machinery composed of actin and myosin is more ordered and stable in muscle cells , the mechanism of mutual sliding of actin and myosin filaments is applicable to non - muscle cells as well . 42 The generation of cellular movement occurs by continuous cycles of protrusion and attachment of the cell at the leading edge , and detachment and retraction at the rear end . Protrusive 7 forces that drive the extension at the leading edge are produced by coordinated assembly of actin filaments . 43 The contractile forces that retract the trailing end of the motile cells are produced by the myosin motor in actin filaments . 44 , 45 Cell motility plays an important role during embryonic development to form tissues and organs and allows immune cells to reach and destroy pathogens and initiate immune responses . In fact , some non - motile cells undergo morphological changes to acquire motile behavior to rebuild tissues upon injury . 34 However , cell motility also leads to certain diseased states , such as the migration of cancer cells initiating invasion and metastasis of tumors and infiltration of immune cells to certain tissue results in inflammatory diseases . Last but not least , microbial pathogens manipulate host actin machinery to facilitate their uptake and spread cell to cell . All these motility processes are powered by the force generated by the actin cytoskeleton . 3 1 . 2 . 3c Cell Adhesion Actin is a component of several cell - cell junctions , such as adherens junctions in epithelial cells . 46 These junctions maintain tissue integrity and are formed primarily by members of the cadherin family of adhesion receptors that are stabilized by the actin cytoskeleton . 47 1 . 2 . 3d Miscellaneous Actin is involved in endocytosis in eukaryotes and budding and fission in yeast . 48 , 49 Endocytosis occurs with the assembly of actin and some associated proteins to interact with the membrane to induce a curvature . As the endocytic membrane moves into the cytoplasm , actin assembly disappears . During the process of cytokinesis in eukaryotes and yeast , a contractile ring is formed by actin and myosin filaments that generate force to pull the membrane into the cleavage furrow , thereby resolving the two daughter cells . 50 8 1 . 2 . 4 Structure Actin in nature can either exist in monomeric form called G - actin or can self - associate to give rise to filamentous - or F - actin . 1 . 2 . 4a G - actin The actin molecule is a polypeptide of 375 amino acid residues folded into a flat molecule that fits into a rectangular prism measuring 55 Å X 55 Å X 35 Å ( Figure 1 . 1 ) . It is composed of two major domains : a small outer domain and a large inner domain . Each major domain consists of two subdomains : subdomain 1 ( residues 1 - 32 , 70 - 144 and 338 - 372 ) and subdomain 2 ( residues 33 - 69 ) , which form the small domain , and subdomain 3 ( residues 145 - 180 , and 270 - 337 ) and subdomain 4 ( residues 181 - 269 ) , which form the large domain . 51 The two main domains are linked by a hinge between subdomain 1 and subdomain 3 . 52 Below the hinge lies the hydrophobic cleft which forms the binding site for certain types of macrolide toxins and many ABPs , and also mediates longitudinal contacts among actin subunits within a filament . 53 A hydrophobic loop / plug ( 265 - 271 ) extends from subdomain 4 of an actin subunit and fits between two actin subunits of the opposite strand where it forms salt bridges , hydrophobic and hydrophilic interactions stabilizing the interstrand contacts between two strands of F - actin . 54 A nucleotide binding cleft is present between subdomain 2 and subdomain 4 . This cleft harbors a nucleotide ( ATP or ADP ) associated with a divalent cation ( Mg 2 + under physiological conditions ) . 52 Subdomain 2 is the smallest and most flexible region of actin . It contains a DNase I binding loop ( D - loop ) ( residues 40 - 51 ) which has been observed in alpha - helix , beta - turn , loop 9 Figure 1 . 1 Globular actin . Ribbon diagram of Globular actin with nucleotide ATP shown as a sticks and Ca + 2 ion as a white sphere bound in the nucleotide binding cleft . The subdomains shown in different colors are labelled as 1 , 2 , 3 and 4 . Image file generated with PyMol using PDB : 1ATN . 10 conformations or completely disordered conformations . 55 The N - and C - termini of actin lie in subdomain 1 and much like the D - loop are flexible and often disordered in X - ray structures . 55 , 56 DNase I Binding Loop ( D - loop ) The first crystal structure of actin was determined in complex with DNase I bound to the D - loop of actin . 51 DNase I is an endonuclease that binds actin and inhibits polymerization . Conversely , the binding of actin to DNase I inhibits its endonuclease activity . 57 , 58 Although the complex is found in vivo , 59 the biological significance of this interaction remains unclear . However , high specificity and affinity of the interaction suggests a biological role for the interaction . 2 The interaction between DNase I and the D - loop of actin is through hydrogen bonds , electrostatic and hydrophobic interactions . The D - loop is involved in the formation of extensive contacts between actin subunits along the length of F - actin . 60 N - and C - termini The N - and C - termini of actin present in subdomain 1 possess a high degree of conformational flexibility . The C - terminus of actin participates in intersubunit interactions within the filament along with the D - loop and a hydrophobic loop . 61 , 62 Structural studies indicate interactions of the C - terminus with subdomain 3 of an adjacent lateral ( across - strand ) actin subunit within a filament and with subdomain 2 of an adjacent longitudinal ( along - strand ) actin subunit . 63 The C - terminus is also part of actomyosin binding during the strong binding state of myosin and it interacts with tropomyosin , a muscle contraction regulating protein . 64 – 66 Cys - 374 , the penultimate amino acid of actin , has been exploited to crosslink actin , inhibit actin polymerization , or monitor actin polymerization and interaction with ABPs such as myosin . This amino acid is the only surface - accessible cysteine on actin . 60 , 67 – 70 Labeling Cys - 374 with 11 pyrene does not impact the properties of actin and is used as a tool to monitor actin polymerization . A significant increase in pyrene fluorescence occurs as a result of polymerization of pyrene actin . 67 In addition , Cys - 374 has been a site for crosslinking actin monomers within the filament . Crosslinkers such as ANP ( N - ( 4 - azido - 2 - nitrophenyl ) putrescine ) , pPBM ( N , N’ - p - phenylene - bismaleimide ) and oPBM ( N , N’ - o - phenylene bismaleimide ) have been used to study the implications of restricting flexibility of actin filaments on actomyosin interactions and generate actin oligomers of defined length for crystal generation . 71 – 74 The N - terminus is the least conserved region of the actin molecule . Being a part of subdomain 1 and lying on the actin filament exterior , the N - terminal region forms part of the binding site for several ABPs . 75 , 76 Evidence suggests that the N - terminus plays a role in electrostatic interactions during the formation of the actomyosin complex . 77 , 78 The N - terminus possesses two to four acidic amino acids and the N - terminal amino acid is acetylated . The mechanism of generating a mature N - terminus differs for different isoforms of actin . In class I actins , including β - and γ - cytoplasmic actins , the acetylated methionine is removed proteolytically , exposing the N - terminal amino acid which is then acetylated to generate mature actin . 79 In striated and smooth muscle actins , the acetyl methionine is first removed from the Met - Cys - acidic N - terminus region . The terminal Cys is then N - acetylated , which is also removed . Finally , the first acidic amino acid in the sequence is acetylated to form the mature N - terminus . This specific mechanism of generation of the N - terminus suggests that the N - terminus processing of actin may have a significance in regulation of actin function . 80 The significance of the N - terminus in actin function has been studied . Elimination of the N - acetyl group from actin decreases the negative charge at this terminus and impacts actin - 12 activated myosin ATPase activity . 76 Similarly , a decrease in the negative charge on the N - terminus causes spontaneous bundling of actin facilitating formation of lamellipodia and filopodia ; a phenomenon observed in the malignant cancer cells . 81 The N - terminus is therefore an interesting region where its unique processing has been maintained across evolution . 1 . 2 . 4b F - actin Actin monomers self - associate in a head - to - tail manner to form a single left - handed helix with a subunit rotation of 166˚ . Two such helical strands twist around each other to give rise to filamentous F - actin . F - actin has approximately 13 molecule repeat every six turns within an axial distance of 35 . 9 nm . 82 Actin filaments are structurally polar with a fast - growing barbed end ( + / plus - end ) and a slow - growing pointed end ( - / minus - end ) . 83 In vivo , ABPs regulate the assembly , elongation , branching , severing and disassembly of actin filaments . In vitro , actin polymerization can be initiated by increasing ionic strength . The growth of the filament is dictated by the concentration of actin monomers . The property of actin to form filaments has been exploited to study several properties of this polymer . Polymerization of actin takes place in three sequential stages : nucleation , elongation and steady - state treadmilling . In the nucleation phase , actin monomers associate to form short oligomers to act as a nucleus . During the elongation phase , the actin nucleus grows into a filament by addition of monomers at both its ends . As the monomers add to the filament ends , the concentration of monomers decreases until that concentration is in equilibrium with the filament leading to a steady - state . For a specific concentration range , the subunits added to the plus - end equals those removed from the minus - end , such that the length of the filament remains constant . This process is known as treadmilling or filament turnover . Treadmilling is regulated by various ABPs . 84 The concentration of actin monomers in solution at steady state is known as the critical 13 concentration ( Cc ) . The Cc can also be described as the concentration of the actin subunits above which polymerization takes place and below which depolymerization takes place . 52 Overall , each step of actin polymerizatoin in vivo is regulated by ABPs ensuring that F - actin is formed at the right place and at the right time in the cell . 85 The rate of actin polymerization and stability of the filament depends on the nucleotide bound to the nucleotide binding cleft . As G - actin with ATP bound in the nucleotide binding cleft is incorporated into the filament , ATP is hydrolyzed to ADP and Pi . ADP F - actin is less stable and such a filament can be readily disassembled . This process is key to the reorganization of actin filaments . 82 Ironically , the property of actin to self - assemble that enables actin to perform varied biological processes , also renders the protein unsuitable for atomic resolution crystallographic studies . Consequently , structural information about F - actin has been deduced from X - ray fiber diffraction and electron microscopy with recent advances in direct detectors producing near - atomic resolution structures of F - actin using cryo - EM images . 1 . 2 . 4c Structural Models of F - actin The first model of F - actin was obtained in 1990 by fitting a crystal structure of G - actin ( G - actin : DNase I structure ) into an X - ray fibre diagram of oriented F - actin gels by the research group of Ken Holmes ; hence , this structure is called the Holmes model . The Holmes model indicated extensive interactions existing between actin subunits within the strand of F - actin . Interstrand contacts were formed by a loop extending from an actin subunit across to the adjacent strand across the filament axis . Since the loop extended from actin subunit of one strand into a hydrophobic cavity formed by adjacent actin subunits of the opposite strand , it was termed the hydrophobic plug . The Holmes model was accepted as the best approximation of F - actin structure ; however , 14 this model could not describe the structural changes that occurred during the G - to F - actin transition . 52 Almost 20 years later , Oda et al . ( 2009 ) obtained a higher - resolution structure ( 3 . 3 – 5 . 6 Å ) of F - actin from X - ray fibre diffraction and helical reconstruction of actin filaments oriented in a high magnetic field . Gelsolin , an actin - severing protein , was used to control the length of the filaments . 63 This work revealed the G - to F - actin transition : a propeller - like rotation of the two major domains by about 20˚ perpendicular to the helix . As a result of the rotation , all four subdomains lie in the same plane in F - actin , with this state called the flat conformation . In 2010 , Fujii et al . published a model of F - actin at 6 . 6 Å resolution , which not only showed the general conformation of F - actin comparable to previous models , but also revealed individual secondary structural interactions , including loops and probable side chain interactions between actin subunits . 7 In the same year , Galkin et al . proposed that actin filaments adopt multiple conformations that can be only explained by an ensemble of different states . They confirmed the structural contacts described in the previous research . 63 In the multiple structural states of actin described at 10 Å resolution , subdomain 2 was observed in diverse conformations and involved in multiple contacts with the C - terminus of the actin subunit above it . However , contacts between subdomain 3 of the lower subunit and subdomain 4 of the upper subunit within the same helical strand were maintained and consistent within the filament in all the states observed . It was postulated that for the existence of multiple conformational states in an actin filament , cooperativity is required within the filament with the length of a cooperative unit being smaller than the actin filament . 55 15 Furthering their research , Galkin et al . produced the first reliable pseudoatomic model of one of the states of F - actin at 4 . 7 Å in 2015 . The conformation of the actin subunits in the filament was comparable to the crystal structure of the G - actin - profilin complex . Their structure differed in some aspects from previous models . 54 , 63 In contrast to Fujii’s model where the N - terminus of actin was quite rigid , the N - terminus in Galkin’s model was disordered and not visualized in the 3D reconstruction . Similarly , unlike the Holmes model , the hydrophobic plug did not participate in making significant lateral contacts between the strands . Additionally , some differences in the residues involved in longitudinal contacts at the subdomain 3 / 4 interface were reported . This model of F - actin placed most of the mutations associated with diseases at interfaces between the subunits in the filament . In view of the models proposed and considering the conformational changes that ABPs induce upon binding , the multiple structural states of in F - actin reported likely results from the structural plasticity of F - actin and not an experimentally induced artifact . 86 Von Der Ecken et al . ( 2015 ) was the first to report a cryo - EM structure of F - actin using data obtained with a direct detector , producing a resolution of 3 . 7 Å . The model not only confirmed the structural organization observed by previous models , but with higher resolution many salt bridges and inter - and intrastrand interactions were revealed . Like previous studies , the N - and C - termini were not resolved , presumably due to disordered structures . Contacts between actin subunits within a strand ( intrastrand contacts ) were mediated by subdomain 2 and subdomain 4 of one subunit and subdomain 3 of the adjacent subunit within the same strand . Interstrand contacts existing between two strands within a filament , were stabilized by salt bridges formed between subdomain 4 and 3 , and between the D - loop and subdomain 3 of the neighbouring subunits in the two strands . In contrast to previous studies , the D - loop was ordered and involved in several hydrophobic and electrostatic interactions . Similar to earlier studies , it was suggested that the D - 16 Figure 1 . 2 Actin filament is stabilized by intrastrand and interstrand contacts . Neighbouring subunits in F - actin are stabilized by salt bridges ( A , B ) and hydrophobic interactions ( C ) . The central actin subunit is shown in pale cyan and the adjacent subunits in aquamarine and green cyan . Surfaces in ( C ) are coloured from high ( yellow ) to low ( white ) hydrophobicity showing intrastrand interactions . Interactions between amino acids are depicted with dotted lines . Figure adapted from material presented in Von Der Ecken et al . , 2015 using PyMOL and PDB : 3J8A . 4 C A B 17 loop makes contact with the C - terminus of actin ; however , the C - terminus could not be resolved in the cryo - EM density . This observation further suggested that the contacts between these regions are transient . The interstrand interactions were mainly through salt bridges and were not very extensive . As a result , two strands of F - actin were held by a few contacts with large empty space between the strands which is likely required for the flexibility of the filaments ( Figure 1 . 2 ) . 4 Another structural study on Plasmodium falciparum actin 1 ( PfAct1 ) highlighted the impact of small alterations at the important contact sites within F - actin in relation to its functional and structural properties . The cryo - EM structure of jasplakinolide - stabilized PfAct1 filaments was determined at an average resolution of 3 . 8 Å . PfAct1 forms a polar double - stranded helix and has overall filament architecture similar to mammalian F - actin and shares its fold with mammalian G - actin , possessing ~ 80 % sequence identity with animals , yeast and plant actin . 4 , 87 , 88 In addition , PfAct1 interacts with Myosin A and other associated proteins to generate gliding motility needed for the parasite to invade host cells . 89 Unlike mammalian F - actin , PfAct1 does not readily form long stable filaments and this inherent filament instability aids in host cell invasion and infectivity . 90 The cause of filament instability was attributed to some deviations observed in the amino acids at the intra - and interstrand interfaces , particularly in the D - loop . Since actin proteins possess extreme conservation , identifying such differences between isoforms can guide drug discovery towards specific species and highlights the potential of cryo - EM as a technique for structure - based drug design . During the time of the research for this thesis , advances in cryo - EM have generated near - atomic resolution structures of F - actin ; nevertheless , crystallography remains a mainstay to obtain atomic resolution structures of biomolecules . 4 – 7 , 9 The major hindrance in obtaining crystals of authentic actin filaments and in complex with ABPs is actin’s inherent property to self - assemble . 18 This leads to heterogenous solutions of actin molecules . Therefore , attempts continue to control the polymerization of actin to generate oligomers of defined length and stoichiometry for crystallographic studies . 1 . 2 . 5 Actin Modification A wide spectrum of F - actin modifications have been examined to gain an understanding of structural , biological and biophysical aspects of F - actin . Actin filaments have been modified with biomolecules , metallic particles , and diamond nanoparticles . 91 – 94 for nanobiotechnology applications . Additionally , a strategic combination of chemical crosslinking and polymerization inhibition strategies have been used to generate non - polymerizable , short F - actin oligomers of defined length for crystallographic studies . Since my work primarily involves a short F - actin oligomer generated by combination of chemical crosslinking and ribosylation which is a polymerization inhibition technique , a brief description of these two techniques are described below . 1 . 2 . 5a Crosslinking Chemical cross - linkers , such as pPBM ( N , N’ - p - phenylene bismaleimide ) , oPBM ( N , N’ - o - phenylene bismaleimide ) and ANP ( N - ( 4 - azido - 2 - nitrophenyl ) putrescine ) have been used , sometimes in combination with actin mutant proteins , to produce inter - or intrastrand crosslinked filaments . 11 , 68 , 73 pPBM crosslinked actin filaments were first obtained by Knight and Offer in 1978 . 69 Following Knight and Offer’s protocol , a previous graduate student in the Dawson lab produced a crosslinked short F - actin oligomer called the ADPr - trimer . 11 Crosslinking begins upon reaction of one of the maleimide groups of pPBM with the sulfhydryl group of Cys - 374 of one actin subunit . The other maleimide group of pPBM reacts with Lys - 191 of an actin subunit in the opposite strand , resulting in laterally - crosslinked oligomers . The reaction is carried out at pH 9 . 0 19 to activate lysine residues for crosslinking . 69 The reaction yields a mixture of oligomers of varying lengths – dimers , trimers , tetramers and other higher order oligomers . These oligomers are rendered non - polymerizable by an ADP - ribosylation reaction . Careful balancing of the two - step strategy yields pure ADPr - trimer . 1 . 2 . 5b Ribosylation Several strategies , such as chemical modification , amino acid substitutions , and ADP - ribosylation have been used to generate polymerization - deficient actin . Intramonomer chemical crosslinking between Cys - 10 and Cys - 374 , chemical modification of Cys - 374 with tetramethylrhodamine ( TMR ) or binding of a 2 . 6 kDa actin peptide from Arg - 177 to Tyr - 198 to actin itself , inhibit actin polymerization . However , these modifications introduce constraints in the structure of actin , thus limiting this approach . 70 , 95 , 96 Mutational strategies have yielded non - polymerizable actin using the baculovirus / Sf9 cell system ; however , such mutant actin only generated structures of G - actin . 97 Actin is modified by several bacterial toxins that inhibit protein function and have deleterious effects on host cell functioning . Such toxins include mono - ADP - ribosyltransferases , such as Clostridium botulinium C2 toxin , iota toxin from C . perfrigens and Photox from Photorhabdus luminescens . These toxins add an ADP - ribose group from NAD + to Arg - 177 that sterically interferes with the intersubunit interaction across the two strands of F - actin and inhibits actin polymerization . 98 – 100 ADP - ribosylated actin can cap the barbed end of F - actin inhibiting further growth of the filament . Thus , the interactions between the barbed end of the filament and pointed end of ADP - ribosylated actin remain unaffected . 101 In fact , the crystal structure of ADP - ribosylated monomeric actin shows that the ADP - ribose moiety does not induce structural changes in the actin ; thus , polymerization inhibition is through steric disruption . 102 20 Of the several actin polymerization inhibiting strategies , the Dawson laboratory employed the enzyme Photox to ADP - ribosylate pPBM crosslinked F - actin and purify non - polymerizable ADPr - trimer . 99 Mass spectrometry data confirmed that each subunit of the oligomer was ribosylated . 11 1 . 2 . 4c Short F - actin Studies Dawson et al . ( 2003 ) obtained G1 ( gelsolin segment 1 ) - bound trimer by crosslinking F - actin subunits with pPBM and depolymerizing with G1 . The trimer had distorted symmetry compared to the helix of F - actin resulting from intercalation of G1 between the actin subunits . 72 The intercalation of G1 interrupted several interstrand contacts suggesting a mechanism of untwisting and breakage of the actin filament upon G1 binding . A 2 . 5 Å resolution structure of a longitudinal dimer was obtained by crosslinking Gln - 41 and Cys - 374 of two actin subunits with ANP . TMR and the actin - depolymerizing drug latrunculin A were used to inhibit polymerization of the dimers . The crystal structure confirmed the interaction between subdomain 3 and 4 in the actin filament ; however , contacts between dynamic subdomain 2 of the lower subunit and subdomain1 of the upper subunit , and the twist present in F - actin was not observed . 73 Sawaya et al . ( 2008 ) solved crystal structures of longitudinal ( Gln - 41 of the lower subunit crosslinked to Cys - 374 of the upper subunit ) and lateral dimers ( Cys - 374 of one subunit crosslinked to Lys - 191 of adjacent subunit of the opposite strand ) . Subtilisin and Kab C were used to inhibit the polymerization of the lateral and longitudinal dimers , respectively . The configuration of the lateral dimer in the crystal did not resemble actin - actin interactions found in native F - actin . The crystallized longitudinal dimer revealed native F - actin - like interactions between subdomain 4 from the lower subunit and subdomain 3 from the upper subunit . These interactions were similar 21 to those observed in previously described crystals . 103 Due to the lack of a third subunit to establish correct F - actin helical turns in the dimers , no possible lateral and longitudinal interactions were present . 68 In the Dawson lab , a laterally crosslinked non - polymerizable ADPr - trimer was prepared and characterized by Perieteanu et al . ( 2010 ) . 11 Crosslinking between subunits of F - actin was introduced by pPBM , and polymerization was inhibited by ADP - ribosylation . The hydrodynamic radii of the ADPr - trimer measured by dynamic light scattering ( DLS ) was comparable to the theoretical values from X - ray crystallography data . ADPr - trimer bound the ABPs gelsolin and DNase I . Gelsolin binding restored the ability of ADPr - trimer to nucleate actin polymerization , suggesting the presence of conformational flexibility in the ADPr - trimer . Conformational flexibility is one of the characteristics of F - actin required to bind several ABPs . ADPr - trimer retained the ability to bind to the barbed end of pre - existing actin filaments , indicating that the modifications do not distort the pointed end of the trimer . Thus ADPr - trimer retains conformational flexibility and both longitudinal and lateral interactions , along with the twist characteristic of native actin filaments . Consequently , ADPr - trimer was proposed to possess one putative longitudinal interface required for the binding of side binding F - actin binding proteins ( F - ABPs ) . However , further biochemical investigation was required . 11 While the research in this thesis was being undertaken , Qu from the Mannherz research group in Germany ( 2018 ) generated a crosslinked actin oligomer with polymerization blocked through the combination of ADP - ribosylation and G1 binding . In this thesis , I will refer to this trimer as heterologous ( het ) ADPr - trimer because the stoichiometry of ADP - ribosylation and G1 binding was not established , differentiating this actin trimer from the homogeneous ADPr - trimer produced in the Dawson lab which is modified stoichiometrically on each subunit . Rather , the 22 hetADPr - trimer was modified only to the point that it activated myosin S1 ATPase activity and bound myosin S1 under rigor conditions while not forming filaments . A preliminary EM structure shows one myosin S1 bound to the trimer . Such a trimer could potentially provide structural insights into stages of actomyosin interaction which remain unresolved by EM approaches . 104 Given the findings from these studies , short polymerization - deficient F - actin oligomers of defined length can yield a stable and functional complex with myosin and other F - actin binding proteins for determining structural details of steps of force generation and actin function regulation . 1 . 3 Actin Binding Proteins An array of proteins called ABPs regulate organization and functions of actin . Over ~ 120 known ABPs are distributed in eukaryotes . 3 This large number of ABPs have likely evolved to modulate the diverse functions of actin requiring distinct three dimensional actin organizations with specific dynamic properties in the cytoplasm or stable structures in muscle filaments . 105 ABPs nucleate actin filament assembly , promote elongation , sever and crosslink filaments . ABPs can be classified into two broad categories : 1 ) monomer - binding proteins , which bind G - actin and inhibit polymerization ( e . g . Thymosin β4 , DNase I , and Profilin ) and 2 ) F - ABPs , which bind to F - actin . F - ABPs are further classified as follows : i ) F - actin end binding proteins , which cap either the pointed end ( e . g . tropomodulin ) or barbed end ( e . g . Cap Z or gelsolin ) and inhibit monomer exchange ; ii ) filament - stabilizing proteins , which bind along the sides of the filament and inhibit its disassembly ( e . g . tropomyosin ) ; iii ) motor proteins , which bind and move along actin filaments ( e . g . myosin ) ; ( iv ) crosslinking proteins , which bind two or more actin filaments resulting in the formation of filament bundles , branching filaments , and three - 23 dimensional networks ( e . g . Apr2 / 3 ) ; and ( v ) depolymerizing proteins that regulate the state of polymerization of actin filaments ( e . g . cofilin ) . 106 Although the physiological roles of most ABPs are defined , a complete picture with molecular details of interactions between ABPs and F - actin remains to be determined . My research concentrates on understanding these interactions , focusing on gelsolin , myosin S1 , and cofilin , all of which are F - ABPs . In this research , I used ADPr - trimer as a scaffold to bind F - ABPs and generate hetercomplexes for structural studies . 1 . 3 . 1 Myosin 1 . 3 . 1a Biology Myosin is a superfamily of ATP - dependent molecular motor proteins that interact with actin to produce force and movement . 107 There are 35 different classes of myosin . 108 Conventional muscle myosin ( myosin II ) forms filaments in muscles and non - muscle cells . It is a hexameric protein comprised of two heavy chains and two pairs of light chains . 109 , 110 Myosin is an asymmetric molecule consisting of three functional subdomains : 1 ) the N - terminal globular head / motor domain , which binds actin and hydrolyses ATP ; 2 ) the neck domain , which binds essential and regulatory light chains ; and 3 ) the tail domain , which self - associates to form homodimers resulting in a two - headed myosin molecules . 111 The motor head domain consists of four structural domains joined by a flexible helix linker : 1 ) the N - terminal subdomain , 2 ) upper 50 kDa ( U50 ) , 3 ) and lower 50 kDa ( L50 ) subdomains , and 4 ) the converter . 112 Together , the converter domain and the neck region extending from the head domain form the lever arm ( Figure 1 . 3A ) . 113 Myosin produces force by rotation of the lever arm upon actin binding and phosphate release . The U50 and L50 kDa subdomains participate in actin binding , and are separated by a large cleft that closes marginally upon nucleotide binding and significantly upon actin binding . 114 , 115 24 Figure 1 . 3 Myosin interacts with actin to generate force and motion . A ) Ribbon diagram of myosin subfragment depicting the components that form the motor head domain and the neck region ( PDB : 1S5J ) . B ) Schematic representation of mechanism of force generation during actomyosin cycle . Figure adapted from Wulf et al . , 2016 . 5 C ) Myosin head ( limegreen ) bound to actin subunits in the rigor state . Myosin head forms contacts with two actin subunits along the same strand ( cyan and blue ) of F - actin . Figure adapted from Gurel et al . , 2017 using PDB : 6BNV . 6 A B C 25 Papain digestion of myosin yields S1 ( myosin subfragment - 1 ) . This region binds ATP and actin , and the two light chains . It has been observed that S1 generates movement in actin filaments in in vitro experiments and is soluble in a low salt buffer ; thus , S1 is ideal for biochemical and structural characterization . 116 , 117 1 . 3 . 1b Actomyosin Cycle In muscles , actin and myosin interact through a cross - bridge cycle , generating force and movement . The force generation mechanism involves binding and hydrolysis of ATP , inorganic phosphate ( Pi ) release , ADP release and movements in the myosin lever arm accompanied by conformational changes in the actin - myosin interacting interface . 42 Upon hydrolysis of ATP bound to the myosin head , myosin interacts with the actin filament in the weak binding state also known as Pre - Power Stroke ( PPS ) . The PPS is followed by release of Pi , transitioning myosin to the ADP state and a large - scale repositioning of the myosin lever arm leading to a power stroke generating force and movement . 113 At the end of the power stroke , ADP is released transitioning to the nucleotide free conformation of myosin bound to actin , otherwise known as the rigor state . 118 , 119 Subsequently , with the binding of ATP , myosin detaches from the actin filament and the cycle repeats . 120 , 121 Biochemical assays detect Pi released during the actomyosin interaction as part of kinetic studies of this interaction in vitro ( Figure 1 . 3B ) . 1 . 3 . 1c Structural Models of Actomyosin Interaction Since F - actin is resistant to crystallization , information regarding actomyosin interactions is derived from X - ray fibre diffraction , cryo - EM , chemical crosslinking , and the use of FRET ( Förster resonance energy transfer ) , peptides , and antibodies . 65 , 122 – 127 26 Holmes et al . ( 2004 ) described interactions at the actomyosin interface by fitting a crystal structure of myosin - V into cryo - EM maps of actin decorated with chicken skeletal S1 . They reported that the L50 kDa domain of myosin participated in the formation of the interface . 65 Lorenz et al . ( 2010 ) obtained a 13 Å resolution structure of the actomyosin interface during strong binding using molecular dynamics simulations constrained by an EM map of the complex . Their model suggested that myosin S1 forms considerable contacts with two actin subunits . Regions of the U50 and L50 subdomains and flexible loop - 2 that is present between U50 and L50 of S1 , and the D - loop of actin contribute to the formation of the actomyosin interface ( Figure 1 . 3C ) . 125 Behrmann et al . ( 2012 ) proposed an 8 Å resolution structure of the actin - tropomyosin - myosin complex using cryo - EM . Myosin interacts with two adjacent actin subunits via several loops through salt bridges , hydrophobic and electrostatic interactions . 127 Following up on their high - resolution structure of F - actin bound by tropomyosin ( 2015 paper ) , Von Der Ecken et al . ( 2016 ) presented the first cryo - EM structure of an actomyosin complex using a direct detector at an average resolution of 3 . 9 Å . They found that the general structure of the rigor complex was similar to the previously described 8 Å structure published in 2012 from the same research group . 127 Since side chains were identifiable in their structure , most interactions at the actomyosin interface were revealed . The most prominent myosin - induced conformational change in F - actin was observed at the N - and C - termini of the actin subunits . The N - terminus was completely ordered in the structure and the two N - terminal glutamate residues of actin were involved in the formation of salt bridges with positively charged residues in myosin . Changes in the N - terminus were transmitted to the nucleotide binding pocket of actin , yet the positions of ADP and Mg 2 + were not greatly impacted . Interestingly , the C - terminus was also 27 completely ordered in this state ; however , it did not participate in the formation of the rigor actomyosin surface . It was postulated that the myosin - induced stability of the N - terminus and adjacent regions likely stabilizes the C - terminus . Thus , the role of the C - terminus in formation of actomyosin surface remains unclear . Moreover , with no high - resolution structures of intermediate states of myosin bound to actin , whether Pi is released before or after the power stroke also remained unexplained . Wulf et al . ( 2016 ) described structural rearrangements occurring in myosin maintaining the Mg - ADP bound state which lead to ADP release and subsequent force generation and the rigor state . The structure of myosin bound to F - actin in rigor and the Mg - ADP state at 7 – 9 Å revealed conformational changes occurring during the transition of Mg - ADP bound state to the rigor state with lever arm movement . Although the Mg - ADP state of myosin bound to actin is a crucial state for actomyosin force generating cycle , only low resolution information of this state was described . 5 Structural transitions induced in myosin upon ATP binding and hydrolysis to force generation were further clarified by Gurel et al . ( 2017 ) . They compared cryo - EM structures of the actomyosin interface in rigor ( 4 . 6 Å ) and the Mg - ADP state ( 5 . 5 Å ) with the previously proposed structures of myosin VI in pre - and post - power strokes . 6 Their model supported mutual structural reorganization in actin and myosin during the transition between subsequent states of the actomyosin cycle , suggesting an active role for structural flexibility in the actomyosin crossbridge cycle . Conformational changes in the actin filaments decorated with myosin in various nucleotide states of the actomyosin cycle have been characterized at an intermediate resolution 5 and through pyrene fluorescence quenching studies . 5 , 71 , 113 , 128 Gurel et al . confirmed that the reorganization of the converter occurs from Pi release state to ADP state with the converter adopting a post - power stroke and rigor state conformation . 113 Nonetheless , understanding the specific molecular 28 interactions involved in transitions between nucleotide states , myosin conformation , and actin filament involvement requires visualization of transient actomyosin states that lead from pre - power stroke to rigor state . Owing to the low affinity binding in some states , this task is challenging . Mentes et al . ( 2018 ) described the structure of the motor domain bound to actin in rigor state at 3 . 9 Å and two ADP - bound states at 3 . 3 Å . They called the two ADP - bound states as AM . ADP A and AM . ADP B . The two ADP - bound myosin states revealed a distinct position of the lever arm and were proposed to present a mechanistic succession of states leading to the rigor state . AM . ADP A state is characterized by the movement of the N - terminal subdomain of myosin causing the nucleotide binding site to open , facilitating release of ADP . Conformational changes resulting from opening of the nucleotide binding site are transmitted to lever arm movement . The AM . ADP B state represents an intermediate state leading to the rigor state in which the nucleotide binding site is almost closed and the lever arm position is similar , but not identical , to the rigor state . It was proposed that mechanical loads that prevent the rotation of the lever arm and movement of the N - terminal subdomain required to release ADP upon the transition to the rigor state influence power output . 7 Further structural and functional studies are required to achieve a full understanding of specific conformational changes at the actomyosin interface that are associated with different nucleotide binding states of myosin and lever arm movement for force production . 1 . 3 . 3d Myosin and Diseases Myosin has been associated with pathogenesis of various diseases . Hypertrophic cardiomyopathy characterized by thickening of the left ventricular wall is caused by mutation in any of the ~ 13 genes that encode contractile proteins of the cardiac muscle ; mutations in the 29 myosin heavy chain gene MYH7 and cardiac myosin binding protein C account for approximately 50 % of all known HCM - related mutations . 129 – 131 Mutations in the skeletal muscle myosin heavy chain gene MYH7 lead to myopathies , including Laing distal myopathy and myosin storage myopathy . The phenotypes of these diseases are diverse ranging from prenatal non - progressive arthrogrypotic syndromes characterized by joint stiffness , to adult onset progressive muscle weakness . 132 Mutations in the non - muscle myosin gene MYH9 has been linked to the May - Hegglin anomaly characterized by abnormal morphology of platelets and leukocytes . 133 Mutations in genes encoding non - muscle myosin VIIA , which plays an important role in organizing actin filaments to form the core of stereocilia in the internal ear , causes Usher syndrome . This syndrome is characterized by deafness and is associated with the loss of vision . 134 - 135 An autosomal recessive mutation in MYO5A , a gene encoding unconventional cytoplasmic myosin - Vb , results in Elejalde syndrome . 136 Patients are reported to have albinism and a number of neurological deficits such as seizures , severe muscle hypotonia and mental retardation . Biochemical and structural characterization of actomyosin interactions can help better understand the mechanisms of diseases and aid in development of potential therapeutics . 1 . 3 . 2 Cofilin 1 . 3 . 2a Biology Cofilin is a member of the ADF / Cofilin family which is expressed in all eukaryotic cells . The members of this family are small proteins that exist as several isoforms with three isoforms being expressed in mammals . These three isoforms regulate actin dynamics in cells and include : Actin depolymerizing factor ( ADF ) found in epithelial and endothelial cells , cofilin - 1 found primarily in non - muscle cells , and cofilin - 2 mainly found in muscle cells . Both ADF and cofilin - 1 have similar roles in regulating actin dynamics ; however , ADF is more efficient in monomer 30 sequestering , while cofilin is more efficient in nucleation and severing . 137 Many studies reported in the literature do not specify the isoform being studied in relation to their depolymerizing abilities because of similar functions of the isoforms and the inability of available antibodies to identify different isoforms . 138 Consequently , the term cofilin is used to describe members of the family , except when specific roles have been studied and described . Cofilin - 1 is generally referred to as cofilin and has been most widely studied because of its ubiquitous presence and its role in embryonic development . 137 Cofilin is best described as a regulator of actin filament assembly - disassembly . In quiescent cells , cofilin is distributed throughout the cytoplasm ; whereas in active cells , cofilin localizes in the cortical regions with a high degree of actin turnover . In the cortical region of active cells , cofilin regulates the ruffling of membranes in motile cells , the formation of the cell division cleavage furrow , as well as the neuronal growth cone . 139 – 141 Cofilin drives filament disassembly by first severing actin filaments and then promoting depolymerization at the ends of the severed filaments . 142 Besides F - actin , cofilin also binds to G - actin in an equimolar ratio that inhibits its polymerization . 143 The role of cofilin depends on the relative concentration of cofilin to actin and to other ABPs . 144 In vitro studies have indicated that at a low ratio of cofilin / actin , cofilin exhibits severing activity while at a high cofilin / actin ratio , cofilin first severs rapidly and then stabilizes actin filaments . 145 Bamburg et al . ( 2010 ) reported that at a higher molar ratio of cofilin / actin ( 1 : 10 to 1 : 2 ) , cofilin severs filaments and because of its cooperative binding , then it binds the severed fragments of filaments and stabilizes them . In vivo , bundles of ADP - actin stabilized by cofilin known as rods are formed during oxidative stress , however a complete understanding of the physiological effect of cofilin concentration on its function is not known . 146 31 Figure 1 . 4 Cofilin decorated actin filament . Cofilin , an actin subunit and other subunits shown in orange , skyblue and cyan , respectively . Cofilin binds to two actin subunits along the length of the actin filament . Cofilin binding induces significant structural changes in the actin filaments resulting in disruption of the canonical interactions between actin subunits within the filament . The changes are cooperatively propagated to the neighbouring actin subunits in the undecorated regions destabilizing the filament . In the decorated regions cofilin maintains the crosslink between actin subunits . Figure generated with PyMol and PDB : 5YU8 . 8 32 Besides dependence on concentration , in vitro studies indicate the influence of pH on the interaction of cofilin with actin filaments . At pH lower than 6 . 8 , cofilin binds cooperatively between two actin subunits along the filament inducing a change in the twist of the filament . At pH greater than 7 . 3 , cofilin rapidly depolymerizes actin filaments . 147 In vivo , the pH dependency of cofilin function potentially stabilizes actin filaments in the vicinity of Na + - H + exchangers . 148 Cofilin is also known to accelerate the assembly of actin monomers . 143 , 149 Because cofilin binds to two actin subunits along the long pitch of the actin helix , it can stabilize long pitch actin dimers that are required to initiate polymerization . 150 , 151 In the presence of cofilin , actin labeled by tetramethylrhodamine at Cys - 374 does not polymerize forms short filaments , perhaps by substituting actin - actin contacts modified by tetramethylrhodamine . 152 1 . 3 . 2b Structural Models and Mechanism of Action Cofilin binding sites on F - actin were first determined at a resolution of 27 . 5 Å by cryo - EM and helical reconstruction of cofilin - bound actin filaments . Cofilin cooperatively binds with two longitudinally associated actin subunits within a strand of F - actin ( Figure 1 . 4 ) . Cofilin binds axially at subdomain 2 of the lower actin subunit and radially at the cleft between subdomain 1 and 3 of the upper actin subunit . This work was the first to reveal the ability of cofilin to significantly change the twist of the filament that produces a strain in the filament resulting in fragmentation . The filaments decorated with cofilin were shown to have ~ 25 % lower crossover length compared to canonical F - actin . Another interesting finding was that although phalloidin binds to F - actin at a site distinct and distant to cofilin , cofilin and phalloidin do not simultaneous bind to actin filaments . These findings were the first to demonstrate that F - ABPs compete for 33 binding by altering the twist of the filament rather than mutual exclusion that could be attributed to overlapping binding sites . 150 Galkin et al . ( 2011 ) proposed a mode of cofilin - induced F - actin severing based on the 3D reconstruction of cofilin - decorated F - actin at 9 Å from cryo - EM maps . They confirmed previously described cofilin - binding sites on F - actin and related cofilin induced changes in the twist of the actin filament with the conformational changes occurring in the actin subunits . Cofilin first binds to subdomain 1 of actin and twists it towards the opposite strand bringing subdomain 2 along with it . This rotation causes the outer subdomain 1 and 2 to rotate by 30˚ towards the opposite strand within the actin filament . As a result , the longitudinal contacts between actin subunits within a strand are disrupted . However , the contacts between subdomains 3 and 4 remain unaltered in contrast to altered contacts between subdomains 1 and 2 of adjacent subunits . Interestingly , cofilin maintains a crosslink between the two longitudinal actin subunits to which it is bound , but cofilin - induced conformational changes are propagated into the undecorated regions of the actin filament . In the absence of cofilin , the filament severs ( Figure 1 . 5 ) . 153 In 2018 , Tanaka et al . presented a 3 . 8 Å resolution structure of F - actin decorated with cofilin and described the mechanism of weakening of inter - and intrastrand leading to severing of actin filaments . They supported the previously proposed idea of cooperative binding of cofilin to F - actin and explained that , during cofilin induced conformational changes , the inner domain ( subdomain 3 and 4 ) and the outer subdomain 1 act as two independently rotating rigid bodies . It is by the relative movement of these two rigid bodies that ABPs regulate conformational changes in the actin subunits of the filament . 8 34 Figure 1 . 5 Cofilin changes the twist of actin filaments . When cofilin ( A ) binds to the side of F - actin ( B ) , the α - 1helix ( green ) of cofilin clashes with the SD1 of actin ( magenta arrow ) . Thus , the outer domain shown by red arrow rotates by approximately 30֯ towards the opposite helical strand to rectify the clash . Upon arranging cofilin deformed actin subunits ( C ) into the canonical F - actin structure , clashes between α4 - helix of cofilin and the lower part of SD1 of actin n + 2 ( red arrowheads ) are observed . These clashes are resolved by rotation of the n + 2 subunit by 10֯ ( D ) around the helical axis ( red arrow ) . Figure taken from Galkin et al . 2011 with permission . 157 A B C D 35 The mechanism proposed by Tanaka et al . also explains the preference of cofilin for ADP - F - actin . 8 In the first step of cofilin binding to F - actin , cofilin binds to subdomain 1 of the ADP - actin subunit within the actin filament . Since ADP bound actin filaments exhibit larger bending and twisting fluctuations than ATP - actin and computer simulations confirm that ADP - F - actin undergoes larger domain fluctuations , such fluctuations in subdomain 1 permit cofilin to span subdomain 1 and its binding site on the next subunit towards the pointed end . 154 – 156 The cooperative binding of cofilin is a consequence of conformational changes that propagate from clusters of bound cofilin to bare actin segments on F - actin . The conformational change required for cooperativity was estimated to be from 2 to > 100 subunits . 158 – 161 Huehn et al . ( 2018 ) used a structure - based method for classifying individual filament subunits for detecting small variations in the twist of the actin filament using cryo - EM micrographs . They found that the cofilin - induced changes propagate to 1 - 2 subunits , thereby limiting the mechanistic models of cooperative actin filament severing by cofilin . A distinct and abrupt change in twist was observed at the boundaries between bare and cofilin bond actin segments . 162 Although the structural basis of severing at the boundary of bare and cofilin decorated filaments is not known , this model suggested that the abrupt or distinct conformations adopted by neighboring subunits potentially causes disruption of the subunit interfaces . 163 , 164 The large conformational changes in the actin filament upon cofilin binding reinforces the plastic nature of actin and that ABPs can induce different conformational changes allowing them to bind in a mutually exclusive manner . 36 1 . 3 . 2c Functions Directed Movement Cofilin defines the direction of cell motility , which is essential for physiological processes such as embryogenesis , neutrophil and macrophage - mediated chemotaxis , lymphocyte - mediated immunity and wound healing . During cell movement , cofilin influences actin turnover at a plasma membrane protrusion formed in response to migratory stimuli . 43 At the extension of the plasma membrane protrusion , an increased number of free barbed ends are required . These barbed ends are increased by severing of actin filaments by coflin . 165 Additionally , cofilin increases actin turnover by increasing the rate of monomer dissociation from the pointed end of the severed filaments . 148 , 149 However , it is yet to be determined how a balance is maintained between barbed end generation , subsequent depolymerization , and cofilin - mediated depolymerization . 149 , 166 , 167 Nuclear Transportation of Actin Although actin does not possess a nuclear localization sequence , it is known to function in chromatin remodeling , ribonucleoprotein complex formation and gene expression . However , cofilin possesses a nuclear localization sequence and has been suggested to have a role in translocating actin to nucleus . 168 , 169 Homeostasis The role of cofilin in maintaining cellular homeostasis in now being understood . Cofilin can act to correct physiological perturbations by regulating actin dynamics . For example , when a cell is energetically stressed during a decline in cellular ATP , cofilin - actin ADP rods ( bundles of cofilin saturated filaments ) appear in cells . These structures reduce the ATP being consumed by 37 actin turnover . 170 These rods potentially maintain normal oxidative potential and are transiently neuroprotective . However , if these rods persist they can accumulate hyper - phosphorylated tau protein , and lead to neural degeneration . 171 1 . 3 . 2d Role in Diseases Cofilin is essential for actin - based motility which is important for embryogenesis , health and disease . It has been observed that cofilin - deficient mice cannot survive due to defects in proliferation , polarization and migration required during embryogenesis . 172 , 173 Dysregulation of cofilin has been associated with various stages of cancer development including secondary immunodeficiencies observed in cancer patients . Macrophages ( tumor reactive T - cells ) infiltrating tumor cells produce enough peroxide to oxidize cofilin . Oxidized cofilin can bind F - actin but is incapable of remodeling it ; as a result levels of F - actin are increased , reducing motility and suppressing the immune response . 174 Cofilin is also reported to be involved in HIV - 1 infection . One of the mechanisms of cofilin activity regulation by phosphorylation on residue Ser3 by LIM kinases inhibits its interaction with actin . 175 HIV - 1 inactivates cofilin directly or indirectly via LIM kinase phosphorylation . This modification impairs the motility of T - lymphocytes and enables the pathogen to evade the immune system . 176 1 . 3 . 3 Gelsolin 1 . 3 . 3a Biology Gelsolin , an 82 - 84 kDa protein , is the founding member of the gelsolin protein superfamily and includes seven proteins : gelsolin , adseverin , villin , capG , advillin , supervillin and flightless I . 38 The members of the gelsolin superfamily are calcium dependent multidomain proteins that regulate the reorganization of the actin cytoskeleton . Gelsolin was identified by Yin and Stossel in 1979 as a regulatory protein in macrophage extracts with the ability to initiate gel - sol transformations of actin filaments in the presence of calcium ; hence , they named it gelsolin . 177 Gelsolin is found in all eukaryotes and exists in two well characterized isoforms : cytoplasmic and plasma gelsolin ; and a lesser known isoform , gelsolin 3 . The isoforms are encoded by a single gene and are derived from differential splicing of the same gene product . 178 , 179 The plasma and cellular gelsolin differ slightly in their molecular weight ( plasma gelsolin 83 kDa ) as plasma gelsolin has a short 25 amino acid peptide at the N - terminus ; otherwise their sequences are identical . 180 , 181 Functionally , gelsolin regulates cellular motility and cytoskeletal remodeling . 182 , 183 The diverse functions of gelsolin is attributed to its ability to sever actin filaments in the presence of calcium and then cap the severed ends , thereby blocking the addition of monomers . Alternatively , gelsolin can bind two actin monomers and initiate actin polymerization . 184 , 185 1 . 3 . 3b Structure and Binding to F - actin The mechanism of actin filament severing by gelsolin is mechanical , with the stoichiometric binding of gelsolin to F - actin subunits followed by weakening and disruption of non - covalent interactions between actin subunits . After severing , gelsolin caps the barbed end of the severed filament , inhibiting elongation at the barbed end and resulting in disassembly of actin filaments . 186 Gelsolin is composed of six gelsolin - like domains named G1 - G6 . The gelsolin molecule can be subdivided into two homologous halves , the N - terminal G1 - G3 and C - terminal G4 - G6 . The N - and C - terminal halves are connected by a long linker . These two halves are thought to be the result of a gene triplication with subsequent duplication ( Figure 1 . 6A ) . 180 Gelsolin adopts a 39 closed inactive conformation in the absence of calcium , while calcium activates gelsolin to bind and sever actin filaments . Based on calcium sensitivity , three actin binding sites have been identified by proteolytic fragmentation of gelsolin : G1 binds actin monomer independent of calcium , G2 - 3 binds the actin filament independent of calcium and G4 - 6 binds actin monomer in a calcium dependent manner . 187 G1 and G4 can bind to actin monomers , whereas G2 binds actin filaments . G1 and G2 possess severing and capping ability , whereas domains G4 - 6 confer calcium sensitivity on severing and are needed to nucleate polymerization . 188 , 189 In the calcium - free inactive state , gelsolin folds compactly with G6 in the center and the other domains arranged around it such that all the actin binding surfaces are blocked . 190 The crystal structure of inactive gelsolin in the presence of EGTA showed that the ‘latch helix’ , a tail extension with a short terminal helix at the C - terminus , blocks the putative actin binding site on G2 . 190 Since calcium binding accompanies large scale conformational changes , a high resolution structure of calcium - activated gelsolin remains elusive . 191 , 192 Nevertheless , a calcium active crystal structure of G4 - 6 by itself and bound to G - actin highlights significant conformational changes and rearrangements in the C - terminal domains of gelsolin upon calcium binding . 193 Further , with the structure of G4 - 6 : actin , G4 was identified as the second monomer binding site , binding to an actin monomer in a manner similar to G1 . 194 The crystal structure of G1 bound to G - actin provided the picture of the gelsolin - fold found in all the six domains ( G - 1 - G6 ) of the gelsolin molecule and its binding site on actin . G1 binds to monomeric actin in the cleft present between subdomain 1 and 3 close to the barbed end ( Figure 1 . 6B , 1 . 6C ) . 195 In the absence of an atomic resolution structure , gelsolin binding sites on F - actin have been identified by cryo - EM structures obtained by helical reconstruction and difference mapping . To control the rapid severing ability of gelsolin , imaging was conducted on filaments decorated with 40 a G2 - 6 derivative of gelsolin which lacks the G1 required for severing . Gelsolin presumably bound via G2 - G3 to two actin longitudinally - associated subunits along the length of the filament as suggested previously by Pope et al . ( 1991 ) . Gelsolin binds radially between SD1 and SD3 of the upper actin subunit and SD1 and SD2 of the lower actin subunit . 186 1 . 3 . 3c Stages of Filament Severing The general mechanism of gelsolin severing has been deduced from the available structural and biochemical data . Although incomplete , the proposed mechanism provides a basis for future research . Severing by gelsolin begins with the binding of G2 to an actin filament subunit , followed by rapid severing and capping of the barbed end of the newly formed filament by gelsolin . 184 , 188 The steps of the severing mechanism are summarized below : Calcium Activation The process of severing is initiated by activation of gelsolin via calcium binding . Gelsolin has two type - 1 and six type - 2 calcium binding sites . Type - 2 sites are present on all the domains of gelsolin and calcium binding to these sites results in small scale local structural changes . In contrast , type - 1 sites exist at the actin binding interface of G1 and G4 . At submicromolar concentrations , calcium binds to type - 2 sites on G5 and G6 and causes the release of the C - terminal helix latch , subsequently exposing the actin filament binding site on G2 . 190 , 196 Full activation of the molecule occurs upon binding of additional calcium to domains G1 , G2 and G4 , thus saturating the molecule with calcium and allowing for actin binding and severing . 194 Filament Binding In the next step , the exposed F - actin binding site on G2 binds to two longitudinally associated actin subunits within a strand of the actin filament . Subsequently , G2 binding directs 41 G1 , the calcium independent monomer binding domain , to its binding site on the actin filament . 197 , 198 Filament Severing Once G2 binds to the actin filament , severing occurs rapidly . G1 wedges its way through two longitudinally associated actin subunits within a strand of F - actin , disrupting actin - actin interactions along one strand of the actin filament . It is not clear if there are additional steps in the severing mechanism that lead to complete disruption of contacts in both strands of the actin filament . The severing ability of gelsolin segments G1 - G3 is similar to that of full - length gelsolin . 187 , 189 , 199 Filament Capping and Uncapping Although not clear yet , it is presumed that capping involves interactions between domain G4 of gelsolin and a barbed end subunit of the actin filament . It is also postulated that gelsolin contacts three actin subunits during severing , while during capping it is associated with two actin subunits . 200 Uncapping of the filament occurs on interaction of the N - terminal half of gelsolin with polyphosphoinositides ( PPIs ) . 201 A model of actin filaments capped with gelsolin has been determined by information gained from X - ray crystallography , EM and NMR spectroscopy in relation to biochemical data available . G2 binds and bridges two actin subunits along the long helix . It binds to the small outer domain of one actin subunit , the same actin subunit to which G1 binds , and an actin subunit below it towards the pointed end . 200 , 202 , 203 The binding of G1 and G2 on the adjacent subunits of the same strand along the long pitch helix was supported by the crystal structure of G1 : actin with a G1 construct containing the linker between G1 and G2 positioned on the surface of actin . 200 , 203 – 205 42 Figure 1 . 6 Structural and functional domains of gelsolin . A ) Domains have been numbered as described for human plasma gelsolin . 190 Actin , calcium and PIP2 binding sites are shown . B ) List of structural data on gelsolin obtained from X - ray crystallography with their PDB ID . 72 , 190 , 193 – 195 , 198 , 206 – 208 C ) Crystal structures of segments of gelsolin alone and bound to G - actin ( pink ) . Domains of gelsolin shown in surface representation : G1 ( pale cyan ) , G2 ( violet purple ) , G3 ( forest ) , G4 ( sky blue ) , G5 ( red ) , G6 ( green ) and the linkers shown in cartoon ( gray ) . 1D0N 1NPH 1EQY 1H1V 3FFK A B C 43 Figure 1 . 7 Schematic representation of gelsolin binding and severing mechanism . An actin filament with subunits from one strand colored cyan and those from the other strand colored pink ( pointed end oriented up ) . Gelsolin with its six domains ( G1 - G6 ) is represented by circles connected by linkers of varying lengths ( a ) . Upon binding of calcium to G6 , the salt bridges between G2 and G6 are broken and the C - terminal latch helix is released ( b ) . Consequently , F - actin binding site on G2 is exposed . Further binding of calcium to G5 completes activation of gelsolin . G2 binds to two longitudinally associated actin subunits ( c ) . Following binding of G2 , G1 is directed to its binding site on actin ( d ) . Severing and capping occurs when G4 - G6 reaches across the filament and binds to actin subunit on adjacent strand of F - actin . Gelsolin remains bound to the barbed end of the filament forming a cap that prevents actin monomers from being added to the filament . There are two possible modes of capping ( e - I and f - I ) . G4 can place itself on different actin subunits on the opposite strand of actin filament . The flexibility of actin filament could contribute to formation of cap ( e - II and f - II ) . In the presence of PIP2 , gelsolin is released from severed filament allowing polymerization at the barbed end . F - actin obtained from PDB : 3G37 .
