Figure adapted from McGough et al . , 2003 . 209 e - II a b d c f - I f - II e - I 44 The positioning of the G4 - 6 segment of gelsolin in the cap on actin is not clear . It is generally agreed that G4 extends across the filament axis , with G4 binding to the actin subunit of the adjacent strand of F - actin . Two possible modes of binding of G4 - 6 have been suggested . Most models suggest that G4 binds to the subunit adjacent to that binding G1 and G2 along the short pitch of the actin helix . Such binding requires the G3 - 4 linker to span 100 Å , which is the distance between the C - terminus of G3 and the N - terminus of G4 , if no significant conformational changes occur in this region upon calcium binding . 186 , 205 Alternatively , G4 could bind to the subunit in the same strand that is above the subunit opposite to the one binding G1 and G2 . In this case the linker would need to span 75 Å . It is possible that the flexibility of F - actin aids in formation of the capped end ( Figure 1 . 7 ) . 210 – 213 Further research is required to obtain a complete picture of the steps of gelsolin binding , severing and capping . Due to the inability of F - actin to crystallize , no structure of gelsolin capped F - actin has been produced . Here I aimed to generate the first near atomic resolution structure using a single particle approach to gain insights into the interaction sites of gelsolin capped F - actin using ADPr - trimer . Detailing and understanding the mechanism of gelsolin binding to actin will advance our understanding of the role of gelsolin in physiological process and various pathologies . This information can then be applied to their potential role as biomarkers or therapeutic targets . 1 . 3 . 3d Functions The physiological role of gelsolin includes processes that require cytoskeletal remodeling . Gelsolin is generally expressed in all embryonic and adult tissues of mesenchymal and epithelial origin . 214 , 215 Cytoplasmic gelsolin is particularly expressed in platelets , macrophages , neutrophils , smooth muscle cells and osteoblasts . 216 , 217 Plasma gelsolin is secreted chiefly by muscle cells . 179 45 Cell motility The role of gelsolin in cellular motility was first observed in gelsolin transfected cultured fibroblasts which exhibited increased mobility . 182 Later , in vivo evidence was provided by gelsolin null mice ( Gsn - / - ) . Fibroblasts in gelsolin null mice had increased stress fibers , no ruffling in response to epidermal growth factor , diminished chemotaxis and delayed wound repair . 216 , 218 In another study , osteoclasts in gelsolin null mice could not form cell adhesion structures , podosomes , resulting in reduced motility . Additionally , the retraction process in neuronal growth cones from which lamellipodia and filopodia form and retract to facilitate growth of axons , appeared to be delayed . 219 Phagocytosis and Wound Healing A continuous rearrangement of the cytoskeleton is required for phagocytosis . Using gelsolin null mice , gelsolin has been shown to play a role in phagocytosis . 220 Despite the evidence of the role of gelsolin in actin cytoskeleton remodeling required for phagocytosis , details of the mechanism is not clear . Gelsolin is the only actin severing protein expressed in megakaryocytes and is suggested to play a role in actin remodeling required for the formation of platelets from cytoplasmic extensions of mature megakaryocytes . 221 Moreover , prolonged bleeding in mutant mice following an injury indicate that gelsolin is required for platelet activation and shape changes during wound repair . 216 Apoptosis Caspases are a family of proteases that initiate apoptosis . One of the members of caspases , caspase - 3 , targets gelsolin . Caspase - 3 cleaves gelsolin such that the generated gelsolin fragment loses calcium control over its severing ability and activates actin cytoskeleton depolymerization . 183 46 Paradoxically , gelsolin not only regulates apoptosis , but also inhibits the apoptotic process . Jurket cells expressing three - fold more gelsolin were more resistant to apoptosis induced by several stimuli . 222 In an in vitro and in vivo apoptotic pathway study , gelsolin was shown to form a complex with phosphoinositides and caspase - 3 which was thought to inhibit the activity of gelsolin resulting in loss of ability of gelsolin to bind actin . 223 Despite the evidence , the role of gelsolin in inhibition of apoptosis is controversial . Role of gelsolin in development Despite the role of gelsolin in a variety of cellular processes , gelsolin null mice develop and reproduce normally . However , the increased bleeding time due to altered platelet function and inflammatory response due to the decreased migratory ability of neutrophils and motility of fibroblasts results in slower wound healing . 216 It is interesting that despite the involvement of gelsolin in regulating physiological processes involving cytoskeleton remodeling , deletion of the gelsolin gene is not lethal . However , processes relying on cell shape changes and cell motility are delayed , but not abrogated . Likely , this lack of lethality in gelsolin null mice is caused by a compensatory mechanism by other members of the gelsolin family . Further investigations are required to completely understand the function and overlap of gelsolin with other members of this family . 224 1 . 3 . 3e Role in Diseases Since its identification , gelsolin has been implicated in a large number of pathological processes such as amyloidosis , inflammation and oncogenic transformation . 225 A variant of gelsolin ( D187Y or D187N ) leads to a hereditable autosomal amyloid polyneuropathy called Finnish type familial amyloidosis ( FAF ) . 226 The disease manifests as corneal lattice dystrophy , progressive cranial and peripheral neuropathy and changes in skin . 227 The amyloid deposition 47 found in the peripheral and central nervous system found in FAF patients is composed mainly of 5 - 8 kDa fragments of gelsolin . The plasma gelsolin obtained from FAF patients is unable to sever or nucleate actin ; however , the remodeling activity of cytoplasmic gelsolin in these patients is unaffected . 228 , 229 With its role in cytoskeletal reorganization , gelsolin has been associated with acute and chronic inflammatory conditions . Gelsolin null mice show slower leukocyte accumulation , thus slower cellular responses to an inflammatory stimulus in the early acute phase . 216 In rheumatoid arthritis , a chronic inflammatory disease , rheumatoid synovial fibroblasts exhibit severe alterations in cytoskeletal reorganization due to failure of expression of gelsolin . 230 Crohn’s disease , another chronic inflammatory condition of the intestine caused when the contractile smooth muscle transforms to migratory cells , is associated with an increase in the expression of gelsolin . 231 . Thus , gelsolin may be a target for anti - inflammatory therapy . Several studies indicate the involvement of gelsolin in the formation of cancer . A reduced expression of the gelsolin gene by 60 - 90 % has been observed during tumor initiation in breast , colon , stomach , bladder , prostrate and lung . 232 – 235 Gelsolin has been suggested as a tumor suppressor gene in breast carcinoma . 236 , 237 1 . 3 . 3f Gelsolin as a Therapeutic Molecule Cytoplasmic actin is released in the systemic circulation upon tissue damage or necrosis . The released cellular actin can form filaments due to the favorable ionic conditions . The presence of continued circulating actin can initiate pathways that lead to secondary tissue damage resulting in a condition similar to multiorgan dysfunction . 238 Therefore , an extracellular scavenger system which includes gelsolin sequesters and clears plasma of circulating actin . A depletion in gelsolin levels has been observed in tissue injury syndromes , such as acute liver failure , septic shock , acute 48 lung injury , cardiac infarction and myonecrosis . 239 Exogenous infusion of recombinant gelsolin in burn - injured rats completely prevents an increase in pulmonary microvascular permeability suggesting the potential use of gelsolin to prevent inflammation - induced pulmonary microvascular dysfunction . 240 Inflammation and apoptosis in burn survivors results in long term cognitive impairment . Animal models suggest that infusion of gelsolin improves survival of mice with burn injuries by reducing inflammation and apoptosis in the brain . 241 Gelsolin rapidly decreases the viscosity of cystic fibrosis ( CF ) sputum in vitro , indicating its potential use as mucolytic agent to clear obstruction of airways by viscous sputum in patients suffering from CF . The earliest known role of gelsolin is calcium dependent remodeling of the actin cytoskeleton . Studies have now extended the potential of gelsolin as a therapeutic molecule in inflammatory events or targeting to inhibit cell migration as in cancer and metastasis . 242 – 244 Obtaining a structure revealing the interaction sites of gelsolin on F - actin can lead to an understanding of the mechanism of action of gelsolin and its role in pathological states . Thus , gelsolin - bound ADPr - trimer complex was purified for structural determination . 1 . 4 Protein Structure Determination 1 . 4 . 1 X - ray crystallography and Cryo - EM – Complementary or Alternative techniques ? Since its introduction in the 1950s , the field of structural biology has played an instrumental role in deciphering cellular processes by revealing the shape and structure of biomolecules . Moreover , knowledge of the spatial relationship between atoms within biomolecules and their rearrangement during molecular interactions describes not only their design and purpose , but also provides the basis for target identification , optimization and discovery in the field of drug development . 245 , 246 Several structural determination methodologies including X - ray 49 crystallography , cryo - EM , Nuclear Magnetic Resonance ( NMR ) , X - ray solution scattering and neutron diffraction have transformed our understanding of physiological processes . 247 Since its discovery , X - ray crystallography has been the mainstay technique for solving the structure of biomolecules at atomic resolution . To date , over 89 % of biomolecule structures deposited in the Protein Data Bank ( PDB ) are derived from X - ray crystallography . 248 Obtaining protein structures with this technique begins with the crystallization of a purified protein homogenous in both composition and conformation . The protein is crystallized at a very high concentration and exposed to an x - ray beam . The resulting diffraction pattern encodes the arrangement of atoms within a crystal and is processed to obtain an electron density map which is used to solve the atomic details of the macromolecule . To begin , X - ray crystallography requires large quantities of highly pure protein to optimize crystallization conditions . Additionally , rigorous molecular engineering , such as side chain modifications or proteolysis , may be required to improve the quality of the crystals . 249 X - ray crystallography has no upper or lower limit to the size of a biomolecule and once the biomolecule is crystallized , this technique can reveal atomic resolution ( 1 Å and lower ) structural details . However , X - ray crystallography relies on the formation of well - ordered 3D crystals and finding optimal conditions for crystallization is a real challenge , especially for mammalian integral membrane proteins or proteins with large flexible loops and domains . Additionally , cytoskeletal filamentous proteins are resistant to crystallization . Recent technical advancements in the field of cryo - EM have sparked a resolution revolution . Cryo - EM has emerged as a technique to solve structures of non - crystallizable biomolecules at near atomic resolution , especially macromolecular assemblies and heterocomplexes . 250 This technique , unlike crystallography , can be used for structure 50 determination of a wide range of specimens such as single protein molecules , multiprotein complexes , thin protein crystals , viruses , helical filamentous complexes , bacterial cells and thin tissue sections . 251 Cryo - EM takes advantage of high energy electrons to illuminate very thin specimens in a transmission electron microscope . Since electrons interact with the Coulomb potential of the individual atoms within the sample , a magnified image of the sample that contains structural features of the macromolecule is obtained . Single particle reconstruction is a cryo - EM technique used to determine structures of non - crystalline biomolecules by computationally analyzing images of thousands of particles embedded in vitreous ice . Vitreous ice preserves macromolecules in their near native conformation and reduces dehydration and radiation damage in the vacuum of the electron microscope . 252 , 253 Particle image data sets which are a 2D projection of individual molecules are aligned and grouped into homogenous classes based on their similarity . All the image data sets within a class are superposed and averaged . The averaged images are oriented relative to one another to generate a 3D reconstruction of a Coulomb potential density map . 254 , 255 The final structure is obtained by docking X - ray crystal structures of the subcomponents of the molecule or its homologues into the EM maps . 256 – 258 The structure of the 10 - mer yeast exosome complex was solved by docking homologous atomic models of the nine subunit core complex and bacterial RNase III solved by X - ray crystallography into an 18 Å cryo - EM map . 259 Like X - ray maps , high resolution EM maps can be analyzed by de novo backbone tracing . However , with low resolution EM maps , docking X - ray segments can provide a structure , but fitting should be interpreted with caution as there could be more than one possible location for a given segment . Nevertheless , these low resolution structures do provide some information which can be a stepping stone to a higher resolution . 260 51 Once considered as ‘blobology’ , in the past few years single particle cryo - EM has revealed near atomic resolution structures of macromolecules . This resolution transformation was triggered by the development of direct electron detection ( DED ) camera technology and increasing computer power to run sophisticated image analysis algorithms . 261 Moreover , two perceived barriers for cryo - EM of crossing an atomic resolution of 2 Å and solving structures of proteins with a MW < 100 kDa were overcome as exemplified by the structure of lactate dehydrogenase ( 145 kDa ) at 2 . 8 Å , glutamate dehydrogenase ( 334 kDa ) at 1 . 8 Å , isocitrate dehydrogenase ( 93 kDa ) at 3 . 8 Å and β - galactosidase ( 463 kDa ) at ~ 1 . 5 Å . 262 , 263 As opposed to X - ray crystallography , which requires a large amount of homogenous material and in some cases rigorous molecular engineering , cryo - EM can be performed with a small sample of biomolecules in their near - native form . Since single particle cryo - EM involves computational alignment of several images of an individual biomolecule in identical conformations and computational image analysis can deal with a certain extent of conformational and compositional heterogeneity , absolute homogeneity of a sample is not a necessity . 255 In addition , cryo - EM can be performed with the buffer that is optimal for the biological function of the specimen , thus revealing structures that are closer - to - the native state . Above all , unlike crystallography , which may or may not yield diffracting crystals , cryo - EM provides information even at a modest resolution which can be improved with biological insights . In the case of crystallography , the existence of a biomolecule in several conformational states interferes with the formation of high - quality crystals . On the other hand , in single particle cryo - EM , if the particles have distinct conformational states that can be identified and computationally assigned , then intermediates and various functional states of a biomolecule can be identified . If the 52 conformational differences are computationally unidentifiable , the averaging of images for structure determination can lead to blurring of structural features . 256 Although the cryo - EM approach is becoming popular , it is not a turn - key approach because data acquisition , image acquisition , and image processing are complex and require significant financial investment . In addition , there is no simple objective quality criterion to assess the accuracy of the density map determined , unlike the R - free value used in X - ray crystallography . 260 Undoubtedly , X - ray crystallography dominates the field of structural biology because of its mature methodology , ability to provide high resolution , ease of accessibility world - wide and large number of experienced users ; however , recent technical advances in cryo - EM techniques have ushered in a resolution revolution for generating structures of non - crystallizable macromolecules . Both techniques with their advantages and caveats can be used in combination to decipher the structure of biomolecules and the mechanisms associated with their function . In addition , since cryo - EM images and crystals of macromolecules are produced under different biochemical conditions , the corresponding solved structures could present different biologically relevant states , thus yielding more elaborate structural information about the biomolecule . Given that X - crystallography reveals structural information at an atomic resolution and with cryo - EM approaching near atomic resolution structural determination for non - crystallizable macromolecules and filamentous systems , these techniques together have immense potential to generate thorough structural information on biomolecules that can be extended into disease management and drug discovery . 53 1 . 4 . 2 F - actin Structure : A Revolution in Resolution Filamentous systems , such as actin , do not pack into crystals and thus eliminate the potential use of X - ray crystallography for structural determination . Therefore , the first model of F - actin was obtained in 1990 by fitting the X - ray crystal structure of monomeric actin into X - ray fiber diffraction data from aligned actin filaments ( Figure 1 . 8 ) . 51 , 52 The orientation of the actin monomers within the filament was confirmed later that year by cryo - EM at a resolution of 25 - 30 Å . 264 It was almost 20 years later in 2009 that high resolution fibre diffraction data ( 3 . 3 – 5 . 6 Å ) revealed the structural changes that occur during incorporation of an actin monomer into the actin filament and the ordering of the D - loop which is normally disordered in G - actin . 51 , 63 , 265 These features were confirmed in 2010 by cryo - EM of an F - actin structure produced at 6 . 6 Å using a transmission electron microscope fitted with charge coupled device ( CCD ) camera . The secondary structures such as α - helices , β - sheets , and loops were unambiguously modelled into the electron density map . 54 In 2015 , a significant improvement in resolution occurred with the development of direct electron detectors . The structure of F - actin bound to tropomyosin with some identifiable side chains was obtained at a resolution of 3 . 7 Å . 4 Further improvement in the data processing in 2016 yielded a 3 . 6 Å resolution structure of the F - actin - myosin - tropomyosin complex . 266 Continuous advances in the field of cryo - EM have yielded near atomic structures ; a few recent structures include myosin bound to F - actin in the ADP and rigor states at 3 . 3 Å and 3 . 9 Å , respectively , and a 3 . 8 Å resolution structure of cofilin bound to F - actin . 7 , 8 Although , cryo - EM is continuously advancing and generating structures of helical polymers , the structural determination of filaments by cryo - EM still relies to a great extent on fitting available crystal structures into the EM maps . For example , the initial model of cofilin bound F - actin was prepared by fitting crystal structures 54 of G - actin ( PDB : 1J6Z ) and chicken cofilin ( PDB : 1TVJ ) . Similarly , the model of actomyosin and tropomyosin was obtained using the crystal structures of rigor - like NM - 2B ( PDB : 4PD3 ) for myosin and the tropomyosin structure ( PDB : 4A7F ) . However , with continuous improvements in imaging and data processing technology , cryo - EM is emerging as the most practical method for high resolution structural determination of helical polymers . 1 . 4 . 3 Chronological Overview of My Research F - actin is one of the major components of cytoskeleton and muscle contractile machinery . Although the crystal structure of monomeric actin was solved in 1990 , information on some molecular interactions within F - actin and with ABPs were available only at low resolutions of 6 . 6 and 10 Å until 2015 . 51 , 54 , 55 Several crystallizable short F - actin oligomers ( SFAO ) were produced by chemical modifications for crystallization . Although some interactions between the actin subunits within SFAO were preserved , chemical modifications distorted some interfaces . 72 , 73 , 103 Thus , a strategically balanced chemical modification approach that retains F - actin like interactions within a SFAO was required . In 2010 , the application of such an approach in the Dawson lab resulted in the generation of a short F - actin oligomer called the ADPr - trimer . This trimer exhibited some F - actin like properties and thus had the potential to act as a scaffold to bind F - ABPs for structural insights . X - ray crystallography being the mainstay technique for structural determination , my graduate research began in the summer of 2015 with the goal of generating heterocomplexes of ADPr - trimer with F - ABPs for crystal trials . That same year , with the availability of direct electron detectors in the field of cryo - EM , the first near atomic resolution structure of F - actin in complex with tropomyosin was published by Von Der Ecken et al . 267 Since then , several other near atomic resolution cryo - EM structures of F - actin itself and in complex with ABPs have been published ( Supplementary Table 1 . 2 ) . My 55 Figure 1 . 8 Timeline showing improvement in the resolution of cryo - EM structures of F - actin itself and in complex with ABPs . Until the second decade of the 21 st century , cryo - EM F - actin structures were produced from imaging samples with transmission electron microscopes fitted with charge coupled devices ( CCD ) . The introduction of direct electron devices ( DED ) revolutionized the field and allowed generation of structures of filamentous protein at near atomic resolution . The first F - actin structure using DED was produced at 4 . 7 Å . Since then , improvements in data processing and resolution have provided structural insights into interaction within and with the actin filament . 56 research began with establishing if the F - ABPs myosin , gelsolin or cofilin bound to ADPr - trimer . Myosin and gelsolin were available in our lab , while cofilin was produced in collaboration with SignalChem Biotech Inc . , Richmond , BC . The findings from these three ABPs are described in Chapter 2 . Among the three F - ABPs , gelsolin yielded a complex with ADP - trimer which was purified for setting - up crystal trials in collaboration with the Kimber laboratory , University of Guelph . Unfortunately , the complex failed to yield crystals . With no high - resolution structure of gelsolin bound F - actin available , in 2017 I explored cryo - EM for structural determination . In collaboration with the Khursigara laboratory , I determined a pipeline for cryo - EM based structural work at Guelph . The stability and homogeneity of the gelsolin bound ADPr - trimer complex for future cryo - EM , was determined by analysing negatively stained images of the complex generated on an FEI Tecnai G2 F20 microscope at the Molecular and Cellular Imaging Facility , University of Guelph . Approximately 600 negatively stained EM micrographs were collected and analyzed using EMAN2 . With the preliminary structural data from negative stained micrographs , a collaboration will be established with the Rubinstein laboratory at the University of Toronto for structural determination using cryo - EM . Thus , my graduate work not only characterized interactions of selected F - ABPs with ADPr - trimer , but also laid a foundation for incorporating advances in the field of cryo - EM for structural determination . Additionally , my research also included advances in mass spectrometry - based proteomics . Rather than using individual F - ABPs , mass spectrometry was used to identify F - ABPs retained on affinity resins in pull - down assays from zebrafish embryo cell lysates and the interactions of identified F - ABPs were validated biochemically . Findings from mass spectrometry and validation of MLC6B as an identified ADPr - trimer binding partner are included in Chapter 3 . 57 2 CHARACTERIZATION OF ADPR - TRIMER – F - ABP INTERACTIONS 2 . 1 Overview F - ABPs purified in - house or commercially available were screened for interactions with ADPr - trimer using physical and biochemical assays . The three F - ABPs examined were myosin S1  , cofilin and gelsolin of which the first two are side - binding and the last is barbed end - binding . ADPr - trimer did not interact with or activate myosin S1 . Neither remodeling of ADPr - trimer with gelsolin , nor alternative means of inhibiting polymerization of PBM - crosslinked F - actin - derived trimers rescued myosin binding . Gelsolin bound to ADPr - trimer and the resulting complex ( GSFL : 3mr ) was purified for structural determination ; however , the complex failed to crystallize . Thus , an EM approach was undertaken to gain structural insights . Analysis of negative stained EM images suggested the presence of heterogenous species of the GSFL : 3mr complex in the sample . Cofilin also bound to ADPr - trimer ; however , cofilin binding overcame polymerization inhibition resulting in filament formation . Consequently , cofilin binding yielded a non - crystallizable complex . Considering that a large number of ABPs exist , application of the candidate approach is limited only to purified F - ABPs ; however , purified proteins yield clear results in physical and biochemical assays . Upon confirmation of an interaction , complexes can be readily purified for structural studies .  Myosin S1 work included in this chapter has been published . Sidhu , N . and Dawson , J . A crosslinked and ribosylated actin trimer does not interact productively with myosin . Biochem . Cell Biol . 97 , 140 - 147 ( 2018 ) . 58 2 . 2 Myosin S1 is an ADPr - trimer non - interacting F - actin binding protein 2 . 2 . 1 Background ADPr - trimer possessing both F - actin - like longitudinal ( intrastrand ) and lateral ( interstrand ) interfaces bound DNase I at the pointed end or gelsolin at the barbed end . 11 I extended these studies to determine the interaction of ADPr - trimer with the side - binding and force - generating protein myosin S1 . Since F - actin cannot be crystallized , the molecular details of binding interactions between F - actin and myosin have most recently come from cryo - EM . 5 – 7 , 125 , 127 , 266 Although cryo - EM structures reveal near atomic details , the current resolution for routinely solved structures is not sufficient to differentiate amino acids with small side chains or reveal small molecules in complexes such as water molecules and other small ligands . 10 , 245 , 262 Thus , production of a crystallizable complex of ADPr - trimer with myosin S1 is valuable for an atomic resolution understanding of the actomyosin binding interface during force generation and movement . Moreover , this knowledge can be applied to studying mutations in actin and myosin that lead to diseases . 2 . 2 . 2 Experimental Procedures 2 . 2 . 2a Reagents Reagents were purchased from either Sigma - Aldrich ( ST . Louis , MO ) or Fischer Scientific ( Mississauga , ON ) . Chromatographic columns were obtained by GE Healthcare ( Piscataway , NJ ) . Protein purification was performed on AKTA pure FPLC system . Membrane filters for protein concentration were procured from Millipore ( Billerica , MA ) . SDS - PAGE gels were made using a 29 : 1 bisacrylamide which was obtained from Bio - Rad ( Hercules , CA ) . 59 2 . 2 . 2b Protein Preparation 2 . 2 . 2b ( i ) Preparation of Actin Actin was extracted from ground turkey breast ( muscle ) as described by Spudich and Watt 1971 . 268 The actin concentration was measured either from absorbance at 290 nm using an extinction coefficient of 26 , 040 M - 1 cm - 1 or Bradford colorimetric assay using Bio - Rad Protein Assay dye reagent concentrate ( Hercules , CA ) . Actin purified in G - buffer was flash frozen in N 2 ( l ) and stored at - 80℃ . 2 . 2 . 2b ( ii ) Preparation of ADPr - trimer ADPr - trimer was prepared from α - skeletal actin extracted from turkey following the method described by Perieteanu et al . ( 2010 ) with slight a modification . 11 , 268 The actin extraction from the acetone powder in G - buffer without β - ME was followed by polymerization and crosslinking with subsequent paracrystallization step . Chemical crosslinking of the extracted turkey actin was initiated by adjusting the solution to a final concentration of 10 mM sodium tetraborate pH 9 . 0 and a 1 . 5 - fold molar excess of a 25 mM stock solution of pPBM ( Aldrich Chemical Company P2 , 398 - 9 ) dissolved in dimethylformamide ( DMF ) . The reaction was terminated after 30 min by the addition of 160 - fold molar excess of β - ME relative to pPBM . The crosslinking step was followed by the addition of 100 mM MgCl 2 to form large paracrystals that can be harvested at 16 , 000 rpm ( 38 , 400 x g ) using larger - volume bottles in a JLA 16 . 250 rotor ( Beckman ) . The resulting pellet was resuspended and dialysed extensively against G - buffer for five to six days with at least eight exchanges of G - buffer . Any remaining F - actin was removed by centrifugation at 167 , 424 x g for 75 min . The resulting depolymerized crosslinked actin oligomers in the supernatant were rendered non - polymerizable by ribosylating Arg - 177 using an enzyme , Photox ( described below ) . The solution was raised to a 60 final concentration of 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 . The Photox reaction was initiated by the addition of 20 to 200 nM ( 1 % v / v ) of Photox and 5 - fold molar excess of β - NAD ( Sigma Aldrich , N1511 ) . The reaction was carried out overnight at 4℃ . 11 Polymerizable oligomers were removed by addition of polymerization salts ( 50 mM KCl , 2 mM MgCl 2 and 2 mM ATP ) with subsequent centrifugation at 167 , 424 x g for 75 min . The resulting supernatant was concentrated and applied to a Superdex 200 ( 26 / 600 ) column pre - equilibrated with Super - G buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 2 mM CaCl 2 , 0 . 25 mM PMSF ( phenylmethylsulfonyl fluoride ) , 0 . 2 mM NaN 3 , 50 mM NaCl , 0 . 2 mM β - ME ) . Elution fractions containing ADPr - trimer and ADPr - dimer were pooled ; ADPr - trimer was resolved by iterative purifications on the S200 column . Although the process is labour intensive , I obtained pure ADPr - trimer at a yield of 1 - 2 % of the starting actin . The concentration of ADPr - trimer was determined using Bio - Rad Protein Assay dye reagent ( Hercules , CA ) . Purified ADPr - trimer was flash frozen in liquid N 2 and stored at - 80℃ ( Figure 2 . 1 ) . 2 . 2 . 2b ( iii ) Preparation of Photox Photox was purified as described by Visschedyk et al . 99 Photox with an N - terminal His 6 - tag was expressed from glycerol stocks of E . coli Rosetta competent cells . Purification was performed by solubilization of Photox in GdnHCl ( guanidine hydrochloride ) followed by metal affinity chromatography . Protein was renatured on the affinity column by excluding the GdnHCl from the elution buffers . The purified Photox was dialysed against binding buffer ( 20 mM Tris , pH 7 , 50 mM NaCl ) and concentrated to 0 . 2 – 1 mg / mL . The protein was flash frozen in liquid N 2 and stored at - 80℃ . Photox concentrations were determined from absorbance at 280 nm using an extinction coefficient of 30 , 820 M - 1 cm - 1 . 99 Photox activity was confirmed by adding 5 to 10 fold - 61 Figure 2 . 1 Purification of ADPr - trimer . A ) Coomassie stained 8 % SDS - PAGE . Supernatant containing crosslinked and ribosylated F - actin oligomers were resolved on a Superdex 200 ( 26 / 600 ) gel filtration column . Elution fractions containing ADPr - trimer and dimer were pooled and pure ADPr - trimer was obtained by iterations of gel filtration columns . Fractions F1 to G5 show ADPr - trimer band just above MW marker 180 kDa . These fractions were pooled and stored at - 80℃ . B ) Chromatogram corresponding to the elution profile of ADPr - trimer fractions on SDS - PAGE shown in A . ADPr - trimer containing elution fractions F1 to G3 in ( A ) correspond to elution volume ranging from 156 ml to 170 ml . A B 62 molar excess of etheno - NAD + ( Sigma Aldrich N2630 ) to G - actin and measuring fluorescence change with a CARY Eclipse Fluorescence Spectrophotometer ( Varian , Mississauga , ON ) at an excitation wavelength of 305 nm and an emission wavelength of 405 nm ( Figure 2 . 2 ) . 2 . 2 . 2b ( iv ) Preparation of Myosin S1 Myosin S1 was prepared by papain digestion of full - length myosin ( FL myosin ) . FL myosin was extracted from rabbit soleus muscle from freshly - killed New Zealand rabbits obtained from Abate Rabbit Packers ( Arthur , ON ) . 116 FL myosin was dialysed overnight against Solution A ( 200 mM ammonium acetate , pH 7 . 2 , 2 mM EDTA ( ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid ) . Dialyzed myosin was diluted to 10 mg / mL , incubated at RT for 60 min and digested with 0 . 03 mg / mL of papain at RT for 8 min . The reaction was stopped by the addition of 1 mM iodoacetic acid and spun at 213 , 102 x g for 15 min . The supernatant containing soluble myosin S1 was dialysed into the starting buffer ( 50 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 1 mM DTT ( dithiothreitol ) , 2 mM EDTA ) and further purified on a HiTrap DEAE 5 mL column ( GE Healthcare , Piscataway , NJ ) equilibrated in the starting buffer . Myosin S1 was eluted with a linear gradient of 0 to 0 . 5 M KCl in the starting buffer . The elution fractions were pooled , stabilized with 3 mg sucrose / mL of myosin S1 , flash frozen and stored at - 80℃ . Protein concentrations were determined using absorbance at 280 nm and the extinction coefficient of 0 . 72 mg mL - 1 cm - 1 . The ability of myosin S1 to bind and release from F - actin was tested with a deadheading experiment in which active myosin S1 is released from F - actin upon the addition of ATP , while inactive myosin S1 remains bound ( Figure 2 . 3 ) . 2 . 2 . 2b ( v ) Preparation of Full - length Gelsolin Full - length gelsolin ( GSFL ) was expressed and purified as described by Morrison and Dawson 2007 . 58 E coli cells expressing GSFL were lysed in lysis buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 1 mM EDTA , 1 mM β - ME , 1 mM benzamidine , and 0 . 5 mM PMSF ) using a French press at 16 , 000 63 psi . The resulting lysate was clarified by centrifugation at 31 , 360 x g for 30 min . The supernatant was developed on an 80 mL Affi - Gel Blue column ( Bio - Rad , Hercules , CA ) pre - equilibrated with TE buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 1 mM EDTA ) using a linear gradient to 1 M NaCl in TE buffer . GSFL - containing fractions were pooled and dialysed overnight against TE buffer containing 1 mM β - ME . Dialysed GSFL was applied to an 8 mL Mono Q 10 / 10 column ( GE Healthcare , Piscataway , NJ ) and eluted with a linear gradient to 1 M NaCl in TE buffer . The fractions containing GSFL were pooled and dialysed against TE buffer with 1 mM β - ME and stored at - 80℃ after flash freezing in liquid N 2 . Protein concentrations were determined by measuring absorbance at 280 and using the extinction coefficient of 1 . 4 mg mL - 1 cm - 1 ( Figure 2 . 4 ) . 2 . 2 . 2b ( vi ) Preparation of Gelsolin bound ADPr - trimer Gelsolin - bound ADPr - trimer ( GSFL : 3mr ) was produced by incubating GSFL dialysed in G - buffer ( 2 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 0 . 2 mM CaCl 2 , 0 . 2 mM ATP , 0 . 2 mM β - ME ) with ADPr - trimer in a 1 . 4 molar ratio for 2 hours on ice . The resulting reaction mixture was developed on a Superdex - 200 ( 10 / 300 ) column preequilibrated in Super G - buffer . The elution fractions were run on a native gel with GSFL or ADPr - trimer alone as controls . The fractions corresponding to GSFL : 3mr complex were pooled , stored at 4℃ and used within 1 - 2 days of preparation ( Figure 2 . 5 ) . 2 . 2 . 2b ( vii ) Purification of DNase I DNase I purchased from Worthington Biochemical Corporation ( Lakewood , NJ ) was further purified on Superdex 200 ( 26 / 600 ) in Super G - buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 0 . 2 mM CaCl 2 , 50 mM NaCl , 0 . 2 mM ATP , 0 . 2 mM β - ME ) . Purified DNase I was dialysed against G - buffer , flash frozen in N 2 ( l ) and stored at - 80℃ . 64 Figure 2 . 2 10 % SDS - PAGE gel of purification of Photox . Elution profile of the clarified lysate ( Load ) from denatured inclusion bodies loaded onto a chelating Sepharose column charged with zinc . The column was washed and eluted in step gradient with buffers containing 5 mM imidazole ( Wash BB ) , 20 mM imidazole wash , 40 mM imidazole and 100 mM Imidazole ( Elution buffer ) . Wash fractions with 20 , 40 and 100 mM imidazole in the buffer contained Photox ( 46 kDa ) . Fractions with Photox were pooled , concentrated and stored at - 80℃ . The activity of Photox was confirmed by adding etheno - NAD + to G - actin and measuring change in fluorescence on CARY Eclipse Fluorescence Spectrophotometer ( data not shown ) . 65 Figure 2 . 3 Purification of myosin S1 . A band shift in the elution fractions indicated formation of GSFL : 3mr complex . GSFL alone and ADPr - trimer alone were run as controls . 68 2 . 2 . 2b ( viii ) Preparation of D : trimer Since the DNase I - binding loop of actin participates in intrastrand interactions between F - actin subunits , only the pointed end subunits are available to DNase I - binding . To prepare DNase I - capped pPBM - crosslinked trimer , F - actin was crosslinked with pPBM under conditions described previously for the production of ADPr - trimer . 11 Crosslinked actin was pelleted by centrifugation at 392 , 000 x g for 20 min . The pelleted F - actin was resuspended in F - buffer ( 25 mM Tris - HCl , pH 8 . 0 , 50 mM KCl , 2 mM MgCl 2 , 1 mM EGTA , 0 . 1 mM ATP , 1 mM β - ME ) . Resuspended F - actin was then incubated with DNase I ( Worthington ) at a 1 : 1 actin subunit : DNase I molecular ratio overnight at 4℃ . The next day the reaction was centrifuged again at 392 , 000 x g for 20 min to remove any filamentous actin . The resulting supernatant was concentrated and resolved on a Superdex S200 ( 10 / 300 ) column in Super G - buffer . The elution fractions were run on native - and SDS - PAGE to identify fractions with pure D : trimer . Protein concentrations were determined by Bradford colorimetric assay and the elution fractions were flash frozen in liquid N 2 and stored at - 80℃ ( Figure 2 . 6 ) . 2 . 2 . 2c Physical Assays 2 . 2 . 2c ( i ) Polyacrylamide gels SDS - PAGE comprised of 8 or 10 % polyacrylamide resolving gel and 5 % polyacrylamide stacking gel . Protein samples were prepared with 2x Laemmli buffer ( 50 mM Tris , pH 6 . 8 , 2 % SDS , 10 % glycerol , 1 . 3 M β - ME and 0 . 1 % bromophenol blue ) and run with 1x running buffer ( 25 mM Tris , 250 mM glycine , and 0 . 1 % SDS ) at 180 V . 269 Protein bands on the gel were visualized with Coomassie brilliant blue dye R - 250 ( Sigma Aldrich , Oakville , ON ) or silver staining ( Thermo Scientific Pierce Product # 24612 ) . 69 Figure 2 . 6 Purification of DNase I - bound pPBM - trimer ( D : trimer ) . A ) Chromatogram of a sample of crosslinked F - actin incubated with DNase I in a 1 : 1 molecular ratio developed on a Superdex 200 ( 10 / 300 ) column . The identity of DNase I bound actin oligomers is indicated on the chromatogram . A B C 70 2 . 2 . 2c ( ii ) Native - PAGE Native - PAGE was performed with non - denaturing acrylamide gels comprised of 8 % resolving and 5 % stacking gel supplemented with 0 . 2 mM CaCl 2 . S1 binding with ADPr - trimer on native gels was performed with reactions containing 2 μM of ADPr - monomer , ADPr - dimer , or ADPr - trimer incubated for 20 min on ice in the presence of 0 . 87 μM myosin S1 in Super G - buffer containing 60 μg / mL each of antipain , leupeptin , TLCK ( tosyl - L - lysyl - chloromethane hydrochloride ) , and TPCK ( tosyl phenylalanyl chloromethyl ketone ) protease inhibitors . Likewise , GSFL : 3mr and myosin S1 reactions containing 0 . 23 μM of ADPr - monomer , or GSFL : 3mr complex were incubated for 15 min on ice in the presence of 0 . 20 μM myosin S1 in Super G - buffer with 24 μg / mL each of antipain , leupeptin , TLCK , and TPCK protease inhibitors . D : trimer and myosin S1 binding reactions for native - PAGE contained 0 . 42 μM of DNase I - capped actin dimer or trimer in the presence or absence of 0 . 37 μM myosin S1 . 33 μg / mL antipain , leupeptin , TLCK and TPCK protease inhibitors were added to the reactions . DNase I alone was also run as a control to identify the band and rule out an interaction of myosin S1 with DNase I . Native gels were run at a low voltage ( < 60 V ) on ice and visualized with either Coomassie Brilliant Blue R - 250 ( Sigma Aldrich ) or Silver Staining kit ( Pierce TM Silver Stain Kit ) . 2 . 2 . 2c ( iii ) Analytical Size - Exclusion Chromatography Analytical size - exclusion chromatography was performed on a Superdex 200 ( 10 / 300 ) . analytical chromatography column equilibrated in Super G - buffer with protease inhibitors . ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 reactions contained 2 μM ADPr - trimer and 0 . 87 μM myosin S1 or 2 μM ADPr - trimer in Super G - buffer with TLCK , TPCK , leupeptin and antipain at a final concentration of 0 . 60 μg / mL incubated for 60 min at RT ( room temperature ) . 71 For GSFL : 3mr and myosin S1 reactions , mixtures containing 0 . 9 μmol GSFL : 3mr and 0 . 8 μmol myosin S1 were analyzed . Elution fractions were run on native - and SDS - PAGE . The bands were visualized with Silver stain ( Pierce TM Silver Stain Kit ) . 2 . 2 . 2c ( iv ) Dynamic Light Scattering ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 were filtered through a Millipore 0 . 22 μM filter ( Billerica , MA ) . Molar concentrations were adjusted using filtered Super G - buffer . Hydrodynamic radii measurements of samples containing 4 μM ADPr - trimer ( side - binding sites ) and 1 . 5 μM myosin S1 were performed on a Nano S Zetasizer ( Malvern , U . K . ) equipped with a 633 nm red laser and a 173˚ backscatter detector . Apparent Stokes radii of the samples were determined by a normal distribution fit of volume distribution measurements . 2 . 2 . 2d Biochemical Assays 2 . 2 . 2d ( i ) Myosin ATPase Assay The myosin ATPase assay is a colorimetric assay that measures the ATPase activity of myosin in the presence of actin . The assay is based on the production of a blue by - product released by the reaction between Pi ( inorganic phosphate ) and molybdate and was modified from Trybus ( 2000 ) for a 96 - well format as described in Liu et al . ( 2017 ) . 270 Single concentration assays with 1 . 5 μM actin on a per - subunit basis for ADPr - trimer in the presence of 0 . 125 μM myosin were performed in triplicate with released Pi measured at 10 minute time intervals . The average ATPase activity was plotted using Prism 7 . 0c software ( GraphPad , LaJolla , California ) . F - actin was run as a positive control and ADPr - monomer and dimer , which do not possess a putative myosin binding site , were run as negative controls . Myosin basal activity was determined by running myosin alone and was used to baseline Pi released measured in all the reactions . For generating F - actin , purified turkey actin was mixed in a 1000 : 1 molar ratio with gelsolin and incubated at RT for 10 min to 72 control filament length / viscosity . Polymerization was induced by addition of 10x Assay Buffer ( 750 mM KCl , 100 mM imidazole , pH 7 , 10 mM DTT , 10 mM EGTA , 10 mM MgCl 2 , and 10 mM NaN 3 ) and the reaction was incubated at RT for 30 min . Working samples were made by diluting polymerized stock with 1x Assay Buffer and Mg - ATP mix . A 2x myosin working solution was prepared in 1x Assay Buffer . Reactions were initiated by addition of myosin to F - actin and test samples . The reactions were stopped at 10 min time intervals for 30 min by transferring 45 μL of reaction to wells containing 45 μL of stop solution ( 60 mM EDTA , pH 6 . 5 , 6 . 6 % SDS ) . 200 μL of colour developing reagent ( 0 . 5 % ferrous sulfate , 25 % of 2 % ammonium molybdate in 4 N H 2 SO 4 ) was added to the stopped reaction wells to visualize Pi production . Pi reacts with molybdate to produce blue by - product that is measured at 750 nm for quantification . Phosphate standards ranging from 0 . 05 mM to 2 mM potassium dihydrogen phosphate were used to generate a standard curve for each assay . ATPase activity of myosin in presence of GSFL : 3mr and D : trimer interaction was measured as described above for ADPr - trimer . However , due to low yield of GSFL : 3mr , the assays were performed with a single concentration of 1 . 5 μM actin on a subunit basis with released Pi measured at 40 and 60 mins for GSFL : 3mr and 20 , 40 and 60 mins for D : trimer . 2 . 2 . 3 Results 2 . 2 . 3a Myosin does not bind ADPr - trimer under rigor conditions Since myosin binds to two adjacent actin subunits present in one strand of F - actin and ADPr - trimer presents one such site , I investigated the binding of myosin S1 to ADPr - trimer under rigor conditions . 7 , 127 Unfortunately , no evidence of interaction was found . The binding of myosin S1 to ADPr - trimer was investigated using physical assays which included dynamic light scattering ( DLS ) , native - PAGE and analytical size - exclusion chromatography , and the biochemical myosin 73 ATPase assay . DLS measurements indicated no significant increase in the hydrodynamic radius of the mixture of ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 compared to controls , ADPr - trimer or myosin S1 alone . The hydrodynamic radii were 4 . 33 ± 0 . 19 nm for ADPr - trimer alone ; 4 . 34 ± 0 . 28 nm for myosin S1 alone ; and 4 . 62 nm ± 0 . 06 for the ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 reaction ( Figure 2 . 7 ) . With native - PAGE , no shift was observed in the band for the reaction mixture containing ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 . ADPr - monomer and ADPr - dimer have no putative myosin binding sites and were therefore run as negative controls ( Figure 2 . 8A ) . Since myosin S1 alone was not observed on the native gels , myosin S1 might be found in the ADPr - trimer band present on the gel . Mass spectrometric analysis on the ADPr - trimer - containing bands from the native - PAGE revealed the presence of only actin peptides , but no myosin peptides . Myosin S1 bands tend to run as a smear on the native gel making it difficult to visualize diffuse signals with 0 . 95 μg of myosin S1 present in the reactions using Coomassie stain . Therefore , 6 . 1 μg of myosin S1 was loaded as a standard on the gel . In addition , all the samples were run on SDS - PAGE to confirm the presence of myosin S1 in all the reactions ( Figure 2 . 8B ) . Analytical gel filtration chromatography was performed with a mixture of ADPr - trimer and S1 , and ADPr - trimer alone . The reaction mix containing ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 eluted at a volume similar to the elution volume for ADPr - trimer alone ( Figure 2 . 9A ) . The elution fractions from the chromatographic column run on SDS - PAGE indicted that the peaks of myosin S1 and ADPr - trimer appear in different fractions suggesting no binding ( Figure 2 . 9B ) . To further confirm that myosin S1 does not bind ADPr - trimer , I performed biochemical myosin ATPase assays with F - actin as substrate as a positive control , and ADPr - monomer and dimer as negative controls . Myosin ATPase activity in the presence of ADPr - trimer was significantly lower than that in the presence of F - actin and comparable to the negative controls ( Figure 2 . 8C ) . 74 Figure 2 . 7 Dynamic Light Scattering measurement of ADPr - trimer and myosin S1 . The hydrodynamic radii of various reactions containing ADPr - trimer ( 4 μM trimer = side binding sites ) and myosin S1 ( 1 . 5 μM ) were measured using a Nano S Zetasizer . The value of radii measured for various reactions were : ( A ) ADPr - trimer alone , 4 . 33 nm ± 0 . 19 ; ( B ) S1 alone , 4 . 34 nm ± 0 . 28 ; and ( C ) ADPr - trimer and S1 , 4 . 62 nm ± 0 . 06 . Compared to ADPr - trimer alone , no significant increase in the radii seen in the reaction with ADPr - trimer and S1 . B ) SDS - PAGE of the samples in A above run on SDS - PAGE to show the presence of myosin S1 in all reactions . C ) The ATPase activity of 0 . 125 mg / mL of myosin in the presence of 5 μM F - actin or purified ADPr - actin oligomers . F - actin was run as a positive control and ADPr - monomer and dimer were run as negative controls . The average activity for triplicate measurements is plotted ±standard error . The ADPr - actin - containing complex activities were significantly different from that in the presence of F - actin ( p values : ADPr - monomer , 0 . 003 ; ADPr - dimer , 0 . 005 ; ADPr - trimer , 0 . 001 ) . ADPr - trimer did not activate myosin ATPase activity beyond that of ADPr - monomer ( p = 0 . 679 ) . A B 77 2 . 2 . 3b Remodeling by gelsolin does not rescue myosin binding 2 . 2 . 3b ( i ) Background The stoichiometry of gelsolin to ADPr - trimer is 1 : 1 in the GSFL : 3mr heterocomplex . While ADPr - trimer alone does not nucleate actin polymerization , GSFL : 3mr acts as a filament nucleator . Given this enabling of nucleating abilities of ADPr - trimer , I tested the hypothesis that gelsolin remodels ADPr - trimer to an F - actin - like structure that permits S1 binding . 2 . 2 . 3b ( ii ) Myosin does not bind Gelsolin bound ADPr - trimer under rigor conditions My results suggest no significant interactions between GSFL : 3mr and myosin S1 . For native gel reactions , no significant shift was observed in the band mobility of reactions with GSFL : 3mr and myosin S1 . Myosin S1 alone , ADPr - monomer alone and ADPr - trimer alone were run as controls on the native gel ( Figure 2 . 10A ) . Since GSFL : 3mr has Rf ( retention factor ) value similar to myosin S1 on a native gel , the reactions were run on SDS - PAGE to confirm the presence of all the reaction components . Some contaminating FL myosin is present in the S1 preparation ( Figure 2 . 10B ) . Chromatograms of a binding reaction containing GSFL : 3mr and myosin S1 indicated no shift in the elution peak compared to the elution peak of GSFL : 3mr alone . A major peak was observed at an elution volume of about 11 . 8 mL on the Superdex 200 10 / 300 column , along with a minor peak eluting at a volume of 15 mL . SDS - PAGE of fractions from the major peak showed the presence of GSFL and ADPr - trimer but no myosin S1 in these fractions . The myosin S1 band was seen in the loaded sample . Similarly , for the silver stained native gel , myosin S1 was present in the loaded sample but not in fractions from the major peak ( Figure 2 . 11 ) . Therefore , I conclude that remodeling of ADPr - trimer by GSFL does not restore myosin binding . 2 . 2 . 3c Alternative polymerization inhibition – D : trimer does not bind myosin 2 . 2 . 3c ( i ) Background Since ADPr - trimer did not bind myosin under rigor conditions , nor with remodeling by gelsolin , it is possible that ribosylation interferes with myosin binding . Therefore , an alternative method of inhibiting polymerization of crosslinked trimer was applied . DNase I is an actin monomer binding protein that forms a binary complex with monomeric actin and prevents formation of filaments . 271 Blanchoin et al . ( 1995 ) reported that DNase I does not block myosin S1 binding to actin , forming a ternary complex of DNase I - actin - myosin S1 . 272 Therefore , I generated a DNase I - capped pPBM - crosslinked actin trimer ( D : trimer ) and tested its binding to myosin S1 . 2 . 2 . 3c ( ii ) Myosin does not bind DNase I bound ADPr - trimer under rigor conditions No interaction between D : trimer and myosin S1 was observed on using native gel analysis or myosin ATPase assays . No new band appeared on native gels for the reactions with D : trimer and myosin S1 . D : trimer did not activate myosin ATPase activity beyond the negative control , D : dimer , and the ATPase activity was significantly lower than F - actin ( Figure 2 . 12 ) . 2 . 2 . 4 Discussion and Conclusion Previous biochemical and physical investigations indicated that ADPr - trimer mimics F - actin . It bound to ABPs such as DNase I at the pointed end and gelsolin at the barbed end . Here I extended this research by exploring whether ADPr - timer has an interface to bind the side - binding F - ABP myosin . My results suggest myosin did not bind ADPr - trimer , nor did it activate actin - 81 Figure 2 . 12 DNase I bound crosslinked actin trimer ( D : trimer ) interactions with myosin S1 . A ) Silver stained SDS - PAGE of binding reactions including 0 . 42 μM DNase I capped actin oligomers in the presence or absence of 0 . 37 μM myosin S1 . DNase I was also run alone to identify that band . No new bands were seen suggesting myosin S1 bound to the DNase I bound actin oligomers . B ) Myosin ATPase activity assays including 0 . 125 mg / mL myosin in the presence of 1 . 5 μM F - actin or DNase I bound crosslinked actin oligomers . No significant activity was observed for DNase I bound actin trimers . A B 82 activated myosin ATPase activity . Moreover , capping cross - linked actin trimer with DNase I to inhibit polymerization or remodeling of ADPr - trimer by gelsolin did not restore myosin binding . As indicated previously , pPBM crosslinking inhibits force generation but not myosin binding or myosin ATPase activity . 71 Therefore , crosslinking in the ADPr - trimer should not interfere with the binding of myosin . Likewise , in another study involving actin crosslinked with glutaraldehyde , which inserts inter - and intramolecular crosslinks through amino acids , myosin bound to crosslinked actin but interfered with the sliding movement . 273 Later in 2007 , Kozaku et al . indicated that the actin filament can exist in different conformational states , described as low and high - FRET conformations . F - actin can transition between these states either spontaneously or upon binding of ABPs . They suggested that crosslinking shifts actin to a lower a conformational state that allows myosin binding , but inhibits the myosin induced motility . 274 Given these points from the previous studies , crosslinks can be inserted into F - actin without interfering with its ability to bind myosin . Another modification that was introduced was ADP - ribosylation of each actin subunit in the ADPr - trimer . The ADP - ribosyl group is located at the intersubunit interaction site in F - actin ; consequently , the bulky group at the site likely interferes with the formation of the correct interface at the contact site involving three actin subunits . The ADP - ribosylated actin monomers can copolymerize with native actin and interact with ABPs including myosin . Therefore , the ADP - ribosyl group does not interfere with binding of myosin on monomeric actin . 275 Since gelsolin can remodel ADPr - trimer into a nucleating - competent structure , binding of GSFL : 3mr with myosin S1 was tested , but the gelsolin - bound ADPr - trimer did not bind myosin . Next , to rule out the possibility that the ADP - ribosyl group on each subunit of ADPr - trimer interferes with myosin binding , DNase I was used to inhibit polymerization of cross - linked F - actin derived trimer 83 ( D : trimer ) . D : trimer did not show any signs of binding to myosin . Why then does the ADPr - trimer not bind myosin ? An answer comes from a parallel research performed by another group in Germany . Qu et al . ( 2018 ) produced a pPBM - crosslinked oligomer similar to my ADPr - trimer . They produced heterologously inhibited pPBM - trimer ( hetADPr - trimer ) by purification of the pPBM - crosslinked trimer on a size - exclusion column followed by polymerization inhibition by substoichiometric ADP - ribosylation on Arg - 177 by iota toxin . Since the ADP - ribosylated crosslinked trimer could polymerize to some extent , complete inhibition of polymerization was achieved by incubating the ribosylated trimer with gelsolin segment - 1 ( G1 ) at an equimolar ratio to trimer . The resulting hetADPr - trimer bound skeletal myosin and activated myosin ATPase . The preliminary negative - stained EM model of hetADPr - trimer suggests myosin bound to the sides of the trimer along the two long pitch actin subunits . 104 The key difference between my ADPr - trimer and the hetADPr - trimer is the use of stoichiometric and substoichiometric strategies for polymerization inhibition . Previously generated G1 - bound pPBM trimer had distorted symmetry due to intercalation of G1 between the subunits . 72 Similarly , stochiometric ribosylation of ADPr - trimer subunits seems to distort the myosin binding interface . 11 , 72 However , use of a substoichiometric combination of ADP - ribosylation and G1 for polymerization inhibition resulted in heterogeneous trimer that not only binds to myosin , but also activates myosin ATPase activity . In conclusion , I believe my stringent polymerization inhibition strategy to obtain a homogenous short F - actin oligomer for crystal studies introduced distortions at the myosin binding surface . In contrast , the combination of two polymerization inhibition strategies generated a heterogenous trimer which bound myosin . 84 Collective data from the ADPr - trimer and hetADPr - trimer binding studies suggest that the presence of an ADP - ribosyl group at the inter subunit interaction site of the three subunits distorts the myosin binding site . Although myosin forms a ternary complex with the DNase I - bound actin monomer , binding of DNase I to the pointed end subunits of the crosslinked trimer may also cause conformational changes remodeling the myosin binding site . Conformational flexibility of actin is required for actin to function . 4 This flexible nature allows F - actin to act as molecular springs for force generation in conjunction with myosin . 6 Studies show that crosslinked actin filaments bind to myosin and activate ATPase activity , but their mobility is reduced . 71 , 276 F - actin exists in multiple structural states that may account for the selective binding of F - ABPs . 55 Alternatively , the binding of F - ABPs induce changes in the twist of the filament . Structural changes in F - actin upon myosin binding are proposed to play a role in actomyosin interactions . These conformational changes are not limited to the ABP binding site but are allosterically propagated to distant sites . 277 Cryo - EM studies of myosin bound to actin filaments during the rigor state have provided some insights into the binding surface . However , what remains unresolved is how the lever arm movement of myosin is coupled to the closure of the actin binding cleft and Pi release . This movement is central to chemo - mechanical force generation by actomyosin . 42 Additionally , the mechanism of the ADP - to - rigor state transition is not known . Cryo - EM reconstructions by Gurel et al . ( 2017 ) of the ADP - bound and rigor states give some idea of sequence of events from ATP binding and hydrolysis steps to force generation . 6 Structural changes at the myosin binding interface propagated across the lateral interface between subunits suggest cooperative myosin binding to F - actin . 128 Allosteric regulation of actin filaments by cooperative conformational changes upon binding of ABPs regulate binding in a 85 mutually exclusive manner . 278 , 279 Despite the bulk of research supporting cooperativity , Qu et al . ( 2018 ) showed that an actin trimer with one myosin binding site is the smallest F - actin scaffold required to bind myosin and activate myosin ATPase activity . Self - assembly of actin into filaments and the interactions between subunits is biologically important for actin to accomplish its physiological role ; thus , creating a short F - actin oligomer to study actin structure and dynamic interactions within and with ABPs is an attractive but challenging research area . Any approaches applied to modify actin should be strategically balanced to maintain physiological interactions that are integral to F - actin structure and function . Considering the work of Qu et al . ( 2018 ) , stoichiometric ribosylation of pPBM crosslinked actin and capping with DNase I at the pointed end of the trimer resulted in disruption of myosin binding interface resulting in no interaction with myosin . However , other ABPs such as gelsolin and cofilin bound to the ADPr - trimer support the view that various ABPs can bind in a mutually exclusive manner . This mechanism has been thought of as a mode of regulating actin function and localization of actin in various regions of the cells . Future study will involve exploring other ABPs that can bind to ADPr - trimer and study actin interfaces that support different modes of binding . 2 . 2 . 5 Future Directions The hetADPr - trimer made by Qu et al . ( 2018 ) is the smallest known short F - actin oligomer that binds myosin S1 and activates ATPase . However , it remains to be established if hetADPr - trimer supports lever arm movement required for force generation . Future work therefore entails purifying hetADPr - trimer and monitoring motility of fluorescently labelled myosin over actin coated surface in an in vitro motility assay using fluorescence microscopy . 280 – 282 Although myosin ATPase activity of pPBM crosslinked filaments remains unaffected , they have reduced velocity in vitro motility assays . 71 Conformational changes in the N - and C - termini 86 of F - actin upon myosin binding have been reported ; however , the exact role of the C - termini remains unclear . 267 Myosin induced conformational changes in the C - terminus of actin have been observed using pyrene labelled actin Cys - 373 ( Cys - 374 in α - actin ) . 283 Pyrene fluorescence results are supported by a stabilized C - terminus observed in the actomyosin structure which is not observed in the F - actin - tropomyosin structure . 4 , 267 The C - terminus in pPBM crosslinked actin is restricted due to the involvement of Cys - 374 ( the second last amino acid ) in crosslinking ; therefore pPBM crosslinked actin can be used to study how restricting the C - terminus affects lever arm movement and force generation . This work will require production of filaments made from purified crosslinked pPBM dimers and trimers , and measurement of their ATPase activity and motility over myosin . For F - dimer and F - trimer formed from pure dimer and trimer , respectively , the calculated gliding velocities would be 50 % and 33 % . These theoretical values are based on the percentage of crosslinked C - termini that would be present in pure F - dimer and F - trimer . In a preliminary experiment , I generated F - dimer and F - trimer from purified crosslinked dimers and trimers , noting some contamination of monomer in the dimer preparation . F - dimer and F - trimer were observed to glide at 70 % and 31 % of the velocity of uncrosslinked F - actin , respectively . Considering that contaminating monomer in the dimer preparation might account for the increased velocity of the F - dimer , these preliminary data support the idea that reduction in the motility of crosslinked filaments is the result of the percentage of subunits with the C - terminus restricted by crosslinking . ( Supplemental Figure 1 ) . 87 2 . 3 Cofilin is an ADPr - trimer binding actin binding protein 2 . 3 . 1 Background Cofilin is an actin severing protein that binds cooperatively to the filament . Alternatively , cofilin binds to severed filaments and stabilizes them . 145 In my study , cofilin bound to ADPr - trimer , but generated a non - crystallizable filamentous complex . 2 . 3 . 2 Experimental Procedures 2 . 3 . 2a Protein Purification 2 . 3 . 2a ( i ) Cofilin - 1 Preparation Recombinant Cofilin - 1 ( CFL1 ) expressed in E . coli was purified using metal affinity chromatography . All reaction components were filtered through 0 . 22 μm Millipore filters . Negatively stained grids and imaging were performed as described above for actin filament binding reactions . 90 2 . 3 . 3 Results and Discussion Cofilin binds F - actin at a pH less than 7 . 3 without destabilizing it and promotes severing at higher pH values . 284 Cofilin decorated actin filaments for cryo - EM structural determination were obtained by binding cofilin to actin filaments at pH 6 . 5 . 153 , 285 Therefore , I confirmed the binding ability of recombinant cofilin to actin filaments at pH 6 . 5 through co - sedimentation assays and negatively stained cofilin decorated actin filaments . The presence of cofilin in the F - actin pellet of co - sedimentation assays confirmed binding of cofilin to F - actin ( Figure 2 . 14 ) . The negatively stained cofilin decorated actin filaments were approximately 20 % thicker than the undecorated filaments due to the mass of the bound cofilin ( Figure 2 . 15 ) . Actin filaments appeared thicker in negatively stained images in the presence of cofilin and this corresponded with an increase in light scattering intensity of F - actin and cofilin reaction mixtures noted by others . 286 Pyrene depolymerization assays demonstrated the binding and severing activity of cofilin . An initial drop in the intensity of pyrene fluorescence followed by a steady state of fluorescence intensity was observed upon addition of cofilin to F - actin ( Figure 2 . 16 ) . The initial decrease in fluorescence intensity could result either from quenching of pyrene fluorescence upon cofilin binding or fragmentation of filaments followed by slow depolymerization or stabilization of fragmented filaments by cofilin . Nishida et al . ( 1984 ) also observed that cofilin addition reduced the fluorescence intensity of F - actin to that of G - actin , suggesting cofilin transforms actin subunits within the filament to a conformation similar to G - actin . The actin observed a linear decrease in fluorescence intensity with increasing cofilin concentration with maximum quenching observed at an equimolar molar ratio . F - actin fragmentation upon the addition of sub - stoichiometric amounts of cofilin was also supported by a decrease in the viscosity of F - actin solutions , an effect similar 91 Figure 2 . 13 10 % SDS - PAGE gel of purification progress of cofilin . Purified cofilin was stored with 10 % glycerol at - 80℃ . 92 Figure 2 . 14 10 % SDS - PAGE gel of co - sedimentation assay for cofilin . 10 μM of F - actin was incubated with an equimolar amount of cofilin on ice for 1 hour . The reaction was spun at 392 , 499 x g for 15 min in TLA - 110 Beckman rotor . The resulting pellet ( P ) and supernatant ( S / N ) were run on SDS - PAGE . The presence of cofilin along with actin in the pellet fraction indicated binding . F - actin alone and cofilin alone were run as controls . 93 Figure 2 . 15 Negatively stained micrographs of F - actin in the absence and presence of cofilin . A rapid decrease in fluorescence intensity was observed upon addition of cofilin followed by a steady phase ( B ) . A B Buffer added Cofilin added 95 to the severing protein gelsolin . Nishida et al . ( 1984 ) observed an increase in light scattering intensity ( LSI ) upon mixing cofilin to F - actin , attributed to the binding of cofilin along the entire length of actin filament . 286 Others have suggested that the initial rapid decrease in fluorescence intensity is due to fast cooperative binding followed by slower act of partial depolymerization and the drop in viscosity upon addition of cofilin could be due to change in flexibility or fragility of the cofilin bound actin filaments . 149 The saturation of actin filaments with cofilin changes the average helical twist of actin filaments by five degrees per subunit . 150 Severing of actin filaments into segments in the presence of cofilin has been confirmed using total internal reflection fluorescence microscopy ( TIRF ) . 152 Thus , co - sedimentation assays , negatively stained EM micrographs and pyrene depolymerization assays all confirmed the ability of cofilin to bind F - actin . With my goal to obtain a heterocomplex , binding between ADPr - trimer or ADPr - monomer and cofilin was determined by native - PAGE . Appearance of a higher new band on the gel indicated binding . The binding of ADPr - monomer and cofilin was further confirmed by analytical gel - filtration chromatography where a right - shift in the elution peak was observed ( Supplemental figure 2A ) . Cofilin binds to monomeric actin and cofilin binding sites on G - actin have been identified with NMR and crosslinking studies . 287 , 288 Since the only known predicted structure of cofilin bound to monomeric actin was obtained by superimposing the crystal structure of yeast - cofilin - 1 onto the structure of Twf - C ( C - terminal cofilin like domain of mouse twinfilin ) bound to actin monomer ( PDB : 3DAW ) , Cof : 1mr ( cofilin bound ADPr - monomer ) was purified and crystal trials were set - up collaboration with the Kimber lab ( Supplemental figure 2B ) . 289 Unfortunately , the complex did not yield any crystals . 96 For native gel reactions including ADPr - trimer and cofilin , the intensity of the trimer band decreased with an increase in the molar concentration of cofilin in the mixture . In addition , protein aggregation was observed in the wells of the gel corresponding to the reaction mix containing ADPr - trimer and cofilin ( Figure 2 . 17A ) . These native gel reactions were mounted on a carbon coated copper grid and stained with uranyl acetate for EM imaging . Filament like structures were observed in the EM micrographs ( Figure 2 . 17B ) . Filament formation might have resulted from cofilin induced conformational changes in ADPr - trimer that overcame the impact of ribosylation - meditated polymerization inhibition . In fact , cofilin binding to actin filaments is known to induce significant conformational changes that are greater than the change from G - to F - actin transformation . 153 Moreover , ADPr - trimer exhibits F - actin like flexibility that allows gelsolin to transform ADP - trimer into a nucleation competent structure ; therefore , conformational changes in ADPr - trimer upon cofilin binding that allows polymerization are possible . 11 Alternatively , cofilin molecules might bridge contacts between subunits of two or more ADPr - trimers resulting in filamentous structures . Cofilin bridges actin - actin contacts in polymerization - deficient rhodamine labelled actin . 152 During severing , cofilin disrupts longitudinal contacts in F - actin but cofilin forms a crosslink that maintains contacts between actin subunits and severing occurs in the undecorated regions to which cofilin - induced changes are propagated . 153 Monomeric actin forms a ternary complex with DNase I and cofilin , suggesting the existence of two distinct binding regions for these molecules on actin , I tested the binding of D : trimer to cofilin on a native gel . 290 A new higher band was observed on the native gel for the reaction with D : monomer and cofilin , whereas no shift in the band was observed for the reaction mixture with D : trimer and cofilin . This indicates that the cofilin binding site is disrupted in the D : trimer ( Figure 2 . 18 ) . 97 Figure 2 . 17 10 % Native - PAGE and electron micrograph of binding assay of cofilin . A ) 10 % Native - PAGE of binding reactions including cofilin and ADPr - monomer in 1 : 1 ratio , and cofilin and ADPr - trimer in 1 : 1 , 1 : 2 and 1 : 3 molar ratios . Cofilin or ADPr - monomer or trimer alone were run as controls on the gel . A shift in the band for the reaction with ADPr - monomer and cofilin indicated binding . For reactions containing ADPr - trimer and cofilin , the intensity of the trimer band decreased with an increase in the molar ratio of cofilin accompanied with protein aggregation observed in the corresponding wells .
