D : monomer D : trimer D : monomer : cofilin 99 The structural features of the cofilin : ADPr - trimer filaments and the precise mechanism of conformational changes in the ADPr - trimer induced upon cofilin binding could not be deduced from the available data and would require further investigation . Overall , cofilin bound to ADPr - trimer but did not yield a complex suitable for crystallization or single particle cryo - EM structure determination . 2 . 3 . 4 Conclusion Cofilin is a well - established regulator of actin dynamics in cells . The binding site of cofilin on F - actin lies on the two adjacent longitudinal subunits along the helix ; a similar interface for side - binding ABPs exists on ADPr - trimer . Hence , to generate a heterocomplex for structural determination , I investigated the binding of cofilin to ADPr - trimer . Recombinant cofilin bound to native F - actin and both ADPr - monomer and trimer . ADPr - monomer binding to cofilin binding was confirmed by a band shift on the native gel and shift in elution peak on analytical chromatograms . The cofilin : 1mr was purified but did not yield crystals . In contrast , cofilin binding to ADPr - trimer resulted in the formation of non - crystallizable filamentous structures . The assembly of ADPr - trimer into filaments upon cofilin binding might be attributed to either the large structural changes influenced by cofilin overcoming the impact of ribosylation or / and cofilin forming alternative contacts between actin subunits of several ADPr - trimers bridging them together . It has not been determined if the filamentous cofilin : ADPr - trimer has an F - actin like helical twist . Interestingly , both myosin and cofilin bind to F - actin cooperatively in clusters and compete for binding to F - actin ; however , unlike cofilin , myosin was unable to bind or induce any conformational changes in ADPr - trimer to facilitate its binding . 278 Understanding the nature of cofilin - induced conformational changes in ADPr - trimer and its physiological significance requires further investigation , and is beyond the scope of this research . 100 2 . 3 . 5 Future Directions Cofilin bound ADPr - timer produced a complex unsuitable for crystallization and single particle analysis , therefore the complex obtained did not have any potential for generating structural information . However , investigating the ADPr - trimer : cofilin with cryo - EM using helical reconstruction and comparing it to the EM structures available might reveal a different mode of binding of cofilin to actin filaments . An alternative actin long - dimer ( LD ) consisting of two actin subunits from the same F - actin strand was prepared by copolymerizing Q41C / C374A human ACTC mutant actin with α - cardiac bovine actin following Morrison’s protocol with slight modifications . 68 Preliminary results from native gel of the LD with cofilin produced a band shift suggesting an interaction . This interaction can be confirmed with other experimental techniques and the heterocomplex purified for future crystal trials or single particle cryo - EM ( Supplemental figure 3 ) . 2 . 4 Gelsolin is an ADPr - trimer binding actin binding protein 2 . 4 . 1 Background Gelsolin is an actin - severing protein . The mechanism of gelsolin binding and severing have been deduced from a combination of biochemical and structural investigations ; however , no high resolution structure of either full - length gelsolin bound to F - actin or gelsolin capped F - actin is available . 209 Here I aimed to generate the first near atomic resolution structure of the gelsolin capped ADPr - trimer . For details on gelsolin biology , severing mechanism and structural models refer to section 1 . 3 . 3 of Chapter 1 . Gelsolin binds to ADPr - trimer in an equimolar ratio to form a GSFL : 3mr complex with an estimated molecular weight of 212 kDa . The GSFL : 3mr complex did not crystallize ; therefore , 101 single particle cryo - EM reconstruction ( SPR ) was considered to resolve the structure of the complex . The suitability of the sample for SPR was determined by negative staining . The GSFL : 3mr negative staining EM work was an initiative aimed to create a workflow and platform for future cryo - EM structural determinations of non - crystallizable actin complexes . The negatively stained micrographs were acquired at the Molecular and Cellular Imaging Facility at Guelph and image analysis was established and performed in collaboration with the Khursigara lab . Potential collaborators beyond the Guelph campus for future cryo - EM imaging and data processing were also identified and established . 2 . 4 . 1a Negative Stain Single particle EM imaging of negatively stained and cryo preserved samples is becoming more common for the structural determination of biomolecules . Negative staining is used to assess the quality of the specimen and optimize conditions for cryo - EM . 291 Negative staining provides information on the compositional and conformational homogeneity of the protein complexes , size and shape of the oligomeric state , and the tendency of the sample to dissociate or aggregate . 260 Negative staining involves embedding the protein molecules absorbed onto a carbon film in a layer of heavy metal salt . Since the protein molecules adsorbed onto a carbon film are enveloped by an electron dense stain , high contrast is produced with particles appearing as light areas because of low electron density and low electron scattering power relative to the surrounding dense stain . Both high contrast and the tendency of proteins to absorb on the carbon film in one or a few preferred orientations allows assessment of the heterogeneity of the sample . 291 , 292 Some sub - structural features are revealed if the stain is able to penetrate into crevices on the protein producing irregular contrast . 292 , 293 However , negative staining can introduce some artifacts ; specifically , flattening of the molecule and air - drying during sample preparation can affect the structural 102 integrity of samples sensitive to dehydration . Since the limits of achievable resolution is ~ 20 Å , reconstructed 3D models from negative stain imaging depict the overall shape of the sample and less information within the core . 292 , 294 2 . 4 . 2b Single Particle Reconstruction Single particle reconstruction ( SPR ) determines structure by averaging multiple views of several copies of the same molecule , so is sometimes referred to as single particle averaging . 251 Structural determination by SPR requires acquisition of a large number of images with high contrast and sufficient resolution to determine structural details . The acquisition and processing of such a large dataset is often time consuming . However , with recent computer advancements , images can be automatically collected and image processing software , such as EMAN2 , Relion , SPIDER , FREALIGN , and SPARX can reconstruct 3D models from 2D micrographs . 295 – 301 3D structural determination from 2D micrographs utilizes SPR algorithms and an advanced set of heuristics to select specific algorithms for each refinement task . 302 – 304 The process of image analysis begins by the labour - intensive process of picking and extracting single protein particles that are oriented and distributed randomly in the EM micrographs . A contrast transfer function ( CTF ) correction is applied to restore undistorted information that is buried in the noise . 305 Structure determination begins with 2D analysis of the extracted particles . The extracted particles are grouped into homogenous subsets based on their angular alignments . The subsets of particles in each homogenous group are aligned and averaged to create class - averages . 2D class averages are then used to estimate and iteratively reconstruct a 3D model ( Figure 2 . 19 ) . 303 I used EMAN2 for SPR because it is user friendly and does not require Nvidia GPU , so it could be installed on the computers available in the Khursiagara lab . 260 103 Figure 2 . 19 Flow chart of single particle reconstruction in EMAN 2 . 2 . Figure adapted from Zhou ( 2015 ) . 306 104 However , automated particle picking in EMAN2 can only be run only on Nvidia GPU ; therefore , I manually picked ~ 42 , 500 protein particles from the micrographs . 2 . 4 . 2 Experimental Procedures 2 . 4 . 2a Purification of Proteins Gelsolin , ADPr - trimer and gelsolin bound ADPr - trimer ( GSFL : 3mr ) were prepared as described previously in section 2 . 2 . 2 . 2 . 4 . 2b Determining Stability of the Complex Purified fractions containing GSFL : 3mr complex were divided into 100 μL aliquots and stored at 4℃ and - 80℃ . Aliquots of fractions were run on native gels on day 1 , 3 and 5 post - purification to determine stability of the complex . 2 . 4 . 2c Negative Stained Grid Preparation 7 μL of purified GSFL : 3mr complex at a concentration of 6 μg / mL was applied onto glow discharged carbon coated copper grids to achieve good distribution of the particles on the grid . After 30 s of incubation of the sample on the grid , excess sample was blotted off from the grid using filter paper . The samples were stained with 7 μL of 2 % uranyl acetate stain for 30 s . Excess stain was blotted off . Grids were stored at RT for imaging . 2 . 4 . 2d Imaging , Data Collection and Processing The negatively stained grids were imaged at the Molecular and Cellular Imaging Facility , University of Guelph using a FEI Tecnai G2 F20 ( FEI Company , Hillsboro ) aligned for parallel illumination and operated at 200 kV fitted with a bottom mounted Gatan 4k CCD . Images were collected with a defocus range between 0 . 599 μm and 3 . 9 μm with a pixel size of 4 . 53 Å / pixel . GSFL : 3mr complex particles were single - dispersed . 105 Particle Picking and Classification Single protein particles were selected manually using the EMAN2 interactive boxing function ( e2boxer ) . The average length of the particles was ~ 75 . 5 Å ; thus , the box size was set to 117 . 9 Å to accommodate particles in the box with enough background . In total , ~ 42 , 500 particles were extracted from the micrographs . A contrast transfer function ( CTF ) correction was applied to the micrographs as recommended in the EMAN2 protocol to improve the appearance of the model and reduce artifacts . Class averages were generated by reference - free classification ( 2Drefine function ) for the entire data set based on an automated iterative alignment approach . 297 In total , 31 class averages were generated . Each class average had a large number of particles with similar size , shape and orientation . As a result , the signal was intensified , and the shape of the complex became more prominent . The class averages presenting sharp and strong features with clearly delineated borders of the protein were used for analysis . Smeared or blurry class averages were removed from the set . Of the 42 , 500 particles picked , ~ 36 , 250 were included for generating the class averages . Any particles that were not centered in the particle selection box were excluded by the aligning function of the software . Class averages underwent 8 iterations ; all parameters for class average generation were selected as recommended by the developer . Building and Refining of the model Producing a 3D high resolution refined model is an iterative process that requires an initial 3D model . The approach for initial model generation is incorporated into the e2initial model function in EMAN2 which is based on a Monte - Carlo algorithm . An initial model is generated from user - identified class averages representing different views of the particle , not including 106 projections of different compositional or conformational states of the particle . The initial model can be iteratively refined with the entire data set of particles using the EMAN2 real space projection matching algorithm ( e2refine ) . 297 In the present work , the sample potentially exhibited heterogeneity and the features of heterogenous species were not identifiable in the class averages obtained , therefore 3D models representing the heterogenous species could not be generated based on the micrographs and available image processing . However , for training purpose and to demonstrate the workflow for EM model generation , an initial model was generated by selecting nine class averages that appeared similar in size and presented different views of the particle . The initial model was refined against the entire dataset . Eight initial models were generated after which the iteration that represented features of the class averages was refined against the entire dataset . Since the symmetry of the complex is not known , C1 symmetry was applied for model generation . Other parameters were selected as recommend by the developer . 2 . 4 . 3 Results and Discussion GSFL : 3mr complex purified on a gel filtration column appeared as a single band on the native gel ( Figure 2 . 20 ) . The complex was stable at 4℃ for up to 3 days , while at - 80℃ the complex formed aggregates present as additional bands on the native gel ( Figure 2 . 21 ) . Therefore , the purified complex was stored at 4℃ and used to prepare negatively stained grids on day 2 following purification . For each round of optimization of staining and imaging , a fresh batch of complex was prepared . Six batches of complex were purified with each complex preparation taking 16 - 18 days . Once the staining and imaging protocol was optimized , the grids with the negatively stained complex were stored at RT and imaged over a period of a few months at the Molecular and Cellular Imaging Facility , University of Guelph . 107 Figure 2 . 20 Purification of GSFL : 3mr complex . A ) 10 % native gel of GSFL : 3mr elution fractions from Superdex 200 ( 10 / 300 ) . B ) Chromatogram corresponding to the elution fractions shown in A . Elution fractions , D2 and D1 , were screened at various concentrations on negativley stained grids to rule out the presence of any aggregates and optimize protein concentration to obtain a uniform distribution of protein particles on grids for imaging . Elution fractions D5 to D1 were obtained in elution volume ranging from 11 . 2 ml to 12 . 2 ml . A B Volume ( ml ) 108 Figure 2 . 21 Stability of GSFL : 3mr complex determined on 10 % native gels . A ) Native gel of fractions , D4 and D3 , on day 1 . GSFL or ADPr - trimer ( 3mr ) alone were run as controls . B ) Elution fractions stored at 4℃ were run on the native gel on day 3 . A band representing GSFL : 3mr complex was visible for each of the fractions , D4 and D3 . C ) On day 5 , fractions stored at 4℃ and - 80℃ were run on gel . Complex in fraction D4 stored at 4℃ had completely degraded , while fraction D3 stored at - 80℃ showed protein aggregation which was seen as additional bands on the gel . Thus , for each round of sample screening for EM , freshly purifed complex was stored at 4℃ and applied to grids on day 2 . A C B 109 Figure 2 . 22 Negatively stained EM micrographs . Scale bar 50 nm . A B 111 More than 600 micrographs were acquired over a period of four months . Overall , 437 micrographs presenting evenly distributed distinct protein particles were used for analysis by EMAN2 ( Figure 2 . 22 ) . In total , ~ 42 , 500 protein particles were selected manually from the micrographs using image processing software EMAN2 ( Figure 2 . 23 ) . The process of manually picking - particle took 7 full days . These particles were organized into 31 class averages which included ~ 36 , 000 particles . Any particles that were not centered in the selection box or did not align with any of the class averages were excluded by the averaging function of the software . The relatively small number of class averages generated from a large number of particles suggest that the GSFL : 3mr complex adsorbs onto the carbon grid in a few favoured orientations . Most of the class averages depicted a donut like shape . The three actin subunits of trimer were visible in some class averages as three dots . The empty space visible in the center of some class averages could be due to the presence of an ADP - ribosyl group at the intersubunit interaction site , conformational changes upon gelsolin binding , or deformation of the complex due to staining . Of the 31 class averages , 19 with sharp and strong features of the protein were chosen for further analysis ( Figure 2 . 24 ) . Those that were smeared and blurry were removed from the set . The class averages differed in their diameter . For example , class averages 4 , 5 , 6 and 7 appear smaller compared to 9 , 10 , 11 and 15 . Different sizes of class averages indicated the existence of either compositional or conformational heterogeneity in the specimen ( Figure 2 . 24 ) . Measurements of specific particles were made using ‘measure’ tool in ImageJ showing the diversity of particle dimensions within the sample ( Figure 2 . 25 ) . Multiples modes of complex formation or unstable complexes that dissociate during staining can lead to heterogeneity in the sample . Heterogeneity can also be introduced to some extent by the negative stain procedure due 112 Figure 2 . 24 Class averages representing features of the GSFL : 3mr sample . Class averages were obtained by e2Drefine function in EMAN2 which uses an iterative reference free method . The initial set of iteration produces a set of class averages based on rotational and translational invariants computed for each particle . This initial set of class averages provide alignment references to which all particle data set was compared and aligned for the next iteration . The aligned particles were averaged , and the least similar particles were excluded . The new class average acts as an alignment reference to the next iteration . Comparison of the class averages suggested presence of particles of different size in the sample . Class averages 4 , 5 , 6 and 7 appear smaller in size compared to 9 , 10 , 11 and 14 . 113 Figure 2 . 25 Enlarged view of a part of two different micrographs indicating negatively stained GSFL : 3mr complex particles . A and B indicate dimensions of 10 particles from micrographs C and D , respectively measured in ImageJ . Particles of different size in the sample suggests presence of heterogeneity in the sample . Scale bar was added using ImageJ ; scale from the original micrographs was used as reference . A B C D 114 to distortions during absorption of the molecule on the grid or due to inconsistent embedding in the stain . 292 Since it is not possible to reliably sub - categorize the observed heterogenous class averages into groups representing different structural complexes , a reliable biologically relevant model could not be generated . However , to demonstrate the process of single particle model building , refinement and rigid body fitting using Chimera , 9 class averages that were approximately similar in length were used ( Figure 2 . 26A ) . These class averages included 8 , 282 particles with 1400 to 700 particles in each class . Different views of the initial model generated from selected class averages is shown in Figure 2 . 26B . Refinement of this initial model with the entire particle set generated a low - resolution heart shaped structure with no visible surface details ( Figure 2 . 26C ) . Both the initial model and refined model presented an empty space in the center , a characteristic also seen in the class averages . Since the refined model was a blob , the electron density map of the initial model was used for rigid body fitting . A simulated model of gelsolin bound actin - trimer was produced in PyMOL from the available crystal structures of gelsolin segments bound to actin monomers and a cryo - EM structure of F - actin . Since the structure of ADPr - trimer is not available , actin trimer was adapted from cryo - EM structures of F - actin resolved by Wakabayshi et al . ( 2010 ) . 307 Thus , the trimer model did not present any variations in the intersubunit interactions introduced by chemical modifications ( chemical crosslinking and ribosylation ) that would exist in the ADPr - trimer . The simulated model was generated using the ‘align’ function of PyMOL to overlay the actin subunits from crystal structures of G1 / actin monomer ( 1EQY ) and G4 - 6 / actin monomer complex ( 1H1V ) onto the trimer subunits . Since , the overall shape of the theoretical model generated in PyMOL based on McGough’s ( 2011 ) model ( see Figure 1 . 7 ) did not resemble the initial model , a simulated model representing a different mode of binding of gelsolin segments 115 Figure 2 . 26 Building model from negative stained data . A ) Nine class averages were used to generate an initial negative staining model shown in B . B ) Different views of the initial model . C ) Initial model in B was refined with the entire data set . The refined model presented no structural details and appeared featureless . A C B 116 Figure 2 . 27 Side view of negative stain ( NS ) map and GS : 3mr model showing G1 and G4 - 6 bound to trimer based on McGough’s model . A ) Simulated model of actin trimer bound to gelsolin segments was generated in PyMOL ( PDB : 3G37 ( F - actin ) ; 1EQY ( G1 / actin monomer ) ; 1H1V ( G4 - 6 / actin monomer ) . B ) Fitting of the simulated model into a NS map was done manually using Chimera . The overall shape of the NS map resembled the simulated model of the complex ; however , some regions of the simulated model did not fit into the NS map Conformational changes introduced into the actin trimer either due to gelsolin binding or chemical modifications ( ribosylation and crosslinking ) or lack of complete structural detail from the small number of class averages used to generate structure could result in an incomplete fit . The NS map was scaled to the simulated model using the A / pixel value from EMAN2 . The model was generated to depict the EM workflow . 18 ֯ 0 A B B 118 was generated to depict the EM workflow ( Figure 2 . 27 ) . The overall shape of this simulated model was similar to the initial model . This proposed simulated model was manually fitted into the electron density map of the initial model using Chimera . However , all the regions of this model did not fit into the map . This could result from missing structural details due a small number of class averages used for initial model building or due to the simulated model lacking conformational changes that occur upon complex formation , segments of gelsolin ( G2 ) , or actin modifications ( crosslinking and ribosylation ) ( Figure 2 . 28 ) . Since class averages did not show finer details , the possibility of inclusion of conformationally different class averages could not be ignored . Since heterogenous sub - populations could not be sub - classified using the workflow described in this thesis , the biological relevance of the model presented is questionable . Based on class - averages obtained , it was not possible to distinguish between different orientations and various conformational states of the complex . In addition , the GSFL : 3mr complex particles seemed extremely small , therefore any finer differences in the class averages were not prominent . For image processing alignment software to identify finer differences in structural features of conformationally diverse species , the sample might need to be imaged at a higher magnification ( ~ 100 - 150K ) than used for micrographs obtained for this project at an actual magnification of 66 , 170 - times . Alternative staining techniques can also be used to make the differences between the diverse species clear and overcome any deformations caused due to staining technique . Since several thousand particles were classified into a relatively small number of class averages , it appears that the conventional uranyl acetate negative staining technique used in this work favored a few preferred orientations of the complex on the carbon support . In addition , heterogeneity in the sample could have been caused by deformations of the complex during staining or incomplete stain embedding . To overcome these issues , an alternative carbon sandwich 119 staining technique that prevents artifacts due to incomplete embedding of specimen in stain could be used . The addition of sugar or glycerol to the specimen in the carbon sandwich technique promotes absorption of protein particles on carbon film in random orientations . However , specimens with glucose and sugars added require imaging at liquid nitrogen temperatures due to the sensitivity of sugars to radiation damage . 305 Dehydration of the sample during negative staining can also cause deformations or cause the complex to dissociate and can be avoided with the carbon layer sandwich technique . 308 In short , alternative staining approaches can improve the quality of 3D structures obtained by negative staining by reducing deformation due to dehydration , adsorption and incomplete staining . Other stains such as ammonium molybdate , aurothioglucose and tungstate stains also are available . 309 These differ in properties and lead to different staining of the samples . Uranyl acetate generates the highest contrast , but requires acidic conditions to prevent precipitation and thus could lead to pH - dependent conformational changes in the samples . However , it has been shown that the stain fixes protein structure on the millisecond time scale , avoiding this issue . 310 Optimizing the staining technique and acquiring images at a higher magnification can reduce artifacts and enhance some finer structural differences in heterogenous species for the image processing software to pick and analyse . Further , various image classification tools can be applied to group heterogenous species into distinct classes averages with distinguishable features for 3D map building . The alignment and classification of particles depend on the software and classification algorithms used . Basically , the classification methods are based on comparing and aligning pixel intensities of the imaged particles . Multi - reference alignment ( MRA ) process of particle classification can identify heterogenous species in a specimen . In this method , unique class 120 averages are selected from the reference - free classification result and used as references for MRA . In MRA , all the particle datasets are cross - correlated with all the references and designated to the reference that gives the highest value of cross - correlation . All images designated to references are averaged . The process is repeated iteratively using averages from each cycle as a reference for the next cycle until further improvement is observed in the resolution of the class averages . 311 IMAGIC , SPIDER , and EMAN have modules to perform alignment , of which SPIDER allows various classification algorithms to process the data set . 299 , 312 , 313 Thus , with the combination of optimized staining approaches and image processing , a reliable 3D map can be obtained from negatively stained heterogenous samples . Due to presence of high signal to noise ratios , negative staining can reveal heterogenous populations which are challenging to distinguish with vitrified samples and would produce unreliable features in 3D reconstructions of cryo - EM samples . 314 , 315 2 . 4 . 4 Conclusions Since there is no known structure of gelsolin - capped actin filaments or any high resolution structure of gelsolin bound to F - actin , I produced and purified gelsolin - bound ADPr - trimer complex for structural determination . 209 The GSFL : 3mr complex did not yield any crystals ; therefore , a negative staining EM approach was used to determine the quality of the complex for vitrification and possible cryo - EM 3D structure determination . Although the complex purified as a single band on the native gel , analysis of the negatively stained complex suggested the presence of heterogeneous species of the complex in the sample . Heterogeneity in the GSFL : 3mr complex sample might explain the inability of the complex to crystallize . Heterogeneity in the GSFL : 3mr complex sample could result from multiple binding modes of gelsolin to actin subunits in the ADPr - trimer , instability of the complex resulting in dissociation during the staining procedure , or artifacts produced by the staining technique . Precise distinctions between the heterogenous states 121 that existed in the sample could not be established based on the class averages obtained from the data acquired and available image processing . Optimized staining techniques coupled with images acquired at a higher magnification could make the finer distinctions between heterogenous species more evident . Moreover , using tools such as multiple reference alignment for 2D particle alignment can lead to identification of heterogenous species and generation of low - resolution 3D map of these species . The goal of work described in this thesis was to utilize the resources currently available in the department to determine feasibility and demonstrate the workflow for future EM structural work . Multiple modes of binding of gelsolin to ADPr - trimer or the complex adopting various conformations is yet it be established with further EM investigations . 2 . 4 . 5 Future Directions Future works entails exploring image classification tools such as multiple reference alignment for generating class averages of heterogenous population and installing automated particle picking software to avoid any errors introduced due to manual particle picking . Additionally , optimizing negative staining and increasing the electron microscopy imaging magnification depending on the protein sample under investigation should also be considered . The combination of these approaches has a potential to establish the suitability of the sample for vitrification and 3D map generation by cryo - EM . An updated computer system installed with GPU required for data processing , training on the image processing software and establishing collaborations with labs that routinely perform protein EM structural work would help streamline the process . Some potential future collaborators include Dr . John Rubinstein , University of Toronto and / or Dr . Joaquin Ortega , McGill University . The Rubinstein lab uses cryoSPARC and the Ortega lab uses EMAN2 for their EM structural data 122 processing . While EMAN2 and Relion are the most commonly used image processing platforms , other software that can be used alone or in combination could be explored . Some of the known software include – cryoSPARC , Eos , IMAGIC , IPLT , MDPP , MRC , Simple , Sparx , Spider , Suprim , SPHI , RE , Xmipp , Bsoft and Cyclops . Low - resolution negatively stained preliminary models of protein complexes can be produced from the images acquired on campus , with updated computing and image processing software . However , the generation of high resolution cryo - EM structures would require submitting proposals to facilities equipped with Krios G3 , a 300 kV Cryo Transmission Electron Microscope , for imaging . The two closet facilities to which cryopreserved samples can be shipped are the High - Throughput cryo - EM Facility , Hospital for Sick Children Research Institute , University of Toronto and the Facility for Electron Microscopy Research , McGill University . Cryo - EM structural work would require preparation of cryo - preserved sample grids and shipping these grids to the imaging facilities . Consistent preparation of protein sample cryo - grids with uniform ice thickness is crucial for obtaining micrographs for structural data . Therefore , I explored the feasibility of generating cryo - preserved samples for GSFL : 3mr complex in collaboration with the Khursigara lab using resources available in the MCI facility , University of Guelph ( Supplementary figure 6 ) . In addition to optimizing the protocol for the preparation of vitrified samples , a protocol for grid storage and shipment needs to be established . Along with establishing a pipeline for the future EM studies in the lab , I expanded my search for F - ABPs that bind ADPr - trimer using advances in proteomics . Since the candidate approach described in this chapter was limited to recombinantly - purified ABPs available to me , I applied an unbiased approach to identify potential ADPr - trimer interacting proteins from zebrafish 123 cell lysates using mass spectrometry . Details of my unbiased approach are described in the next chapter . 124 3 IDENTIFICATION OF ADPR - TIMER BINDING PARTNERS WITH ADPR - TRIMER PULL 1 DOWNS AND MASS SECTROMETRY 3 . 1 Overview In addition to the candidate - based approach described in chapter 2 , an unbiased approach was used to identify ADPr - trimer binding partners from cell lysates . Since we had access to the zebrafish facility in the Hagen Aqualab at the University of Guelph , we used 5 dpf ( days post fertilization ) zebrafish ( Danio rerio ) embryos for generating cell lysates . Additionally , the zebrafish genome has been completely sequenced and at least one zebrafish homolog exists for 70 % of all human protein - coding genes . 316 Actin binding proteins from zebrafish cell lysates were retained on affinity resins obtained by coupling G - actin or ADPr - trimer ( 3mr ) to affigel - 10 , called G - affigel and 3mr - affigel , respectively . A control experiment showed that the actin binding segments 4 - 6 of gelsolin ( G4 - 6 ) bound to and could be eluted from G - affigel . 317 Actin monomer binding proteins were removed from the clarified zebrafish embryo lysate by incubating with G - affigel and the resulting flow through was incubated with 3mr - affigel . Any non - specifically binding proteins were removed with a 50 mM KCl wash . Proteins bound to the resulting resins were identified by mass spectrometry . The initial list of F - ABPs bound to ADPr - trimer was generated in consultation with Dr . Jennifer Geddes - McAlister , University of Guelph . The proteins that bound to G - affigel were eliminated and proteins detected with 3mr - affigel only with more than one detected peptide were examined . This presence / absence approach eliminated any further investigation of non - specific or background interactors . The identified hits were ranked based on their Q - value . The actin - associated functional role of identified hits was researched and myosin light chain 6B ( MLC6B ) was selected for further biochemical validation . Recombinant MLC6B was purified from a bacterial expression system with a removable affinity His 6 - tag . Our 125 results from pull - down assays indicate that apo - MLC6B and MLC6B associated with myosin binds to ADPr - trimer , supporting the MS results . Interestingly , apo - MLC6B does not bind uncrosslinked F - actin , suggesting that ADPr - trimer represents a conformation of F - actin that is favoured for MLC6B binding , with implications on the in vivo function of MLC6B . 3 . 2 Introduction 3 . 2 . 1 Mass Spectrometry Mass - spectrometry - based proteomics play a key role in protein identification and quantification in the study of protein - protein interactions , protein function , modification and localization . 318 The identification and characterization of proteins by MS involves two approaches : top - down and bottom - up . In the top - down approach , the intact proteins are used directly for analysis . 319 In the bottom up approach , proteins are enzymatically digested , and the resulting peptides are analysed for identification and characterization . The bottom - up approach , also referred to as the shotgun approach , uses labelled and label - free techniques for protein quantification . 320 The labelled technique requires incorporation of isotopic labels into samples being probed . 321 Labels can be introduced either in vivo by supplementing cell culture media with stable isotope - containing amino acids or in vitro by chemical or enzymatic means . 322 – 324 Labels allow identification of identical peptides from different samples , allowing several samples to be run on MS simultaneously , thereby removing variability between MS runs . 325 The main advantage of the labelled technique is that the molecular composition of the labelled sample and control are similar , thus identical peptides generated can be compared directly . 326 However , the labelled technique requires a culturable sample which involves a complex experimental protocol that uses expensive reagents , with the possibility of incomplete labelling and incomplete understanding the nature of different labels and the way they are introduced , or their efficiency . 327 Consequently , 126 label - free quantification techniques ( LFQ ) have gained in popularity . In contrast to the labelled technique , LFQ does not require peptides to be labelled and the peptides are compared directly across different samples from independent MS runs . Technical advances in high performance liquid chromatography systems ( HPLC ) , high resolution and scanning rates of mass spectrometers have made this possible . A detailed description of these technical advances is beyond the scope of this thesis . 327 Label - free quantification technique requires no extra labelling experimental steps and many samples can be compared simultaneously . The peptide mixture resulting from protein digestion of the samples is analysed by tandem MS ( MS / MS ) and identified by a database search . A major drawback with the label - free technique is that MS run conditions ( e . g . temperature , experimenter , column condition ) may differ between samples . Therefore , errors resulting from measurement conditions are more likely to occur in the label - free than labelled technique . However , including a well - chosen standard in label - free experiments ( e . g . a labelled control sample mixed to each sample ) prior to the MS run may reduce this problem . 326 Since the zebrafish embryos used in this project are not culturable and chemical labeling would involve a high cost , the LFQ technique was used for identification of F - ABPs retained on affinity resins in pull - down assays . The LFQ method broadly includes four fundamental steps : preparation of the sample , separation of peptides , analysis of the sample by MS / MS and data analysis ( identification , quantification and statistical analysis ) ( Figure 3 . 1 ) . 127 Figure 3 . 1 A typical workflow for a standard bottom - up proteomic analysis . Figure adapted from Mikalsen et al . ( 2008 ) . 325 128 3 . 2 . 1a Sample Preparation and Detection by MS / MS Preparation of the protein samples includes reduction of proteins by DTT or triethylphosphine followed by alkylation and digestion of the protein mixture with a protease , with trypsin being the most commonly used . The resulting peptide mixture is separated by high performance liquid chromatography and the effluent containing peptides is electro - sprayed into a mass spectrometer . The mass spectrometer collects MS / MS spectra for the peptides of the protein sample . The relative abundance of the protein in the original sample is deduced by comparing the number of MS / MS spectra among a set of experiments . Extensive MS / MS data detection across the chromatographic elution profile leads to protein identification and quantification . 327 , 328 3 . 2 . 1b MS Data Analysis Several software packages , such as MaxQuant , Scaffold and Proteome Discoverer are available for quantification of data obtained from label - free mass spectrometry techniques . These software packages provide an interface for a wide range of proteomics workflows , including protein peptide identification and quantification , and post translational modifications . Protein peptide identification of the MS / MS data involves database search engines , such as MASCOT , SEQUEST and X ! Tandem . These search engines compare observed spectra to the theoretical spectra of the reference proteome obtained in silico by virtual cleavage of peptides in the proteome sequence or spectral libraries of annotated observed spectra . 329 These search engines use different scoring and matching algorithms to assign scores to the peptides , providing the best matches . The match between spectrum and best scoring peptides is called Peptide - spectrum match ( PSM ) . With an increased number of unique peptides identified , the confidence in the identification of the proteins is increased . 330 However , there could be false identifications which are validated by applying a filter called the false discovery rate ( FDR ) , the expected percent of 129 false predictions in a set of predictions . The strict and relaxed FDR for PSM is usually set at 1 % and 5 % , respectively . A FDR value of 1 % indicates that only one in one hundred filtered matches are expected to be false positives . The confidence of specific identification is given by the Q - value ; the minimum false discovery rate required to accept the identification . 331 For example in Table 1 , a Q - value of 0 . 009 for Tyrosine 3 - monooxygenase activation protein and RAB2A means 0 . 9 % of all the proteins with a Q - value less than this are expected to be false positives i . e . , out of 378 of total identified proteins with a Q - value of less than 0 . 009 , only 3 . 4 of them are likely to be false positives . In case of MLC6B , a Q - value of zero indicates that the likelihood of having that as a false positive is extremely rare . Protein quantification or relative abundance is determined either by spectral counting or chromatographic peptide peak intensity measurements . Spectral counting estimates protein abundance by correlating the number of MS / MS spectra matched to a peptide from a protein to the amount of protein in the sample . 332 , 333 Studies indicate that the peptide spectral counts across different control runs are comparable and reproducible . 334 , 335 Peptide intensity measurements are obtained by integrating the area under the curve for a given peptide ion intensity over its chromatographic elution volume . 336 Studies indicate that both spectral and peptide intensity measurement correlate with protein abundances and inclusion of statistical analysis facilitates detection of small , but biologically significant differences in complex biological samples . 336 – 338 3 . 2 . 2 Light Chains of Myosin The lowest Q - score hit from my ADPr - trimer MS data analysis was MLC6B , a non - muscle essential light chain ( ELC ) that was identified as a potential binding partner of ADPr - trimer . MLC6B binds to both non - muscle myosin - IIA and - IIB . 339 A multiple sequence alignment shows 130 Figure 3 . 2 Multiple Sequence Alignment ( MSA ) of ELC isoforms . MSA of sequences of skeletal ELC isoforms found in human , rabbit and chicken with MLC6B . The major structural elements identified for ELC skeletal muscle are indicated as : A - actin binding region ; M - myosin SH3 binding region , I - IV - EF hand motifs . 340 Ala - Pro - Lys - Lys residues at the N - terminus interact directly with actin . 341 Removal of the first 11 amino acids of recombinant ELC A1 ( an ELC found in skeletal muscle ) bound to S1 abolishes crosslinking of ELC A1 with actin . 342 MSA was performed using CLUSTALW and the figure was generated in ESPript 3 . 0 . 131 Figure 3 . 3 Structural overview of myosin light chains . A ) Myosin light chains associated with the heavy chain . Myosin heavy chain , ELC and RLC are shown in gray , cyan and magenta , respectively . ELC and RLC bind to the IQ motif in the neck domain distal from the globular head domain ( PDB : 1S5G ) . B ) Overlay of theoretical model of MLC6B ( cyan ) with CaM ( tv green ) in cartoon representation . Since the structure of MLC6B is unknown , a theoretical model was generated using the Swiss - Model server with myosin light chain from PDB : 1W7I as template . The generated theoretical model of MLC6B was aligned with the structure of CaM ( PDB : 2IX7 ) . Like CaM , MLC6B possesses N - and C - terminal lobes consisting of two EF hand motifs . A B 132 a significant sequence identity between zebrafish MLC6B and human , chicken and rabbit skeletal muscle ELCs ( Figure 3 . 2 ) . Thus , it is important to review the structure and function of myosin light chains to set the context for the work described here . Myosin is a multiprotein complex composed of heavy chains and light chains . The heavy chains form the N - terminal motor domain , the central neck region , and the tail domain . The neck region of the heavy chain possesses IQ motifs that bind light chains . When bound to light chains , the neck region is referred to as the lever arm . 114 An IQ motif is 20 - 25 amino acids long containing the consensus sequence IQXXXRGXXXR which is widely found in all myosins . Two types of light chains known as Essential light chains ( ELCs ) and Regulatory light chains ( RLCs ) bind to myosin ( Figure 3 . 3A ) . The regulatory light chains are so named because they take part in the regulation of the enzymatic activity of myosin . 343 Similarly , the essential light chains are so termed because they can be removed from the myosin heavy chain only under harsh conditions ( high pH ) and upon removal of these chains , myosin loses its enzymatic activity . 344 3 . 2 . 2a Isoforms of MLCs Several isoforms of myosin light chains are known to exist . The RLC gene family found in humans include : MYL2 , MYL5 , MYL7 , MYL9 , MYL10 , MYL11 , MYL12A and MYL12B . The ELC gene family includes MYL1 , MYL3 , MYL4 , MYL6 , and MYL6B . 345 These isoforms are expressed in a tissue specific manner ; for example , ELCs MYL1 and MYL3 are expressed in human adult cardiac tissue , and MYL6 and MYL6B exist in non - muscle myosin - II . The isoform specific tissue distribution and cellular localization of MLCs is determined by the N - terminal region of the light chains which is variable between isoforms , while the C - terminal half shows high sequence conservation . 346 , 347 133 3 . 2 . 2b Structure and Binding of ELCs MLCs belong to the calmodulin ( CaM ) and CaM - related gene families ; thus , they show structural similarity to CaM . 111 , 348 CaM is a conserved intracellular Ca 2 + sensor that interacts with several proteins found in all eukaryotic cells . 349 Some non - conventional myosins bind CaM as light chains . 350 CaM is a dumbbell - shaped molecule consisting of an N - terminal and a C - terminal lobe separated by a central helix . 351 Each of the CaM lobes possess two helix - loop - helix motifs termed EF hands . The loop that connects two helices binds Ca 2 + which can coordinate with oxygen or nitrogen atoms of amino acids side or main polypeptide chain . In the absence of Ca 2 + , the EF hands adopt an antiparallel ‘closed’ conformation , while in the presence of Ca 2 + , the EF hands are oriented in a perpendicular conformation called the ‘open’ conformation ( Figure 3 . 3B ) . 352 Structural details of myosin ELC in the ‘free - state’ not bound to a heavy chain are not available . However , ELC and RLC bound to the neck region were observed in the crystal structure of myosin S1 ( 2MYS ) and scallop myosin regulatory domain ( 1WDC ) . 115 , 353 – 355 Like CaM , ELCs bound to eukaryotic myosins have 4 EF - hand motifs . 114 , 345 The N - terminal region of an ELC binds a heavy chain in a closed conformation and the C - terminus binds in a semi - open conformation winding around the heavy chain binding closely . 114 , 115 , 354 In the absence of myosin heavy chain , the N - and C - terminal lobe of the ELCs are suggested to adopt a closed conformation . 356 An alternative view suggests that the free ELCs exist in unfolded state ; this would explain why no structural data of the free form is available . 357 3 . 2 . 2c Functional Role of ELCs MLCs allosterically interact with myosin heavy chain and are critical for maintaining functional and structural integrity of the myosin . These chains are regulated either by cation binding or phosphorylation . Removal of light chains from myosin in vitro results in the collapse 134 of the alpha - helical neck domain due to exposure of the hydrophobic IQ motif . In the absence of an appropriate number of light chains , myosin will not hydrolyze ATP and the power stroke is compromised . 358 , 359 Vanburen et al . ( 1994 ) demonstrated the significance of ELC interaction in the actomyosin cycle by selective removal of ELC from chicken skeletal myosin where a 50 % reduction in the force generation was observed . 358 ELC mutations resulting in E10K and E13R charge reversal changes inhibit myosin actin activated myosin ATPase activity suggesting a prominent role in the mechano - enzymatic activity of smooth muscle myosin . 360 To conclude , ELCs play a critical role in the motor functions of myosin . 3 . 2 . 2d Role of ELC N - terminus The role of the ELCs N - termini in the regulation of muscle contraction has been investigated . Intact and skinned human cardiac muscle fibers reconstituted with N - terminal ELC synthetic peptides of varying lengths showed increased generation of isometric tension . 361 Proteolytic deletion of the first 13 amino acids from the N - terminus in rabbit skeletal and / or cardiac muscle ELC eliminated the Ca 2 + - induced reversible mobility of myosin head S1 away from the myosin filament backbone , a movement which is observed in normal myosin assemblies under physiological conditions . Such structural transitions are essential for the function of myosin filaments . 362 Cardiac ventricular ELC missing amino acids 5 - 14 showed decreased isometric tension with no change in Ca 2 + sensitivity in skinned ventricular strips . 363 Haase et al . ( 2006 ) showed that expression of a 15 N - terminal amino acid peptide of cardiac ELCs in transgenic mice was consistent with improved intrinsic contractility of isolated perfused hearts . 364 The kinetic parameters of actin - activated ATPase activity ( turnover ( k cat ) and dissociation constant ( K d ) for S1 with ELC lacking 13 amino acids from its N - terminus were larger than S1 containing ELC with an intact N - terminus . 365 135 3 . 2 . 2e Interaction of the ELC N - terminus with Actin A number of results indicate that the N - terminus of the ELCs expressed in striated muscles make contact with the negatively - charged C - terminus of actin . 341 , 366 – 369 Milligan et al . ( 1990 ) first presented evidence of interactions of the N - terminus of myosin ELC on F - actin using three dimensional maps of muscle thin filaments . 264 ELCs expressed in striated muscles are rich in lysines in the first 10 N - terminal amino acids and the remaining region has proline - alanine repeats . 75 , 370 , 371 The C - terminus of ELCs interact with myosin heavy chain and possibly the RLC . 114 , 354 The first experimental evidence of large structural changes in the N - terminal extension of ELC in the presence of actin was provided by 1 H - NMR . 372 Later , crosslinking experiments indicated interactions of the N - terminal positively - charged lysine residues of ELC from chicken skeletal muscle with the C - terminal acidic residues 360 - 363 of actin . 75 Further experiments using affinity chromatography and 1 H - NMR also suggested binding of the N - terminal region of ELC to actin . 368 The structural information on the first 46 amino acids of the N - terminus of ELC is missing from the chicken skeletal muscle myosin S1 crystal structure due to degradation of this region by papain . 114 Adylt et al . ( 2007 ) modeled this missing region onto a model of actin - myosinS1 complex . They proposed that the N - terminus is a rod - like structure rather than a helix that extends from myosin to its actin binding site on the filament . 373 It has been suggested that the proline - alanine repeats found in the N - terminal region forms an extended semi - rigid extension that allows interaction between lysine residues of the ELC and the C - terminal residues of actin . 373 , 374 Interestingly , another study has shown the proline - alanine repeats in the vicinity of the SH3 domain of myosin heavy chains suggesting a role of the N - terminus of ELC in modulating myosin ATPase activity . SH3 domain of myosin heavy chain is involved in ATPase activity of 136 myosin . 375 However , this experimental observation was conducted on actin filaments fully occupied with S1 where there is no interaction of actin with the ELC extension , a condition far from physiological . 366 Pliszka et al . ( 2001 ) further confirmed binding of the N - terminal region of ELC with a C - terminal fragment of S1 containing acidic amino acids . 376 It has been proposed that when myosin binds to actin with either no nucleotide or ADP bound , the N - terminal ELC extension interacts with the actin filament . This binding generates additional actin binding surface on the myosin head . Upon binding of ATP to myosin , myosin and the ELC retract from the actin filament and the N - terminal ELC region binds to the motor head domain . 357 Molecular modeling and experimental evidence strongly suggest that the ELC not only stabilizes the lever arm but also modulates the actomyosin system . However , structural details are not available for ELCs not bound to myosin or the N - terminal region that binds with actin during the actomyosin cycle . 357 Previous research indicates an important role of myosin ELC in modulating the interaction between actin and myosin during actomyosin force generation . Further research into the structural aspects of the interaction of ELC with regions of RLC , myosin and actin can provide new insights into the mechanism of muscle contraction . Since the lowest Q - score hit from my ADPr - trimer MS data analysis was MLC6B , the binding of MLC6B with ADPr - trimer was validated through a series of experiments , described in this chapter . 3 . 3 Methods 3 . 3 . 1 Affinity Resin Preparation Affigel - 10 resin ( Bio - Rad Laboratories ( Canada ) Ltd . , cat # 1536046 ) equilibrated with G - Hepes buffer ( 5 mM HEPES , pH 7 . 5 , 2 mM CaCl 2 , 2 mM ATP ) was incubated with either G - actin 137 or ADPr - trimer in buffer without reducing agent for 60 min at 4℃ with continuous mixing . The reaction was terminated by washing G - affigel and 3mr - affigel with the blocking buffer ( 25 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 2 mM CaCl 2 , 2 mM ATP ) . The resulting resin was stored at 4℃ in G - buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 0 . 2 mM CaCl 2 , 0 . 2 mM ATP , 0 . 5 mM β - ME , 0 . 002 % NaN 3 ) and used within a day of preparation . The binding capacity of affigel - 10 was determined to be 1 mg of G - actin or ADPr - trimer per mg of resin . The coupled resins were washed with buffer A ( 10 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1mM ATP , 0 . 2 mM PMSF , 2 mM β - ME ) containing 200 mM NaCl to determine loss of either G - actin or ADPr - trimer from the resins . Gelsolin segment 4 - 6 ( G4 - 6 ) was bound to G - affigel and eluted to verify the functionality of the protein coupled to affigel - 10 . 3 . 3 . 2 Affinity Chromatography Preparation of Cell Lysate Zebrafish embryos were obtained from the Zebrafish facility in the Hagen Aqua lab , University of Guelph . About 120 , 5 dpf zebrafish embryos were lysed using glass beads in 1 . 5 mL of lysis buffer ( 10 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM ATP , 0 . 05 % NP40 , 2 mM β - ME , Sigma protease inhibitor cocktail ( cat # P8340 ) ) . The lysate was clarified by spinning at 13000 × g for 10 min at 4℃ . The protein concentration in the lysate was determined with the Thermo Scientific , Pierce BCA Protein Assay Kit ( cat # 23225 ) . Affinity Chromatography G - affigel and 3mr - affigel were equilibrated with buffer A ( 10 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM ATP , 0 . 2 mM PMSF , 2 mM β - ME ) . The clarified lysate containing 3 . 4 mgs of total protein was applied to 100 μL of G - affigel resin to remove G - actin binding proteins . The flow - 138 through from G - affigel was applied to 50 or 100 μL of 3mr - affigel . Following binding , each of the resins were washed with buffer A , buffer B ( 10 mM Tris , pH 7 . 5 , 50 mM KCl , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM ATP , 0 . 2 mM PMSF , 2 mM β - ME ) and again with buffer A to remove any salt . The resulting resins were stored at - 80℃ in buffer A . 3 . 3 . 3 Identification of ABPs by Mass Spectrometry Frozen G - and 3mr - affigel ( 50 and 100 μL ) samples were analyzed at the SPARC BioCentre at SickKids as a fee - for - use service . The proteins on the resin were digested by trypsin and the resulting peptides were analyzed on the Q Exactive HF - X hybrid quadrupole - Orbitrap mass spectrometer . The data analysis was executed on Proteome Discoverer software compatible with Sequest HT search engine configured to search the UniProt database . Identified proteins had at least one unique peptide identified , and protein abundance values were obtained by chromatographic peak intensity measurements . A total of 215 - 230 proteins were identified for G - affigel replicates and 260 - 280 proteins were identified for 3mr - affigel replicates . An initial list of eight proteins binding to 3mr - affigel was generated using the presence / absence approach ( Supplemental table 1 ) . Based on this approach , the proteins that bound to G - affigel were eliminated and the proteins that appeared in all three 50 μL and 100 μL 3mr - affigel samples were shortlisted . Each hit was then ranked based on their Q - value and those proteins with only one peptide detected were removed . Finally , an in silico search of potential interactors was done to define biological processes , and molecular functions of the hits . 3 . 3 . 4 MLC6B Purification MLC6B was overexpressed in E . coli BL21 cells that were transformed with a kanamycin resistant pET - 28b vector containing the mlc6b gene with an N - terminal His 6 tag synthesized by Bio Basic Canada Inc . ( Markham , ON ) . Starter culture was initiated by inoculating 50 mL of 139 Lysogeny Broth ( LB ) containing 50 μg / mL kanamycin with a single colony of transformed BL21 cells grown on LB plates . Expression culture was started by adding 50 mL starter culture into 500 mL of LB . Cells were grown at 37℃ until the cell density ( A 600 ) reached a value of approximately 0 . 6 before induction with 1 mM isopropyl - 1 - thio - β - D - galactopyranoside ( IPTG ) . Cells were harvested 3 hours post - induction by centrifugation at 5 , 000 x g for 10 min . Cell pellets were resuspended in 40 mL of binding buffer per litre of culture ( 10 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 50 mM KCl , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM PMSF , 10 mM imidazole , β - ME 0 . 1 % v / v protease inhibitors ( benzamidine , TLCK , TPCK , leupeptin ) . The resuspended cells were lysed using a French press at 16 , 000 psi . The lysate was centrifuged at 31 , 360 × g for 30 min . The clarified lysate was loaded onto a nickel - charged chelating Sepharose column washed with binding buffer and eluted with 0 - 100 mM imidazole , pH 7 . 5 . Elution fractions were run on SDS - PAGE gel and the fractions containing MLC6B were pooled . The resulting protein was dialyzed against storage buffer ( 50 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 5 mM CaCl 2 , 1 mM DTT ) overnight at 4℃ . Then , 10 % glycerol and protease inhibitors ( 0 . 05 % v / v benzamidine , TLCK , TPCK , leupeptin ) were added and the protein was flash frozen and stored at - 80℃ . 3 . 3 . 5 Removal of 6xHistidine tag His 6 - tagged MLC6B was dialyzed into thrombin cleavage buffer ( 0 . 2 mM Tris , pH 8 . 0 , 150 mM NaCl , 25 mM CaCl 2 ) overnight . 0 . 004 units of thrombin ( GE Healthcare , Picasaway NJ ) was added per μg of protein and incubated overnight at 4℃ . The reaction was quenched with 2 mM PMSF . Cleaved His 6 - tag or any remaining His 6 - MLC6B was removed by incubating the reaction with Ni - NTA resin equilibrated in thrombin cleavage buffer . The flow through from the resin contained untagged MLC6B . His 6 - MLC6B and untagged MLC6B were run on SDS - PAGE . 140 3 . 3 . 6 Co - sedimentation Assay Co - sedimentation assays were performed for both His 6 - tagged and untagged MLC6B . Polymerized actin ( 5 μM ) was incubated with 2 μM MLC6B on ice for 30 min . F - actin alone and MLC6B alone were run as controls . The reactions were centrifuged at 95 , 000 rpm ( 392 , 499 x g ) for 15 min ( Beckman TLA - 100 rotor ) . The resulting pellet and supernatant were run on SDS - PAGE . 3 . 3 . 7 Preparation of HMM and Light Chain Exchange HMM ( Heavy meromyosin ) was prepared from full - length myosin extracted from rabbit soleus muscle . 116 Essential light chain exchange on HMM was performed following the protocol described by Weeds and Wagner ( 1977 ) . 377 HMM ex was prepared by incubating HMM and His 6 - MLC6B in a 1 : 5 molar ratio in exchange buffer ( 100 mM imidazole . HCl , pH 7 . 0 , 2 mM EDTA and 2 mM DTT ) , and ammonium chloride was added to a final concentration of 4 . 7 M . The reaction was performed on ice with continuous mixing for 12 min and dialysed overnight against 3 mM imidazole . HCl , pH 7 . 0 , 6 mM KCl , 1 mM DTT to remove the ammonium chloride . HMM mock was prepared by incubating HMM with exchange buffer followed by dialysis . The proteins were flash frozen and stored at - 80℃ . HMM ex was further purified to remove any unbound light chains for Western blotting using the ‘deadheading’ method ( see Section 3 . 3 . 9 ) with slight modifications . HMM ex was sedimented with F - actin in the absence of ATP . The pellet was washed twice with 1x polymerization buffer and finally the HMM ex was released by adding ATP followed by centrifugation at 95 , 000 rpm ( 392 , 499 x g ) for 15 min ( Beckman TLA - 100 rotor ) . 3 . 3 . 8 Western Blot Proteins were separated by SDS - PAGE and transferred onto PVDF ( polyvinylidene difluoride ) membrane for 60 min at 100 V in transfer buffer ( 25 mM Tris , 190 mM glycine and 141 20 % v / v methanol ) . Following the transfer , PVDF membrane was washed with TBST ( 20 mM Tris , pH 7 . 6 , 150 mM NaCl , 0 . 1 % Tween 20 ) and incubated in 5 % milk protein in TBST for 60 min to block non - specific binding . Blocked membranes were rinsed with TBST and incubated with anti - His antibody ( Clontech Laboratories Inc , A Takara Bio Company , cat # 631212 ) at 4℃ overnight on a rocking table . The next day the membrane was washed three times for 5 min each with TBST and incubated with secondary antibody ( goat anti - mouse antibody ) conjugated with horse - radish peroxidase ( Promega , cat # W4028 ) for 60 min at RT . The resulting membrane was washed with TBST . Proteins were visualized with enhanced chemiluminescence ( ECL ) reagent ( Thermo Scientific Super Signal TM West Femto , cat # 34096 ) . 3 . 3 . 9 In Vitro Motility ( IVM ) Assay The IVM assay was performed as per Liang et al . ( 2003 ) and Viswanathan et al . ( 2017 ) , with some modifications . 378 , 379 Briefly , flow cells were created by adhering nitrocellulose - coated glass coverslips to microscope slides with double - sided tape . Any inactive myosin heads were removed by deadheading . HMM , HMM mock and HMM ex samples were incubated with F - actin in the absence of ATP , followed by centrifugation . The active myosin heads were released by the addition of ATP . Active HMM samples were bound to the nitrocellulose flow cell , followed by the addition of diluted rhodamine - phalloidin - labeled F - actin . Videos were captured for 15 s each at 2 mM and 0 . 1 M ATP concentration on a digital video camera mounted on a Quorum Deconvolution microscope ( Quorum Technologies Ltd . , Lewes , U . K . ) using a Texas red filter . Three videos were collected per assay for 2 mM ATP concentration . Analysis was performed to quantitate the velocity of motile filaments at 2 mM ATP concentrations for HMM , HMM mock and HMM ex . Videos were imported and analyzed in ImageJ . Up to ten filaments were selected based on directed movement ; if fewer than ten filaments were motile in a given video , only those that 142 showed movement were chosen . The distance covered by a single filament over a period of 10 frames was measured from the start and end point of a filament using the line tool . This data was recorded using the “Measure” command in ImageJ and saved as . xls files before being imported into a custom Microsoft Excel spreadsheet . Data collection was done by Grace Teng and IVM videos were analysed by Michael Jones , both graduate students in the Dawson Lab . Velocity data was obtained using following Equation : 𝑉 ( 𝜇𝑚 𝑠 ) = ( 𝐷 𝐹 𝐸−𝐹 𝑆 ) 𝑋 89 . 46 𝑛𝑚𝑝𝑖𝑥𝑒𝑙 𝑋 2 . 48 𝑓𝑟𝑎𝑚𝑒𝑠𝑠 1000 𝑛𝑚𝜇𝑚 where D is the distance traveled in pixels , F E is the end frame number and F S is the start frame number . 3 . 3 . 10 Pull - down Assay 3mr - and BSA - affigel were prepared as described in Section 3 . 3 . 1 . A 100 μg of 3mr or BSA was bound to 150 μL of resin . 3mr - or BSA - affigel were incubated with 200 μg of His 6 - MLC6B or HMM ex for 60 min at 4℃ with continuous shaking . The bound resins were washed with buffer A , buffer B and buffer C ( buffer B + 0 . 05 % NP40 ) . Loading buffer was added to the washed resins and run on SDS - PAGE gel for Western blotting as described in section 3 . 3 . 8 . 3 . 4 Results The stability of coupling of G - actin and ADPr - trimer to affigel - 10 was confirmed by washing the coupled resins with lysis buffer , buffer A and buffer B . SDS - PAGE of the washes confirmed no loss of ADPr - trimer or G - actin from either G - or 3mr - affigel , respectively ( Figure 3 . 4A ) . Based on the presence / absence approach and ranking the proteins by their Q values , we identified eight protein hits binding to 3mr - affigel in six samples ( 3 x 50 μL + 3 x 100 μL 3mr - affigel ) . Four of these identified hits with more than one unique peptide were identified and selected for validation ( Table 3 . 1 ) . Since MLC6B ranked highest on the list and the literature suggests interactions between actin and MLCs , His 6 - tagged MLC6B was purified in the lab for validation of the interaction observed by MS ( Figure 3 . 5 ) . I hypothesized that MLC6B will bind F - actin since MLC6B was identified as interacting with ADPr - trimer by MS . However , no interaction between these proteins was observed in the co - sedimentation assay ( Figure 3 . 6 ) . Since the N - terminus of essential myosin light chains like MLC6B interact with actin , the N - terminal His 6 - tag might interfere with the binding of MLC6B to F - actin . However , untagged MLC6B with the His 6 - tag cleaved using thrombin ( Figure 3 . 7A ) did not bind to F - actin in the co - sedimentation assay ( Figure 3 . 7B ) . 75 , 370 , 371 To explain the lack of binding of MLC6B to F - actin , I tested the idea that MLC6B might exist in an inactive or unfolded state when not bound the IQ motif in the myosin heavy chain lever arm . 356 , 357 Native ELCs on HMM were exchanged with His 6 - MLC6B ( HMM ex ) followed by co - sedimentation with F - actin . A signal for HMM ex with an anti - His antibody in the Western blot confirmed replacement of native ELCs on HMM with His 6 - MLC6B ( Figure 3 . 8A ) . Since ELCs play a role in the force and motion generation during actin - myosin interaction , the exchange was further confirmed by an IVM assay where a decrease in actin filament velocity was observed 145 Table 3 . 1 Prioritized list of ADPr - trimer binding candidates .
