HMM with native light chains bound was run as a positive control . The velocity of HMM mock and HMM ex was 38 % and 10 % that of native HMM , respectively ( Figure 3 . 8B ) . Although MLC6B did not appear to interact with F - actin , the appearance of a signal in the Western blot from pull - down assays of 3mr - affgel incubated with HMM ex or MLC6B alone suggested interactions of ADPr - trimer with both HMM ex and His 6 - MLC6B . Almost no HMM ex bound to the negative control BSA - affigel ( Figure 3 . 9 ) . 3 . 5 Discussion and Conclusion MS data was analysed using the presence / absence approach which eliminated further investigation of non - specific or background interactors or the need for more replicates for statistical analysis . MLC6B was identified as the top hit in the list of potential ADPr - trimer interactors . MLC6B is an ELC found in the smooth muscles of zebrafish . An earlier structure of myosin found ELCs bound to the heavy chain of myosin . 114 Later , crosslinking and fluorescent probe experiments indicated that the N - terminus of ELCs interacts with actin . 342 , 366 , 380 The interaction was confirmed by an EM structure in which additional electron density was seen close to the C - terminus of actin . 264 However , the N - terminus of the ELC was not resolved in the crystal structures of myosin S1 , likely due to high mobility in the absence of F - actin . 381 Since ADPr - trimer possesses F - actin like properties , I thought that recombinant MLC6B should bind F - actin . However , co - sedimentation assays suggested no interaction between F - actin and MLC6B . Considering that the N - terminal amino acids of ELCs are known to interact with C - terminal residues of actin , the N - terminal His 6 - tag on recombinant MLC6B could be interfering with the interaction . Hence , the N - terminal His 6 - tag on MLC6B was cleaved using thrombin , but again no 152 interaction between untagged MLC6B and F - actin was observed . Some researchers have proposed that in the unbound form , the N - and C - terminus of ELCs exists in a closed conformation , while others suggested that when not bound to the heavy chain , ELCs exists in an unfolded state which has hindered complete structural determination of the free form of light chains . 356 , 357 No crosslinking was observed between isolated A1 ( an ELC found in skeletal muscle ) and F - actin , in contrast to when A1 was bound to S1 when crosslinking occurred . 382 Since the MLC6B in the cell lysate used for MS was likely bound to myosin , native ELCs on HMM were exchanged with His 6 - tagged recombinant MLC6B . The exchange was confirmed by Western blot and changes in velocity in IVM assays . The Western blot showed a signal for HMM ex with anti - His antibody . Interestingly , a significant decrease in the sliding velocity of the actin filaments was observed for HMM ex compared to HMM and HMM mock . Actin filaments exhibited little to no movement over HMM ex at a concentration of 2 mM ATP ; however , in the presence of 0 . 1 M ATP , the filaments detached from the HMM ex heads ( Supplemental figure 7 ) . Such an observation is indicative of altered actomyosin interaction kinetic parameters ( k cat and K M ) being influenced by the light chains present on the heavy chains resulting in impaired interactions and slower movement of actin filaments . The altered kinetic parameters could be the result of either an influence on the release of myosin ATP hydrolysis products or slower association between actin and myosin - ADP + Pi ( see Section 1 . 3 . 1b in chapter 1 for steps of the actomyosin cycle ) . 377 Light chains of myosin are required for generation of movement . Trybus and Chatman ( 1993 ) showed that the velocity of actin was similar over skeletal heavy chain with skeletal LCs or chimeras of skeletal and smooth LCs . However , the results contradicted the findings where smooth muscle heavy chain with added skeletal RLC completely inhibited both ATPase activity 153 and actin motility . 383 Removal of light chains from HMM reduced the velocity of actin filaments significantly ( almost 10x ) from 8 . 8 μms - 1 to 0 . 8 μms - 1 without significantly impacting the ATPase activity ; however , reconstitution of myosin with the complete set of light chains restored the sliding velocity to normal . 359 Thus , LCs are critical for conversion of chemical energy to motion in actomyosin force generation . It has been observed that skeletal myosin carrying A1 type ELC ( S1 ( A1 ) ) containing an N - terminal region that interacts with actin moves actin filaments slower than myosin carrying A2 type ELC ( S1 ( A2 ) ) missing the actin - binding N - terminus . This slower gliding velocity could be due to the A1 isoform binding to actin . 359 A difference in ATPase kinetic parameters of myosin was reported depending on the form of the two ELC isoenzymes present . Myosin S1 containing light chain A1 had a lower K M for actin and slower turnover of MgATP ( k cat ) than S1 ( A2 ) . 342 Wagner and Weeds ( 1977 ) also reported in their hybridization experiments that the k cat for S1 ( A2 ) was twice that of S1 ( A1 ) and the ratio for K M was 4 : 1 . 377 Pull - down assays with 3mr - affigel indicated binding of both HMM ex and His 6 - MLC6B to ADPr - trimer confirming MS results . Timson et al . ( 1998 ) demonstrated that both free and S1 - bound ELC crosslinked to actin . 342 In contrast to a previous study , the crosslinking was attributed to the protocol in which molecules were allowed to come to equilibrium before adding the crosslinker . 382 The heavy chain of S1 is known to direct the binding of ELC on actin , but it is likely that in a less structured free state in solution , the N - terminal actin binding site of ELC was exposed to solvent allowing crosslinking . 342 , 384 Interestingly , MLC6B in both the HMM - bound and free states interacted with ADPr - trimer , although no such interaction was observed with F - actin in co - sedimentation assays . The N - terminal basic amino acids of ELCs interact with acidic amino acids in the C - terminus of the 154 actin . 75 The same highly flexible C - terminus of actin participates in intersubunit interactions within the filament and might require binding of myosin heavy chain to orient the C - terminus of actin to bind ELC . 61 , 62 However , in the case of ADPr - trimer , the penultimate C - terminal Cys - 374 is involved in and stabilized by pPBM crosslinking and may adopt a fixed conformation that allows interaction with MLC6B even though ADPr - trimer itself does not bind myosin as described in Section 2 . 2 of chapter 2 . Alternatively , the ribosyl groups at the Arg - 177 of each actin subunit at the intersubunit interaction site might place the actin subunit in the trimer in an orientation that favours MLC6B binding . Further investigation using PBM - crosslinked actin filaments is required to evaluate these possibilities . The binding functionality of G - actin coupled to affigel - 10 was confirmed by binding and elution of G4 - 6 from G - affigel . However , my results present interaction of MLC6B with ADPr - trimer only when coupled to affigel - 10 , therefore the possibility of altered conformation of ADPr - trimer resulting from overcoupling of the primary amines with the resin cannot be ruled out . This issue can be resolved by performing reverse pull - down of ADPr - trimer on MLC6B coupled resin . 3 . 6 Future Directions Altered kinetic properties of HMM upon replacement of light chains can be studied with myosin ATPase assays . Together with IVM data , the ATPase assay data will provide information on ELCs in the regulation of the mechanochemical actomyosin interaction . The hypothesis that stabilization of the C - terminus by crosslinking facilitates the binding of MLC6B on ADPr - trimer can be validated by using PBM - crosslinked F - actin in co - sedimentation assays . Upon confirmation of the interaction , the structure of MLC6B bound to F - dimer ( actin filaments formed by polymerization of PBM - crosslinked actin dimers ) can be determined using cryo - EM . Based on the hypothesis that MLC6B binds to the crosslinked C - terminus end of actin , MLC6B would bind 155 along one side of the F - dimer filament . Alternatively , based on the results of pull - down assays , a heterocomplex of MLC6B bound to ADPr - trimer can be purified for single particle cryo - EM structural determination . MLC6B could be in either its free form or bound to a recombinantly - expressed myosin IQ motif . If required , the resulting complex can be stabilized by crosslinkers for purification . Finally , future work also involves validating and characterizing interactions of other F - ABPs identified by MS ( Table 1 ) . While no literature regarding direct interaction with actin was found for α - 1 , 4 glucan phosphorylase , the literature suggests a role for tyrosine 3 - monooxygenase activation protein and RAB2A in the regulation of the actin cytoskeleton . Tyrosine 3 - monooxygenase / tryptophan 5 - monooxygenase activation protein / beta polypeptide - like protein is a member of the 14 - 3 - 3 family . Members of this family are known to play a role in cellular trafficking and actin dynamics through interactions with LIM kinase , cofilin and other actin binding proteins . 385 – 387 One of the known mechanisms by which 14 - 3 - 3 proteins regulate actin dynamics is through sequestration of phosphorylated cofilin . 386 , 387 However , multiple isoforms of 14 - 3 - 3 proteins exist in eukaryotes leading to inconsistent results as to whether 14 - 3 - 3 proteins interact directly with actin . In Giardia lambila , a protozoan parasite that lacks cofilin and other canonical ABPs , 14 - 3 - 3 protein was found associated with actin . 388 The 14 - 3 - 3 protein sigma isoform forms a complex with actin in breast cancer cells and regulates cell motility during invasion . 388 Another hit identified by MS , RAB2A is a member of the Ras - related family of low - molecular weight GTP - binding proteins . RAB proteins regulate vesicular transport pathways including formation of vesicles , actin and tubulin - dependent vesicle movement and specific targeting to and fusion with the membranes . 389 – 391 No evidence of direct binding between RAB2A 156 and F - actin was found in the literature , since it is yet to be established how RABs and their binding partners regulate the cytoskeleton near membranes . It has been suggested that myosin initiates nucleation of its actin track around vesicles and that RAB binding controls an enzyme promoting actin assembly . 392 , 393 Discussing the details of the pathways and multiprotein complexes involved in the interaction of Tyrosine 3 - monooxygenase / tryptophan 5 - monooxygenase activation protein and RAB2A is beyond the scope of this work . However , further investigation of the potential of direct or indirect interactions of these proteins through the formation of multiprotein complexes can reveal insights of actin dynamics regulation and open new perspectives for structural investigation . The above listed proteins can be recombinantly expressed and purified in the lab with gene synthesis from industrial sources . Alternatively , purified recombinant homologs of these proteins from other species can be purchased . MyBioSource Inc . ( San Diego , USA ) provides human - tyrosine hydroxylase activation / 14 - 3 - 3 beta recombinant protein ( cat # MBS536781 ; 82 . 6 % sequence identity with zebrafish homologs ) and Alpha - 1 , 4 glucan phosphorylase ( cat # MBS1057192 ; 45 . 5 % sequence identity with zebrafish homolog ) . Human - RAB2A with 88 . 15 % sequence identity with zebrafish homolog is available from LifeSpan Biosciences ( cat # LS - G1318 , Seattle , WA ) . 157 4 FINAL DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSION The following section focuses on the general goal of my research to identify F - actin binding proteins that bind ADPr - trimer to produce heterocomplexes for structural determination . Why short F - actin oligomers ? Filamentous systems such as actin form the cytoskeleton and play an essential role in the cell division and muscular contraction . They interact with a large number of proteins to maintain homeostasis of the cell , and are thus associated with many diseases , particularly myopathies , cancer and neurodegeneration . 394 – 396 Understanding how actin assembles , disassembles , interacts with itself and a large number of ABPs depends on understanding the structure of actin filaments . The challenge researchers face is the fundamental property of actin to self - associate that hinders crystallization studies . The crystal structure of monomeric actin was determined and information on how monomers fit together into the polymer was known at a low resolution of 8 . 4 Å until 1990 . 52 , 96 , 397 Since crystallization is the mainstay technique for atomic resolution determination of proteins , one approach adopted by researchers was to crystallize small oligomers of actin to reveal interactions at binding interfaces . 72 , 398 , 399 These defined oligomers were obtained by limited crosslinking in either lateral or longitudinal directions and inhibiting polymerization by chemical modifications . 69 , 71 , 400 , 401 However , these modifications can impact the interactions among actin subunits within the oligomer and with their binding partners , resulting in a complex with altered biological significance . Some of the crystal structures of short F - actin oligomers provided an idea of interactions between subunits , while in others , the subunits did not adopt a conformation representing F - actin or were incompatible with the known F - actin structures . 72 , 73 , 103 For example , interactions of ANP - crosslinked actin dimer with myosin remained relatively unchanged , but 158 DNase I and G1 binding to the dimers to inhibit polymerization resulted in loss of productive interactions with myosin . 400 , 402 , 403 Similarly , crystal structures of oligomers with polymerization inhibition by TMR , latrunculin A or G1 did not present a conformation representing F - actin and were incompatible with known F - actin structures . 72 , 73 , 103 A strategic balance of chemical modifications with a minimalistic approach was required to generate oligomers that function as an F - actin - like scaffold . Over 10 years of research and biochemical investigations in the Dawson lab culminated in the production of ADPr - trimer as an F - actin scaffold . Actin subunits in the ADPr - trimer were held together by introducing crosslinks in the adjacent actin subunits in the filament followed by depolymerization . An ADPr - ribose moiety was bound at Arg - 177 of each actin subunit at intersubunit interaction sites , suggesting conformational flexibility in the ADPr - trimer . Although the presence of crosslinking might introduce constraints overcoming perturbations caused by the ribose moiety , potential disruptions of intermolecular contacts by stoichiometric ADP - ribosylation cannot be ignored . The binding of DNase I or gelsolin to ADPr - trimer indicated an intact pointed end and barbed end , respectively . In my thesis , I extended this research by investigating the interaction of the ADPr - trimer with side binder proteins , myosin S1 and cofilin . Since there are over 100 known ABPs , the search for ADPr - trimer interacting proteins was expanded using ADPr - trimer affinity resin to pull - down binding partners from a cell lysate followed by identification by mass spectrometry . Gelsolin and cofilin bind , S1 does not bind ADPr - trimer The results of my research indicated that myosin S1 does not bind ADPr - trimer , while cofilin and gelsolin bind to the ADPr - trimer . Such findings suggest that cofilin and S1 have different mechanisms of binding to the side of actin filaments and induce distinct conformational changes . ABPs can induce specific conformational changes that propagates along the filament . 279 159 Ngo et al . ( 2016 ) showed that both cofilin and myosin bind co - operatively to F - actin , but in a mutually exclusive manner . It has been suggested that conformational changes in the actin filaments contribute to the mutually exclusive cooperative binding of myosin II and cofilin . 278 This spatial and temporal regulation of ABPs binding to F - actin is yet to be understood . According to one view , in addition to biochemical signalling , mechanical stimuli can regulate ABP binding . 404 , 405 For example , stretched filaments do not bind cofilin in vivo and in vitro , whereas an increased affinity for such filaments is observed for myosin II in vivo . 405 , 406 Another view suggests that ABPs introduce local structural changes in F - actin , leading to differentiation of mutually exclusive ABP binding sites along a single filament . Cofilin and myosin II introduce opposite changes in the helical twist of the filament . 405 , 407 , 408 While cofilin supertwists the helix , 157 , 409 , 410 myosin slightly untwists the filament in the absence of ATP . 411 , 412 Perhaps these different twist changes explain the mutually exclusive nature of myosin and cofilin binding to F - actin . The different twists induced by myosin and cofilin also suggest why cofilin binds ADPr - trimer while myosin does not . I suggest that the presence of the ADPr - modification inhibits the untwisting required for myosin binding while accommodating the supertwist seen with cofilin . To test this model , one could compare the structure of ADPr - trimer alone and to the structure of F - actin with myosin bound , focussing on the position of the ADPr - modification and its likelihood of inhibiting conformational shifts needed for myosin binding . In addition , studying the ADPr - trimer : cofilin filamentous assemblies can likely reveal a different mode of binding and filament stabilization by cofilin . Like cofilin , gelsolin bound to ADPr - trimer . Interestingly , Van Troy et al . ( 1997 ) used small peptide fragments of cofilin and the G2 segment of gelsolin to show that both cofilin and G2 160 segment share common binding sites . 413 Since both full - length cofilin and gelsolin bound to the same short F - actin structure , results described in this thesis support Van Troy’s findings . The selective binding of ABPs to ADPr - trimer indicate disruption of particular intersubunit interactions required for some ABP binding . ADP - ribosylated monomeric actin interacts with ABPs , such as DNAse I , vitamin D binding protein , thymosin B4 , cofilin , gelsolin segment 1 and myosin S1 , but when present in a trimer , the ADPr - modification distorts the binding sites for myosin S1 and potentially other F - actin binding proteins . 275 However , the hetADPr - trimer produced by a combination of crosslinking and polymerization inhibition by G1 and ribosylation did bind myosin S1 . 104 It is yet to be established if hetADPr - trimer is the smallest F - actin unit that can support myosin force generation . This can be determined by monitoring motility of fluorescently labelled myosin over het - trimer - coated surfaces . 280 – 282 Thus , modifying filamentous systems to produce oligomers that bind ABPs can alter binding interfaces for some ABPs , though some binding properties of F - actin are retained . However , the physiological significance of such complexes needs to be determined . Despite the possibility of deformation of intersubunit interactions or the binding interface for F - ABPs due to chemical modifications , the hetADPr - trimer did show that a suitable combination of modifications can lead to an actin oligomer that binds to myosin . However , the heterogeneity of modifications makes the hetADPr - trimer : S1 complex unsuitable for crystallization . Similarly , the gelsolin bound ADPr - trimer was non - crystallizable . Nevertheless , a cryo - EM approach can be applied to such non - crystallizable bio - complexes for structural determination . 161 Does ADPr - trimer mimic any biological state of F - actin ? ADPr - trimer binds selectively to cofilin and gelsolin but not S1 , all of which are F - actin side - binding proteins . Potentially , ribosylation inhibits the relative movement of the subunits required for presenting binding interface for S1 , but allows super twisting that supports cofilin binding . Alternatively , since both gelsolin and cofilin bind to G - actin , these proteins could be binding to individual actin subunits within ADPr - trimer through their G - actin binding sites . 204 , 289 Additional bands seen on the native gel for gelsolin - ADPr - trimer reactions prior to purification suggests binding of more than one gelsolin to ADPr - trimer through their G - actin binding segments ( G1 or / and G4 - 6 ) ( Supplemental figure 5 ) . Negative stain EM data shows heterogeneity which could result from multiple modes of gelsolin binding to ADPr - trimer . G1 and G4 - 6 segments can bind to any two actin subunits within the ADPr - trimer while , G2 ( F - actin binding segment ) either binds to two longitudinally associated actin subunits or remains unbound adopting various conformations ( Supplemental figure 6 ) . In future , binding of recombinantly expressed G2 segment to the ADPr - trimer can be verified using physical assays , such as native gel . ADPr - trimer pull - down assays from zebra fish cell lysate presented MLC6B as a binding partner of ADPr - trimer , but not G - actin . The literature supports the role of interaction of N - terminus of ELCs with the C - terminus of actin during actomyosin force generation . 75 I suggest that binding of MLC6B to ADPr - trimer could be the result of the restrained C - terminus of actin subunits ; however , any alterations in the conformation of ADPr - trimer upon coupling to resin cannot be ignored . Since ELC extracted from rabbit skeletal muscle has been shown to bind to G - actin in a crosslinking experiment , binding of MLC6B to 3mr - affigel does not confirm F - actin like interaction with ADPr - trimer . 384 162 Considering that cofilin , gelsolin and MLC6B can bind to G - actin raises questions on the validity of ADPr - trimer as a biologically relevant mimic of F - actin . Since no structural data is available , a concrete conclusion on if any F - actin like interactions are retained in ADPr - trimer cannot be drawn . Hence , using ADPr - trimer as a short - F - actin scaffold for future structural studies with F - ABPs stays questionable and must be considered carefully . Application of cryo - EM to filamentous systems has revealed near atomic resolution structures , thus utility of modified short F - actin oligomers for structural studies needs to be reconsidered . 4 - 9 However , the hetADPr - trimer that binds to S1 can be used for biophysical assays . HetADPr - trimer could be used to establish if trimer is the smallest F - actin unit that can support movement or long range interactions between actin subunits is required for actomyosin motility . Cryo - EM : Application to short F - actin oligomers and filamentous form Since the application of cryo - EM with direct electron detectors to F - actin in 2015 , the year I began my research , cryo - EM has revolutionized F - actin structural studies . I therefore initiated a pipeline for cryo - EM work in the Dawson lab using resources available on campus . From the first F - actin reconstruction obtained at a resolution of 40 Å , which revealed the helical structure and two large domains , to the most recent structure at 3 . 1 Å resolution with visible side chains and nucleotides , the field of cryo - EM has seen significant advances and has been extended to actin filaments decorated with myosin and other ABPs yielding near atomic resolution structural information ( Supplemental Table 1 , 2 ) . 9 , 127 , 266 , 412 , 414 The resolution revolution in past 5 - 6 years has been attributed to the development of direct electron detectors , microscope automation and image processing tools . 163 With EM work extended to F - actin and F - actin bound ABPs , one might argue that we no longer need short F - actin oligomers . However , F - actin is dynamic and exists in multiple states . 55 , 277 Therefore , crosslinking might still be useful for isolating specific states of F - actin . For instance , crosslinked actin filaments exhibit a state that binds myosin , but inhibits myosin motility , and I have already shown that the ADPr - trimer does not bind S1 , but binds cofilin and gelsolin . 71 MLC6B bound ADPr - trimer but not F - actin in my co - sedimentation experiments and was identified as the top - most hit in my MS results . This result suggests that crosslinking held the ADPr - trimer in a conformation preferred for MLC6B binding . Thus , crosslinking can be used to isolate specific states of F - actin to study its interaction with binding partners . There is evidence that the conformation of the C - terminus of actin is involved in some ABP binding . 266 Since Cys - 374 , the penultimate amino acid of actin , participates in the PBM crosslink , I believe that modification of the C - terminus is involved with the affinity of MLC6B for ADPr - trimer . There is evidence that the N - termini of some MLCs interact with the C - terminus of actin , supporting my model . 368 , 373 , 415 In addition to MLC6B , Kim et al . ( 2002 ) showed that in vitro motility of crosslinked F - actin by myosin is reduced . I believe this reduced motility is due to the role of the actin C - terminus in myosin force generation . 71 I tested this hypothesis with filaments made exclusively from crosslinked dimers or trimers and have preliminary results suggesting that the reduction in gliding velocity of crosslinked filaments is proportional to the percentage of crosslinked - restricted C - termini ( Supplemental Figure 1 ) . Future experiments can follow up on these results with cryo - EM structural determination of myosin S1 - decorated actin filaments consisting exclusively of crosslinked - dimer ( called F - dimer ) . The C - termini of the subunits in one strand of F - dimer are constrained in the crosslink , while the C - termini on the other strand are free to move . If my hypothesis is correct , the lever arms of all myosin S1 on the constrained side of the 164 filament should be in the pre - powerstroke state ( therefore they do not produce force ) , while the myosin on the opposite strand will be in the post - powerstroke state after producing force . Modifying filamentous actin can pose challenges , but a balanced approach can be used to isolate specific states of F - actin and to study interactions with ABPs , including the mechanical regulation of binding . Further development in EM imaging and computational work are transforming the landscape of structural determination of filamentous systems . In the future , further advances in cryo - electron tomography can be applied to observe filamentous structures within cells . Although the cost is significant and current demand for the high resolution cryo - EM instrumentation is outstripping supply , it is anticipated that the rapid expansion in the field of cryo - EM will provide a significant understanding of cellular machines in the coming decade . My research aimed to characterize the interactions of myosin S1 , cofilin and gelsolin with ADPr - trimer structurally and biochemically . This approach was refined by including advances in proteomics and structural biology . An unbiased approach using the combination of pull - down assays and MS led to the identification of proteins from cell lysates that bind the ADPr - trimer . MLC6B was identified as the top hit and binding of MLC6B to ADPr - trimer was verified by pull - down assays performed with purified His 6 - MLC6B . The MS approach generated a list of other potential interactors of ADPr - trimer . In the future , the interaction of these binding partners with ADP - trimer can be characterized using physical and biochemical assays leading to structural studies . Setting the stage to determine the structure of the GSFL : 3mr complex with state - of - the - art high - resolution cryo - electron microscopy was accomplished by establishing a workflow at Guelph , not only for future structural determination of short F - actin complexes and F - actin but also for other non - crystallizable biomolecules . The identification of ABPs through proteomics and the workflow established for cryo - EM structural determination will advance our understanding of 165 the different ways F - ABPs interact with F - actin and the critical role of these interactions in regulating eukaryotic cell function and life . 166 5 BIBLIOGRAPHY 1 . B A 199 Supplemental Figure 2 ADPr - monomer binds to cofilin . A ) Analytical size - exclusion chromatogram of binding reactions containing ADPr : monomer and cofilin . A mixture of 10 μM ADPr - monomer and 10 μM cofilin in Super G - buffer or 10 μM of ADPr - monomer alone were incubated on ice for 60 min . The reactions were developed on a Superdex 200 ( 10 / 300 ) analytical gel filtration column equilibrated with Super G - buffer . A shift in the elution peak for the reaction with ADPr : monomer and cofilin confirmed formation of a complex . B ) 10 % Native - PAGE of purification of Cof : 1mr complex for crystal trials . 176 . 5 μM of ADPr - monomer was incubated with equimolar amount of cofilin overnight at 4℃ and developed on Superdex 200 ( 10 / 300 ) . The eluted fractions were run on a native gel . Fractions containing pure Cof : 1mr complex were pooled and concentrated for setting - up crystal trials . Protein bands in addition to the major GSFL : 3mr complex band suggests binding of more than one gelsolin molecules to ADPr - trimer through their monomer binding domains . 202 Supplemental Figure 5 Possible modes of binding of gelsolin segments G1 and G4 - 6 to trimer Gelsolin segments G1 and G4 - 6 can bind to actin subunits of a trimer through their actin monomer binding sites in multiple ways . Presumed models of gelsolin segments bound to actin trimer were generated in PyMOL ( PDB : 3G37 ( F - actin ) ; 1EQY ( G1 / actin monomer ) ; 1H1V ( G4 - 6 / actin monomer ) . G1 and G4 - 6 are shown in yellow and yellow orange , respectively . The trimer consists of two subunits from one strand of F - actin ( cyan ) and one subunit of the counterpart strand ( pink ) . The trimer does not present any alteration in inter - subunit interactions that could occur due to crosslinking or presence of a ribosyl group on each subunit . 203 Supplemental Figure 6 Preliminary data from cryo - grid preparation for GS : 3mr complex . C - flat grid ( CF400 - Cu - UL , Electron Microscopy Sciences , Hatfield , PA ) was glow discharged , 5 ul of sample at 12 . 5 μg / mL was applied to the grid and the grid was flash frozen using Cryoplunge3 ( Gatan Inc , Pleasanton , CA ) . A and B represent uniform ice thickness with some particles indicated with arrows . No particles were observed in C , potentially due to thicker layer of ice . D represents an area of the “bad” ice showing ethane contamination at the bottom and some crystalline ice ( blackspots and fuzzy areas ) . Cryo - grid preparation and imaging were done in collaboration with the Khursigara lab at Molecular and Cellular Imaging Facility , University of Guelph . The particle density on the grid was low and needs to be optimized for future imaging . Additionally , reproducible production of grids with uniform ice thickness will be pivotal for future work .
